# 黄帝九鼎神丹经诀

**The Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon: Instructions and Secrets**

**Title:** *The Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon: Instructions and Secrets*
**Author unknown.**
**Comprising twenty scrolls.**
**Scroll One** contains *The Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon*, the main text, dating from the late Han Dynasty.
**Scrolls Two through Nineteen** are commentaries and elucidations, likely compiled between the Wei-Jin and Sui-Tang periods.
**This work** expounds upon external Daoist elixir cultivation and methods of ingestion, drawing extensively from diverse sources, and serves as a crucial historical record for studying Han-Tang alchemical elixir practices.

**Source:** *Zhengtong Daozang* (Orthodox Daoist Canon of the Ming Dynasty), *Dongshen* (Cavernous Gods) section, *Zhongshu* (Miscellaneous Arts) category.

**Table of Contents:**
**Scroll One** – *The Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon*
**Scroll Two** – *Clarifying the Origin and Refining of Divine Elixir, and the Noble Methods of Obtaining It*
**Scroll Three** – *Clarifying the Selection of a Master and Receiving the Secrets Without Borrowing from the True Ones*
**Scroll Four** – *Clarifying the Warding Off of Malevolent Spirits and Demons, Preserving the Daoist Essence, and Protecting the Body*
**Scroll Five** – *Clarifying the Refinement of Divine Elixir: It Must Depend on the Daoist Virtue and the Illumination of the Way. The Three Sovereigns’ Daoist Texts and the True Forms of the Five Peaks. The Symbolic Methods for Invoking the Divine and Their Verification*
**Scroll Six** – *Clarifying the Functions and Benefits of Divine Elixir*
**Scroll Seven** – *Clarifying the Practice of Unity (守一), Avoiding Malevolence, and the Furnaces, Cauldrons, and Elixir Houses*
**Scroll Eight** – *Clarifying the Transformation of Stones into Water and the Methods of Refining Saltpeter (硝石)*
**Scroll Nine** – *Clarifying the Proper and Harmful Methods of Ingesting Gold and Silver*
**Scroll Ten** – *Clarifying the Prohibitions and Precautions in Refining Medicinal Herbs According to Yin-Yang Principles*
**Scroll Eleven** – *Clarifying the Longevity Methods of Mercury (水银) and the Arts of Refining and Detoxifying It*
**Scroll Twelve** – *Clarifying the Methods and Functions of Lead (铅) in the Nine Elixirs*
**Scroll Thirteen** – *Clarifying the Virtue and Power of Cinnabar (丹砂), Its Entry into the Path of Longevity, and the Labor Required*
**Scroll Fourteen** – *Clarifying the Methods of Refining Realgar (雄黄)*
**Scroll Fifteen** – *Clarifying the Essence and Spirit of Various Stones and Medicinal Herbs*
**Scroll Sixteen** – *Clarifying That the Refining of All Stones and Medicinal Herbs Contains the Methods of Longevity*
**Scroll Seventeen** – *Clarifying the Order of Medicinal Herbs, the Effects of Intoxication, and the Origin of the Hua Pool (华池)*
**Scroll Eighteen** – *Clarifying That Stalactite (钟乳) and Other Stones, as Well as Various Copper and Iron Ores, All Contain Methods of Longevity*
**Scroll Nineteen** – *Clarifying the Methods of Refining Copper and Iron Ores, Transmuting Poisonous Stones, and Their Proper Uses, as Well as the Methods of Warding Off and Harmonizing*
**Scroll Twenty** – *Clarifying the Taboos and Defeats in Combining Elixirs, and the Hidden Secrets of the Nine Cauldrons Elixir*

**Scroll One of *The Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon: Instructions and Secrets***

The Yellow Emperor received the supreme Dao of the Returning Elixir from **Xuannü** (玄女, the Mysterious Lady).
**Xuannü** is a celestial maiden.
The Yellow Emperor combined and ingested it, thereby ascending to immortality.

**Xuannü** instructed the Yellow Emperor:
*"Those who seek longevity but cannot obtain the Divine Elixir or Golden Liquid merely torment themselves in vain.
Though one may practice breathing techniques—expelling the old and drawing in the new—and ingest herbal medicines, it may extend one’s years but not escape death.
The Divine Elixir grants one the Dao of the Immortal Sage, harmonizing with the heavens and earth, sharing the luminosity of the sun and moon, gazing upon the ten thousand miles, commanding ghosts and spirits, elevating one’s entire family to the Void, flying without wings, riding clouds and dragons, ascending and descending the **Taqing** (太清, Supreme Purity), traversing the eight extremes between the **Loucang** (漏刻, moments marked by water clocks) and beyond, unconstrained by rivers, unfearing of a hundred poisons."*

The Yellow Emperor passed this on to **Xuanziji** (玄子, the Mysterious Son), solemnly declaring:
*"This Dao is most weighty; it must be entrusted only to the worthy.
Even if one possesses mountains of gold or dominion over ten thousand miles, do not reveal this Dao unless the recipient is truly the one.
One who has attained even a single **Cauldron** (鼎) is sufficient for immortality; why need nine?"*

The method of transmission was as follows:
*"A golden figure weighing nine *liang* (两), and a golden fish weighing three *liang*, must be cast into flowing eastern waters as an oath. Both the figure and the fish shall emerge from the one receiving the Dao."*

Before the ritual, one must fast and bathe, setting up a seat for **Xuannü** upon the water in a secluded, uninhabited place.
Burning incense and offering white libations, one declares:
*"I wish to transmit the Dao of Longevity to a certain individual, and place the Elixir Canon upon the seat.
Now, I desire to join this Dao."*

Facing north, one must prostrate oneself for the duration of a **shi** (时, double-hour).
If the sky is clear and the wind still, the transmission may proceed.
Upon receiving the Dao, one must drink the blood of a white rooster as a pledge, and also receive the oral instructions for combining the elixir, as well as cast the golden figure and golden fish into the water.
Those without the **bone of the Immortal Sage** (神仙骨), even numbering ten million, shall never see this Dao.

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"To combine the Divine Elixir, one must seek the depths of mountains and great marshes, or the solitude of remote villages and barren wilderness.
If one must do so among people, it must be within high walls and thick barriers, ensuring that none from within or without can see.
The companions assisting should not exceed two or three."*

Beforehand, one must fast for seven days, bathe in fragrant waters, and maintain absolute purity.
One must avoid visiting households that have experienced impurity, death, or marriage.
The Yellow Emperor said:
*"To purchase divine medicines, one must first fast for seven days, bathing on the **Zi-Chou** (子丑) days, and buying them on the **Jǐ** (执) days.
One must sit in the **Yuededi** (月德地, Virtuous Moon Earth), refraining from contention over rank or status."*

**Xuannü** said:
*"The best days for refining medicines are the **Fifth of the Fifth Moon** (五月五日, Great Yang) and the **Seventh of the Seventh Moon** (七月七日).
The most auspicious days begin with **Jiazi** (甲子), **Dingwei** (丁巳), and **Kaichu** (开除) days, followed by **Jiaxian** (甲申), **Yiwei** (乙巳), and **Yimao** (乙卯) days.
The prohibited days for refining medicines are:*
- *Spring: **Wuxin** (戊辰) and **Jii** (己巳)*
- *Summer: **Dingwei** (丁巳), **Wuxian** (戊申), **Renxin** (壬辰), and **Jiyou** (己未)*
- *Autumn: **Wuxu** (戊戌) and **Xinhao** (辛亥), **Gengzi** (庚子)*
- *Winter: **Wuyin** (戊寅), **Jiyou** (己未), **Gui Mao** (癸卯), and **Guiyou** (癸酉)*
*Additionally, the days of **Yue Sha** (月杀, Moon Killing), **Zhi Tianji** (支天季, Heavenly Season of the Branches), **Four Meng Zhongji** (四孟仲季, Mid-Season of the Four Beginnings), **Yue Shou** (月收, Moon Collecting), **Renwu** (壬午), **Bingxu** (丙戌), **Guihao** (癸亥), and **Xinwei** (辛巳), as well as all **Yue Jian** (月建, New Moon) and **Zhu Wang** (朔望, Full Moon) days are inauspicious.
*One must not use these days to kindle fires or refine the Divine Elixir."*

One must be cautious not to converse with the vulgar or associate with ignorant, gossipy, or untrustworthy individuals who do not believe in the Dao.
If such people hear of it, the divine medicine shall fail to manifest.

Once the divine medicine is perfected, one becomes a **True Person** (真人), able to ascend to the heavens or descend into the depths, to transform and vanish at will, and to elevate one’s entire family to immortality—why limit oneself to a single body?

The vulgar covet wealth and do not combine the elixir, nor do they trust in herbal medicines.
For herbs and woods, when buried, they rot; when boiled, they decay; when burned, they char.
How can they, which do not even sustain themselves, sustain others?
They may only treat illnesses and nourish the **qi**, yet still cannot escape death.

The essential secrets of the supreme Dao of the Returning Elixir are not common knowledge.

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"When kindling the fire, one must perform a sacrifice at the cauldron’s edge.
Use fine white wine, five *sheng* (升);
dried beef and mutton, three *jin* (斤) each;
yellow millet rice, two *sheng*;
large dates, three *sheng*;
pears, one *dou* (斗);
boiled chicken eggs, thirty in number;
three crucian carp, each weighing three *jin*.
All offerings must be placed in three tables, and each table must contain two cups.
Burn incense and bow twice."*

The Master of Rituals said:
*"Your humble servant [Name], a minor Daoist adept, sincerely invokes the Great Dao Lord, the Old Lord, and the Lord of Great Harmony.
On this day, your humble servant [Name], greedy for life and enamored with the Dao, commands that the elixir not ascend nor perish—all must be subdued by fire.

When the elixir is refined and pure, it transforms with each touch: yellow and white, all suppressed. Upon consuming the elixir, one ascends as an immortal, attending the Purple Palace, with life prolonged boundlessly, attaining the Supreme True Person.

The ritual of wine invocation is complete; twice more I bow. All red fruits, woods, tangerines, and pomelos are offered in full, then fire is kindled as prescribed.

The Yellow Emperor said:
*'To craft the Divine Elixir, first prepare the Mysterious Yellow.
The method for Mysterious Yellow: Take ten *jin* (斤) of quicksilver, twenty *jin* of lead, and place them in an iron vessel. Fiercely subject them to fire below, and the lead and quicksilver will emit their refined essence—purple as violet or golden as yellow gold.

With an iron spoon, collect and name it Mysterious Yellow.
It is also called Yellow Essence, Yellow Sprout, and Yellow Light.
Now, place the substance in a bamboo tube and subject it to a hundred steams. Then, with Realgar and Cinnabar water, mix and let it ascend. The Realgar and Cinnabar water are found in *The Thirty-Six Waters*.

The Yellow Emperor said:
*'Again, prepare the Six-One Mud.
The method for mud: Use alum, martial salt, brine, and gypsum—four substances. First, roast them. For twenty days, command the left-facing oysters of the Eastern Sea, the red stone pitch, and the talc.
In total, seven substances, divided by measure.
The quantities are at one’s discretion; pound them with ten thousand mortars until they become fine as powder.
In an iron vessel, combine and wrap them, then subject to fire for nine days and nine nights.
Fiercely apply the fire below; the elixir turns a true red, like flame.
Pound it again with ten thousand mortars, sift through silk, and blend with the hundred-day flower pool to make mud.
When ready, open it.

Use the mud to coat an earthenware cauldron, ensuring it can hold eight or nine *sheng* (升), or up to one *dou* (斗) for larger ones.
Apply the coating so that both inside and outside are three *fen* (分) thick.
When complete, place it in the midday sun for ten days, until it is thoroughly dry.
Then take orpiment and roast it, until it is golden in hue.
Take the earlier Mysterious Yellow in equal measure, blend with the hundred-day flower pool, and coat the earthenware cauldron inside and out to three *fen* thick. Expose it for ten days, until fully dry.
Then it may be used to refine the elixir’s essence.

Another method: When the elixir vessel and Six-One Mud are prepared, place the lid inside and dry it in the shade. The vessel should be three or four *chi* (尺) above the ground, ensuring it does not become damp.
The first—The Divine Elixir is called *Danhua*.
Its preparation requires true sand—one *jin*.
Or it may be two *jin*.
Or it may be ten *jin*."*

「The quantity is flexible, according to one’s wealth or poverty.
Place it within the cauldron.
Cover it with brine and pound it.
Coat the cauldron’s mouth with Six-One Mud, ensuring no leakage occurs.
Carefully observe it—do not let any cracks form like hair, for then all the elixir’s essence will scatter and fly away.
Only the dregs will remain, which are useless to consume.
Once coated, dry it for a few days, then it may be used.
If not thoroughly dry, it must not be heated.

First, ignite it with *Mǎtōng* husks.
Five *cùn* (寸) from the cauldron, warm it for nine days and nine nights, then fan the flames toward it, again for nine days and nine nights.
Next, place a fire-bag around the cauldron’s midsection for nine days and nine nights.
In total, this spans thirty-six days.
Then cease the fire for one day, allowing the elixir’s essence to rise and cling above—like five-colored *lánggān* (琅玕) or a shooting star, or like frost and snow, or pure red like cinnabar, or green or purple.
Sweep it down with a *péng* (朋) brush; for every *jīn* (斤), it yields only four *liǎng* (两) of refined essence.
If the elixir does not submit to the fire, it must be made to fly again.
Mix it with *Xuánshuǐ* (玄水) essence and *Lónggāo* (龙膏) dew, blending thoroughly until moist.
Then place it once more in a *Xuánhuáng* (玄黄) cauldron, sealing the mouth as before.
Apply fierce flames and make it fly.
After thirty-six days, the elixir is complete.
In all, the process takes seventy-two days.

To consume the elixir, one must observe five to seven days of fasting, purification, and bathing, then burn incense.
At dawn, facing east, kneel and bow in reverence before taking it—like a grain of *dàshǔsù* (大黍粟), or perhaps like a small bean.

The refined adept, upon consuming it, ascends to Heaven in seven days.
The mediocre adept attains immortality in seventy days.
The foolish mortal achieves transcendence in a year.

This *Danhua* (丹华) essence, the second elixir refined by the cauldron’s flight,
along with the Nine Elixirs and all divine elixirs, is supremely beneficial.

*Xuánnǚ* (玄女) says:
When the *Danhua* (丹华) is complete, test it by making gold.
If gold forms, the elixir is complete.
If gold does not form, the elixir is not complete.
An unrefined elixir cannot be consumed.
This failure may stem from either an imperfect cauldron coating or violating prohibitions.

Recheck the earlier flight method.
If a *Lónggāo* (龙膏) pill the size of a small bean is formed,
place it in fierce flames, blow it with a bellows for a short time—it will immediately become poor gold.
Again, take twenty-four *zhū* (铢) of *Danhua* (丹华) essence
and mix it with one *jīn* (斤) of powdered mercury—it will also form yellow gold.
If yellow gold is made, use it to fill a container for the elixir;
or take one *zhū* (铢) of *Danhua* (丹华) essence
and add it to one *jīn* (斤) of mercury, or one *jīn* (斤) of lead.
Apply strong flames and gradually blow it fiercely—all will become yellow gold.

The ratio of *jīn* (斤) to *zhū* (铢) must be precise; do not exceed it,
for then the gold will be hard and unyielding.
Do not reduce it,
for then the gold will be soft and malleable—
both results will fail to withstand hammering.

It is also said:
If gold forms, the world can be transformed.
If gold does not form, life cannot be sustained.
All efforts are wasted—what protection is there in the outcome?

*(Annotations: *Dàshǔsù* (大黍粟) = large millet grain; *Lánggān* (琅玕) = a type of precious stone; *Mǎtōng* (马通) = a plant used in alchemical fire; *Xuánnǚ* (玄女) = a mythical female alchemical deity; *Péng* (朋) = a brush for sweeping; *Fen* (分), *Chi* (尺), *Cùn* (寸), *Jīn* (斤), *Liǎng* (两), *Zhū* (铢) = traditional units of measurement.)*

The second **Divine Elixir** is named **Divine Seal**.

Take **mercury** without toxicity.
Adjust its quantity as needed and place it within a **six-to-one clay furnace** (六一泥釜), seal it tightly, and dry it thoroughly—just as when refining **Dan Hua** (丹华).

Fly it nine times; when the **upper and lower coldness** (上下寒) appears, sweep and gather it, blending with **carp bile** (鲤鱼胆).
Reseal and coat it as before, then fly it again nine times.
When the **upper and lower coldness** (上下寒) appears once more, sweep and gather it, blending with **Dragon Tallow** (龙膏).
This is called **Divine Seal**.

Take **ten catties of lead** (铅) and **Dan Hua** (黄华), measure it into a vessel, and heat it with **charcoal fire** (炭火).
Then take **seven catties of mercury** (水银) and pour it into the lead.
Apply fierce fire for a brief moment—its essence will rise and emerge,
in form like **yellow gold** (黄金), yet also resembling a **falling star** (流星).
Purple-red droplets flow like pearls;
five-colored **mysterious yellow** (玄黄) radiance.
Use an **iron spoon** (铁匙) to collect it.
If you obtain ten catties, it will refine into **Nine Transformations** (九转).
This is called **Yellow of Dan Hua** (丹华之黄),
also known as **Liquid of Mysterious Yellow** (玄黄之液) and **Seal of Heaven and Earth** (天地之符).

Then pound and refine the **mercury** (汞), transforming it into an elixir,
which is named **Returning Elixir** (还丹).
The **Sages** (圣人) keep it concealed.
It is not known by ordinary Daoist practitioners (凡俗道士),
nor by those of uncommon insight (殊达者) unless they truly understand.

Fire is named **Zǐmíng** (子明).
Mercury is also named **Zǐmíng**.
One is the essence of lead—
also called **Tàiyín** (太阴),
**Jīngōng** (金公), **Héchē** (河车),
**Chāinǚ** (姹女), or **Lìzhìshí** (立制石).

The ignorant in their craft simply use **Lìzhìshí** from the mountains—
this is incorrect.
The **True Ones** (真人) say:
*"All stone bile comes from lead.*
The foolish masses, refining divine medicines,
wrongly use **Qiānglǐ stone bile**—
this is false, a path diverging ten thousand *lǐ* from the Dao.
Because of this, the medicine fails."*

The **True Ones** say:
*"Refine cinnabar essence into flowing pearl frost,
lead essence into **Returning Elixir** (还丹),
and **yellow-white** (黄白) perfection is achieved—
take it, and you become a transcendent immortal.
Without these two substances, even if the medicine attains elixir form,
taking it is still akin to awaiting death."*

**Tàiyín** is lead; **Tàiyáng** is cinnabar.
Take nine *jīn* of mercury and one *jīn* of lead,
place them together in a red-earth crucible,
and apply fierce fire from midday until noon the next day.

Some say:
*"At the hour of **shuì** (巳, 11 AM–1 PM),
mercury and lead essence both emerge,
golden in hue—
named **Huángjīng** (黄精),
also **Huángyá** (黄芽),
**Huángqīng** (黄轻),
and **Huánghuá** (黄华).
Boil it with **jǐnghuá water** (井华水),
and it is called **Huánghuá Pool** (黄华池),
also **Huánglóng** (黄龙),
**Huángfú** (黄服),
or **Lìzhìshí** again.*

Take **mysterious yellow** (玄黄) and mix it with **mysterious water essence** (玄水液),
knead it into pills like sealing wax,
and place them in a red-earth crucible,
sealing with **liùyī mud** (六一泥) three *fēn* thick inside and out.
Let it dry for ten days without leakage.
Burn it with **Mǎtōng** (马通) or husk fuel for eighty days—
the **golden medicine** will then be complete.

Take one *dāojī* (刀圭) of **mysterious yellow**,
place it in fierce fire, and blow it with a bellows for the time it takes to eat a meal—
it will all dissolve into **gold**.

If the gold does not form, the medicine remains raw and cannot be used.
Return it to the red-earth crucible,
reseal it with sealing wax,
and fire it again for eighty days—
only then may the medicine be taken.

**Mysterious yellow** is also called **Fúdān** (伏丹) or **Zǐfěn** (紫粉).
To take it, do so on a **jiǎzǐ day** (甲子) at dawn,
facing south, bowing twice with knees bent,
swallowing one pill the size of a small bean daily.
After a hundred days, you will become immortal,
all ailments cured—
even severe madness and leprosy vanish,
and there is no plague you cannot overcome.

Then take the **hundred-day Huá Pool** (百日华池),
mix it with **mysterious yellow** into a paste,
and place it in a red-earth crucible,
sealing inside and out with three *fēn* of mud.
Add one *jīn* of mercury—
or up to ten *jīn*—
as much medicine as desired.
Three *jīn* suffice for one immortal.

Extract ten *liǎng* of **mysterious yellow essence**,
take three *jīn* of mercury,
place it in an earthen crucible,
cover it with **mysterious yellow** two *cùn* thick,
seal it with another crucible,
and bind it with **liùyī mud**,
ensuring no leakage.
Expose it to the sun until thoroughly dry,
then fire it.

If it is damp, do not fire—
heat will cause it to crack.
Follow the method for refining **Danhuá** (丹华):
burn with **Mǎtōng** husk fuel for nine days and nights,
then rest it for one day.
When opened, the medicine will rise like frost on the crucible—
purple, crimson, vermilion, and green radiance,
two *fēn* thick.
Sweep it down with feathers,
mixing it with **yellow dog bile**—
or **Hébó’s leftover fish bile**—
as the secret says:
*"This is **crucian carp bile**."*

Some say:
*"Knead this **mysterious yellow** into sealing wax."*

The note says:
*"The substance used for pill-making is **water from springs**."*

Reseal and return it to the crucible,
covering it with **mysterious yellow** one *cùn* thick.
Some say:
*"Seal the crucible tightly,
bind it with **liùyī mud** as before,
expose it to the sun for ten days until fully dry—
do not fire if damp.
Once heated, the crucible will crack."*

Refine it again for nine days and nights,
then rest it for one day.
When opened, sweep down the rising essence—
if only purple, it is called **Shénfú Huándān** (神符还丹).
Mix it with **lónggāo** (龙膏) into bean-sized pills.

Take them daily at dawn on a **jiǎzǐ day**,
facing south, bowing twice with knees bent.
After a hundred days, you will meet immortals,
**Yùnǚ** (玉女) will come to you,
and you will ascend with the gods, flying through the skies.

To cross great waters,
mix **Shénfú** with **lónggāo**,
or apply **Hébó’s bile** to your feet—
you will walk upon the water without sinking.

To enter fire,
take one pill, and you will feel no heat.

After a hundred days of taking the medicine,
the **Three Corpses and Nine Worms** (三尸九虫) will self-destruct,
granting eternal life.

---
**The Third Divine Elixir** is called **Shéndān** (神丹).

First, coat the inside and outside of two red-earth crucibles
with **liùyī mud**, three *fēn* thick each.

Take **mǔlì** (牡蛎), **chìshízhī** (赤石脂), and **císhí** (磁石)—
if no magnetite is available, retain the original text unchanged.
Divide these three substances equally,
pestle them ten thousand times into powder.
Mix with **hundred-day Huá Pool** until moistened.

Some say:
*"Place it in a straight crucible,
coat the inner surface,
then apply **mysterious yellow essence** on top,
one *cùn* thick."*

Take two *jīn* of **Dìnán** (帝男, realgar) and one *jīn* of **Dìnǚ** (帝女, orpiment).
First, moisten them with **hundred-day Huá Pool**,
then grind them in an iron mortar ten thousand times
until they become powder.
Place them in the crucible,
cover with **yellow powder** one *cùn* thick,
seal it with another crucible,
and bind it with **liùyī mud**—
ensure no **qi** escapes.
Let it dry for ten days.

Then burn it with **Mǎtōng** husk fuel for nine days and nights,
keeping the fire five *cùn* from the crucible’s edge.
Use a fire-pusher to surround it for nine days and nights.
Push the fire inward until it reaches the crucible’s center,
then apply fierce flame to its lower half for nine days and nights—
a total of thirty-six days.
Rest it for one day.

With a feather, sweep away the flying essence adhering above, then mix it with **Dragon Fat** and introduce it into the crucible.
Seal it again with mud, dry it, and fire it for another thirty-six days.
*Some say*: twenty-seven days.
Then, after cooling it for one day, open it—the flying essence will adhere above. This is called **Flying Essence**; those who refine it call it **Divine Elixir**.

The superior adept, taking one *dāo* of it daily for fifty days, becomes a transcendent.
The mediocre adept requires a hundred days; the foolish, a year—then they too become transcendent.
Even common men, women, children, slaves, and livestock who ingest it shall become immortal and never die.
It wards off the Five Weapons; when worn as an amulet, it guards against all calamities.

After taking the elixir for a hundred days, all transcendent beings will come to welcome them—**Yùnán** (玉男), **Yùnǚ** (玉女), **Yùntóng** (玉童)—along with mountain marshals and marshals of the marshes, appearing in human form.
The method depends on one’s own cultivation; it is not inherited.

---
**Fourth Divine Elixir**, called **Returning Elixir**:
Take **alum stone**, **yellow ore**, **red earth**, **martial salt**, **oysters**, **red stone pitch**, **earth dragon arrow**, **mica**, and **soapstone**—nine substances in total.
Burn each for one day and night with fierce flame, then grind them separately until powdered.
Mix with **Left Elixir** until it resembles mud.
Place in a crucible one *cùn* deep, adding one *jīn* of **mercury**.
Then layer **realgar**, **copper acetate**, **alum stone**, **yellow pitch**, **saltpetre**, **Yǔyúliáng** (禹余粮, "Yu’s surplus grain"), and **alum stone** again, with **yellow ore** on top and **mercury** alone at the bottom—seven substances in total, each ground separately into powder.
Place the **mercury** (one *jīn*) alone at the bottom, then layer the rest in order.
Seal the crucible with **Left Elixir** and **liùyī mud**, drying it for ten days.
Place it on three iron tripods, nine *cùn* high, and fire it with **Mǎtōng** husk fuel, keeping the flame five *cùn* from the crucible’s base.
Let the fire burn for nine days and nights until it reaches the crucible’s center.
Then increase the flame to the crucible’s midpoint for another nine days and nights.
Constantly dampen the crucible’s surface with a wet cloth to prevent the medicine from dispersing.
When the cloth dries, rewet it.
After eighty-one days, cool it for one day, then open it—the medicine will rise as five-colored vapors, adhering to the crucible’s lid. This is the **Flying Method**, the essence of the alchemy.

Sweep the vapors with a **parrot’s feather**, mix them with **hundred herbs’ flowers**, and dissolve in **well-bloom water** to ingest.
After a hundred days, a **crimson bird** and **phoenix** will hover above, and divine beings and **Yùnǚ** will arrive.
After two hundred days, one can ascend to heaven or descend to earth, with transcendent beings attending.
After a year, **Tàiyī** (太一) will welcome them in a **cloud chariot** drawn by dragons.

Those who take this elixir will never feel hunger or thirst and will live a hundred years.
They may drink from **stone springs**, eat twenty **dates and chestnuts**, and consume five *cùn* of **dried meat**.

Moreover, if **Returning Elixir** is used to inscribe **amulets**, the money will return on its own when used in trade.
If written on a **target’s frame**, all ghosts will flee in terror.
Additionally, if one *dāo* of the elixir is mixed with powdered **mercury** (one *jīn*) and fired, it instantly becomes **true gold**.
*Another method*: mix the medicine with **Dragon Fat** and fire it for nine days and nights to produce genuine gold.

---
**Fifth Divine Elixir**, called **Nourishing Elixir**:
Take one *jīn* of **mercury** and place it in a **liùyī crucible**.
Add one *jīn* of **realgar**, ground into powder, layering it over the mercury.
Then add one *jīn* of **Yǔyúliáng**, ground into powder, layering it over the realgar.
Seal the crucible’s rim with **liùyī mud**, dry it, and fire it with **Mǎtōng** husk fuel for nine days and nights.
Then switch to **charcoal fire**, burning for another nine days and nights.
After cooling for one day, open it—the medicine will rise as frost-like vapors, adhering to the lid.
Sweep it with a feather, mix with **Dragon Fat** and **Shàoshì Tiānxióng** (少室天雄, "Heavenly Tiger of Shao Mountain") in equal parts—*or* **parrot blood**—into *dāo* doses.
Taking one *dāo* daily for thirty days grants **feathered ascension**; myriad spirits will attend, and **Yùnǚ** may be summoned.
Transcendent beings will welcome them to ascend to heaven.
Even **ghosts, ancestral spirits, and wind/rain deities** will come to serve them.

---
**Sixth Elixir**, called **Refined Elixir**:
Take eight stones to forge it.
The eight stones are: **Bāyuè cinnabar**, **realgar**, **orpiment** (ground to fly), **copper acetate**, **alum stone**, **yellow ore**, **stone gall**, and **lodestone**—eight substances in equal parts, ground separately into powder and mixed with **earth dragon fat**.
Take two *shāng* of **earth dragon arrow**, combined with **yellow dog’s liver and gall**, forming the crucible.
Grind **oysters** and **red stone pitch** (three *jīn* each) into powder.
Mix with **Left Elixir** to form mud, coating the crucible’s interior and exterior, three *fēn* thick, and dry it.
*Another method*: adjust the proportions freely, using **earth dragon fat** and one *shāng* of **earth dragon arrow**, mixed with **yellow dog’s gall**, then two *shāng* of **earth dragon arrow**, along with powdered **oysters** and **red stone pitch**, forming mud to coat the crucible’s interior and exterior, three *fēn* thick, and dry it.

Layer the eight stones in powdered form: **cinnabar** at the bottom, then **realgar**, **orpiment**, **copper acetate**, **alum stone**, **yellow ore**, **stone gall**, and **lodestone** on top.
Seal the crucible with **liùyī mud** at the rim, drying it as before.
Fire it with **Mǎtōng** husk fuel for thirty-six days.
After cooling for one day, open it—the medicine will rise as frost-like vapors, adhering to the lid.
Sweep it with a feather, mix with **Dragon Fat**, and pill into **small mung bean** sizes.
Take one pill daily after meals; in ten days, one becomes transcendent.
Ghosts and spirits will attend and obey.

It can also be used to forge gold.
Not only men—women too may ascend as immortals.
If one wishes to abstain from grains, let them always refrain from sexual intercourse, drinking only water and avoiding all contact.

This elixir’s dregs can cure a hundred ailments.
Another method: fuse lead to make gold, then refine it into elixir. Combine one *jin* of mercury with *dāo guī* (male and female minerals), and fire it until gold forms.

Some say *soft cinnabar* resembles *refined elixir*—smooth, glossy, and easy to ingest.

**The Seventh Elixir, called Soft Cinnabar:**
Take three *jin* of mercury, mix it with *zuǒwèi* (left mineral) and *Xuányuán* (primordial yellow) into a paste, then coat the inside and outside of an earthen crucible, three *fēn* thick each.
Place the mercury inside a crucible, seal the rim with *liùyī* mud, and dry it for ten days.
Then fire it, following the *Tàidān Huá* method, for thirty-six days.
After cooling for one day, open it—the vapors will rise like frost on the crucible’s lid. Sweep them with a feather, mix with *Dragon Fat*, and take as *small mung bean* pills, three daily, to become immortal and deathless.

If mixed with *dízhì* (antimony juice), a ninety-year-old man who takes it for twenty days will turn his white hair black, strengthening his *yang* essence and *yin* qi. Even with intercourse, he will father countless children.

With *soft cinnabar*, one may draw on *wu tong* wood to create living figures.
Writing characters with it ensures slaves will never flee.
An eighty-year-old woman who takes it will bear children.
A high-ranking official who takes it will be promoted.

With lead, combine it by fire to form gold and silver, another name being *Huángjīn* (Yellow Gold).
The eighth elixir is called *Fù Dān* (Suppressed Elixir).
Its hue is dark purple, like a five-colored radiance.

Take one *catty* of mercury, or even more.
Use *Xuányuán Huá* (Dark Yellow Flower) to refine the earthen crucible, making its interior and exterior each three *fen* thick.
Then add *dízhì* (antimony juice), *zéng qīng* (magnetite), and *cǐshí* (lodestone), grinding them into powder.
Apply the *Xuányuán Huá* to the crucible, then layer the powders of *zéng qīng* and *cǐshí* over the mercury.
Seal it with another crucible, coat the junction with *Liùyī* (Six-One) mud, and dry it for ten days.
Then ignite it with *Mǎtōng* (horse-dung) charcoal fire for nine days and nights.
Turn the upper crucible to become the lower one, and fire it again for nine days and nights.
Repeat this process, alternating upper and lower crucibles, nine times in total before stopping.
Cool it for one day, then open it—sweep with a feather to collect what rises and clings to the lid.
Mix with *Dragon Fat*, then return the residue to the crucible and fire it once more for ten days before stopping.
Cool it again for one day, open it, sweep to collect what rises and clings to the lid, and grind it into powder.
Store it in a gold or silver tube, or in a fresh bamboo tube.
At dawn, face the sun with hands bound, bow twice in a long kneeling posture, and swallow one *dāo guī* (knife-shaped dose) in *jǐnghuá* (well-flowered) water—this will make one a Daoist immortal.
If shaped into a pill the size of a date pit and carried in the hand, it banishes one hundred spirits.
If written on doors and thresholds with this *róu Dān* (Soft Elixir), all malevolent spirits, *jiāngmèi* (rogue spirits), and *bìméngliángliáng* (demonic entities) dare not approach.
It also repels thieves and bandits, even tigers and wolves will avoid it.
If a woman guards herself alone and keeps such a pill the size of a large soybean, one hundred spirits and thieves will flee far and not dare to come.

The ninth elixir is called *Hán Dān* (Cold Elixir).
Its method uses a red-earth crucible, coated inside and out with *Liùyī* mud to a thickness of three *fen*, and dried as per the *Dān Huá* (Elixir Flower) method.
Take one *catty* each of *Dì Nán* (Imperial Male—realgar), *Dì Nǚ* (Imperial Female—orpiment), *zéng qīng* (magnetite), *yùshí* (sulfur), and *cǐshí* (lodestone), grinding them separately into powder.
First, apply the *Xuányuán Huá* to the *Liùyī* crucible as per the *Dān Huá* method.
Then place one *catty* of *liúzhū* (sulfur pearls) into the crucible.
Next, layer *Dì Nán* over the *liúzhū*, followed by *Dì Nǚ*, then *zéng qīng*, *yùshí*, and finally *cǐshí* on top.
Seal it with another crucible, coat the junction with *Liùyī* mud to a thickness of three *fen*.
Additionally, mix half a *catty* each of *tǔlóngshǐ* (earth dragon’s arrow—possibly a type of clay or mineral) and yellow soil into a paste.
One alternative method states: coat it with *mǔlì* (oyster shell) and *chìshí zhī* (red stone pitch—possibly cinnabar or red lead) to a thickness of three *fen*.
Then coat it again with *tǔlóngshǐ*.
Expose it to the sun for ten days until it dries.

Now, with gentle fire, first refining with *Wén* (cultivation), then with *Wǔ* (martial/transformation), for nine nights.
On the tenth day, let it cool, then open it and sweep away with feathers what adheres to the top.
Mix with *lónggāo* (dragon fat—possibly a resinous substance) and yellow dog bile, forming pills the size of small beans.
At dawn, with *jǐnghuá* (well-bloom water—water exposed to sunlight), facing the sun and bowing twice, swallow one pill.
This will make the body light, and within a hundred days, all ailments will vanish.
A *yùnǚ* (jade maiden) will attend you, the *sīmìng* (record-keeper of fate) will erase your name from the register of death, and you will be inscribed in the register of immortals.
You may then fly above and below, entering and exiting without hindrance, beyond all constraint.
You may sit and vanish, or rise lightly upon the clouds, ascending to heaven.

---
**The Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon, Volume One, Complete**
**The Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon, Volume Two: The Origin and Method of Obtaining the Refined Elixir**

The subject reports: The Nine Methods of Returning the Elixir stem from the Nine Heavens’ *Yuándào* (Primordial Dao), the supreme scripture of the Nine Directions.
In ancient times, the True Persons *Wáng Qiāo*, *Chìsōngzǐ*, and the Yellow Emperor received it from *Xuǎnnǚ* (the Mysterious Maiden).
*Xuǎnnǚ* is a celestial maiden.

The first Dao illuminates the True Person’s Way. *Sùnǚ* (the Naked Maiden), the True Person, is the sovereign of the immortals.
As the teacher of Heaven and Earth, her rank is *Zhēnrén* (True Person), and all immortals revere her.
The True Person is born before Heaven and dies after Earth. Water cannot drown them, fire cannot burn them, poison cannot harm them, and weapons cannot injure them.
Their divine transformations are boundless, their will unfettered, and they command the multitudes of immortals without fail.
They discern the essence of spiritual medicines and communicate with the numinous.
Thus the scripture says: “This is the True Person.”

Those who ingest the elixir become immortals, attaining the rank of True Person, even able to summon the Wind Lord and command the Rain Master.

The rank of *xiānrén* (immortal) surpasses a hundred ghosts and subdues ten thousand spirits.
This is achieved through the ingestion of minor elixirs—cloud mother, eight minerals, and herbal medicines.

The *qīngyāo yùnǚ* (green-waisted jade maiden) is the daughter of the Wind Lord, inferior to *Xuǎnnǚ* and *Sùnǚ*.
The *yùnǚ* are mortal women who, upon attaining the Dao, are titled as such and serve as consorts or attendants to immortals.

This *Jiǔdān Jīng* originates from *Wáng Qiāo*, *Chìsōngzǐ*, and the Yellow Emperor receiving it from *Xuǎnnǚ*—not from lesser immortals like myself.

The subject reports: *Gě Hóng* states in the *Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon*:
“The Yellow Emperor ingested it and thus ascended to Heaven.
If one practices breathing exercises and ingestion of herbal medicines, one may prolong life—but death is still inevitable.
If one ingests the divine elixir, however, one attains boundless longevity, equal to Heaven’s completion.
One may ride the clouds and dragons, ascending and descending the *Tàiqīng* (Great Clarity).”

Thus, the Yellow Emperor transmitted it to *Xuánzǐ* (the Mysterious Sage), who declared:
“This Dao is of utmost importance—it must be passed only to the worthy.
Even if one possesses mountains of gold, do not transmit it to the unworthy.”

Those who receive it must cast a golden man and golden fish into flowing water as an oath, swearing with enemy blood.
Without the bones of an immortal, one cannot even hear or see this Dao.
Those who hear or see it have the fate to possess this Dao.

When refining the elixir, one must seek secluded mountain peaks, places untouched by men, and never gather more than three companions.
First, observe a hundred days of purification, bathe in five-scented waters, and maintain absolute purity—avoid all defilement and contact with commoners or those who doubt the Dao.
For if such persons speak ill of the divine medicine, the elixir will fail.
If successful, the entire household becomes immortal—not just one person.
Commoners should not refine divine elixirs, nor should they rely solely on herbal medicines.
Herbal medicines rot when buried, decay when boiled, char when burned, and decompose when left idle.
How can they, which cannot sustain themselves, sustain a person?
How can they, which cannot fortify themselves, fortify a person?

This Ninefold Elixir is the key to eternal life—beyond the comprehension of ordinary mortals.

**First Elixir: *Huádān* (Flower Elixir)**
The scripture says: “Ingesting this elixir grants immortality in seven days.”
Form pills with *Xuángāo* (mysterious fat) and place them over fierce flames—momentarily, they become yellow gold.
Again, with 240 *shū* (a small weight measure) of this elixir and 100 *jīn* (catty) of mercury, when heated to a red glow, it becomes yellow gold.
If the gold does not form, reseal the medicine and heat it again—when the days are sufficient, the scripture says: “The essence is unformed.”

**Second Elixir: *Shénfú Dān* (Divine Symbol Elixir)**
The scripture says: “Ingesting it grants immortality in a hundred days.”
When crossing great waters, anointing the soles with this elixir allows one to walk upon the surface without sinking.
It dispels the *sānshī jiǔchóng* (three corpses and nine pests), and all ailments are cured.

**Third Elixir: *Shéndān* (Divine Elixir)**
The scripture says: “Ingesting one *dāoguī* (a measure of elixir) grants immortality in a hundred days.”
Even if swallowed by livestock, they will never age or die.
It also repels the five weapons.
After a hundred days, a *yùnǚ* (jade maiden) will attend you, and mountain spirits and ghosts will regard you in human form.

**Fourth Elixir: *Huándān* (Return Elixir)**
The scripture says: “Ingesting one *dāoguī* grants immortality in a hundred days.”
The *zhūquè fènghuáng* (vermilion bird and phoenix) will hover above, and a *yùnǚ* will attend you.
With one *dāoguī*, take 1 *jīn* of mercury and heat it—it instantly becomes yellow gold.
Anointing money or objects with this elixir causes them to return the next day.
Writing this elixir on a mortal’s eyes causes all ghosts to flee in terror.

**Fifth Elixir: *Ēdān* (Nourishment Elixir)**
The scripture says: “Ingesting it grants immortality in forty days, with ghosts and spirits attending, and a *yùnǚ* arriving.”

**Sixth Elixir: *Liàndān* (Refined Elixir)**
The scripture says: “Ingesting it grants immortality in fifteen days.”
It also, when combined with mercury and fire, becomes yellow gold.

**Seventh Elixir: *Rǔdān* (Soft Elixir)**
The scripture says: “Ingesting one *dāoguī* grants immortality in a hundred days.”
When mixed with autumn *fùpén zhī* (mulberry leaf juice) and ingested, even a ninety-year-old man may father children.
When combined with lead and heated, it becomes yellow gold.

**Eighth Elixir: *Fúdān* (Subduing Elixir)**
The scripture says: “Ingesting it grants immortality immediately.”

---

With an elixir the size of a date pit worn as an amulet, a hundred ghosts will flee in terror.
If this elixir is inscribed on a door, malevolent spirits dare not approach, and it also repels thieves, bandits, tigers, and wolves.

**Ninth Elixir: *Hándān* (Cold Elixir)**
The scripture says: “Ingesting one *dāoguī* grants immortality in a hundred days, with *yùnǚ* arriving to attend, and the ability to soar and rise lightly.”

The scripture also says: “All nine elixirs, when properly combined into one, will grant immortality.”

It does not matter if they are all made; it depends on what the practitioner desires.
Those who wish to ingest the nine elixirs and ascend to heaven may do so at will, or if they wish to cease human questioning, they may also do so at will—then they can freely enter and exit without harm.

According to my study, the *Jīnyè huándān* (Golden Liquid Return Elixir) method, when combined, requires ingesting one *liǎng* (two *qīán*—a unit of weight) to ascend as an immortal.
If one does not yet wish to leave the mortal realm but instead desires to become a *dìxiān* (Earthly Immortal), they should fast for one hundred days, then ingest half a *liǎng*, and thus attain eternal life without dying, immune to all calamities and poisons, able to keep wife and children.

If one holds an official rank, they may act according to their desires without restriction.
If later they wish to ascend to heaven, they should fast again and ingest the full nine elixirs, completing one *liǎng*, and then immediately soar as an immortal.

All who wish to ascend to heaven must first abstain from grains for over a year before ingesting the elixirs.

According to my further study of the *Zhēnrén Jiǔshēng Jīng* (Scripture of the True Person’s Nine Ascents), those who ingest the nine elixirs to ascend to heaven should follow the prescribed days as in the main scripture.
If one desires to become an Earthly Immortal, they may ingest half the amount, storing the rest—even if stored, they will still attain eternal life without harm, beyond all danger.
Later, if they wish to ascend to heaven, they should ingest the remaining elixirs.

According to these teachings, those who ingest the divine elixirs and great medicines, following the scriptural days, will ascend lightly to heaven.
If they store and ingest half, they will attain eternal life without dying, becoming Earthly Immortals—of this there is no doubt.

I have heard that there are eight reasons why one may fail in cultivating the Dao:
1. They casually learn one technique and claim it sufficient, toiling over tripods and flames, yet never achieving success by the time their hair turns white.
2. Though they seek extraordinary methods, they dismiss them as not true, relentlessly pursuing until they die with their coffin sealed.
3. They cannot distinguish truth from falsehood, study without a master, and lack a fixed resolve—thus wasting time and energy.
4. They rely on their own cleverness, neglecting the true teachings, and arrogantly believe they have already attained the Dao, failing to complete the master’s instructions.
5. The true methods and secrets are not easily seen or encountered; they believe they lie in famous mountains, risking life and limb to seek them.
6. Their family lacks even a single *dàn* (unit of weight) of resources, and hunger and cold press upon them—whether they obtain the methods or not, they know them as little as if they did not.
7. Their nature lacks focus and perseverance, and even after a master has imparted the secrets, they hesitate and do not act.
8. The teachers they encounter are themselves shallow and inferior, begrudgingly imparting only a little, claiming the Dao is scarce, and hoarding precious techniques as if they were true—thus leading to futile waiting like the *shǒuzhū* (one who waits for a fallen gourd).

The Dao does not lie in multiplicity; do not say that minor methods are insignificant, for even within the great elixirs, none surpass the *Jiǔdǐng* (Nine Tripods) Dao, transmitted by the True Person.
The True Person passed it to *Xuányǚ* (玄女), who in turn passed it to *Huángdì* (Yellow Emperor), who obtained it and passed it to *Xuánzǐ* (玄子). From that time onward, those who received the method became True Persons.
I have never heard of True Persons personally instructing others; those who attain it are worthy of esteem.

Later generations valued hearing over seeing, abandoning the near for the distant.
Thus, the First Emperor of Qin saw *Ānpí* (安期) yet lost the Dao,
and the Emperor Wu of Han sought *Shǎojiūn* (少君) without completing the method,
then searched for *Fāngzhàng* (方丈) and crossed the *Cāngbō* (沧波), yet ultimately failed to succeed, vainly striving for honors and rewards.

The skilled seeker does not rely on official appointment,
and the cunning taker does not labor under coercion.

When *Xuānyuán* (轩辕—Yellow Emperor) ruled the world, *Guǎngchéng* (广成) did not assist him, yet his virtuous governance was not diminished.
When *Tángyáo* (唐尧—Emperor Yao) held the Four Seas, *Cháoyóu* (巢由) did not aid him, yet his later virtue was not lacking.

The Four *Hào* (皓) were confined in *Shāngluò* (商洛), yet they did not hinder the Han’s many worthy scholars.
*Zhōudàng* (周党) composed poetry in the woods and marshes, yet it did not diminish the legal measures of Emperor *Xiàowén* (孝文).

The favored and noble could not sway their resolve;
their hearts were tranquil and silent,
their nature loathed flattery and noise,
they feared indulgence and shunned official honors as obstacles.
They lived in humble simplicity, dressed in coarse rags, and wore grass mats instead of fine robes.
They took the fragrant groves as their palaces,
the steep cliffs as their grand halls,
the emerald orchids as their mattresses,
the green leaves as their curtains.
They wore hemp garments instead of decayed silks,
and relied on gourd vines as their fine meals.
They did not till the fields to fill their bellies,
nor did their wives weave to cover their bodies.
They guarded their constancy until death,
despising the Three Joys (of music, women, and fine food),
fearing swift death,
not scheming for mere survival,
rejecting a thousand *jīn* (金) in weighty offers,
ignoring the prestige of high ministers,
free and unrestrained in their ways,
without worldly attachments—
all were praised in their time as noble and lofty.

These men could neither benefit the state above nor aid the people below.
Though the annals of history still speak of their names, they sought only the higher Dao of eternal life.

The art of learning the great methods of divine elixirs,
they refused to enslave their bodies to worldly affairs,
but relied solely on medicinal substances to aid themselves,
so that external calamities could not reach them,
and internal ailments would not arise.
They transformed their aged bodies and altered their forms,
enduring without death for long years,
their spirit undiminished.
They meticulously examined and refined countless techniques,
gaining their efficacy,
judging their merits and demerits,
and always striving to improve.
They despised the vulgarity of the earth,
treating fame as morning dew.
Within the Eight Extremes of existence,
how many would they curse?
Their aspirations were vast,
and their benefits profound.

The pursuit of this craft requires essential tools;
without these few individuals, it cannot be accomplished.
If pressed or coerced, success would not be attained.

When the winds of fame stir, the hearths of recluses grow cold;
when the Way of the Sage-King flourishes, extraordinary men withdraw.
Now the world is at peace, oxen rest, and horses roam free,
the beacon fires lie dormant, arms are sheathed,
the multitudes are subdued, and the world’s labors cease.
Yet, even in such times, men like **Zi Fang** (子房) emerge from their seclusion only to return to ordinary life,
and **Xin Bu** (信布) lay aside their armor to take up fishing and hunting.

Within the universe, few are earnest in their love of this Dao and capable of achieving it—
perhaps not one in ten thousand.

In days of old, the Yellow Emperor donned his ceremonial robes
and governed the world beneath the heavens,
his virtue as radiant as flowing pearls,
transforming frost and snow into dew.
In his era of elevated peace, he entrusted the affairs of state,
and after a hundred and ten years, his Dao was complete—
his body refined, he ascended as a **White Day Immortal**.

This was achieved through the power of **Guangcheng** (广成) and **Xuan Nü** (玄女),
not by mere chance.

In ancient times, the **Hao Wang** (昊王) struck stones to build his palaces,
and within the clefts of those stones, he found a book of purple script on golden tablets.
Unable to read it, he sent his emissary to consult Confucius,
saying: *"Hao Wang, in his leisure, saw a red crane peck at a book,
which he placed before the hall.
He does not know its meaning,
so he sends it far to seek your wisdom."*

Confucius examined the text and declared:
*"This is the **Lingbao** (灵宝) formula,
the method of eternal life,
which the Great Yu consumed,
and thus his lifespan matched the heavens and earth.
As Yu was about to ascend and transform,
he sealed this book within a mountain and stone vault.
Now you say the red crane pecked it—
this must be a heavenly gift."*

Thus it is known that from ancient times,
emperors and kings who eagerly sought eternal life
never failed to live long years.

Even if one searches but does not find,
it is better than not searching at all.
For there are those who, though not seeking,
still achieve it.

One need not fear the absence of the Dao within the heart,
but only that one does not strive diligently.
If one persists without ceasing,
one must attain it.

Again, those who seek the Dao
are like the poor man longing for wealth,
or the lowly desiring noble station—
how could the Dao ever be unattainable?

Yet, they fear their resolve is not steadfast,
pursuing immediate gains while neglecting distant ones.
They rejoice at hearing it and hasten to take their place,
but soon forget it as if it never existed.
Before minor advantages are even fully realized,
great losses have already befallen them.
How then can they hope to exhaust the profound and subtle,
and perfect the Dao after their knowledge has waned?

Even if their resolve is earnest and their efforts tireless,
without encountering a wise teacher,
they cannot succeed.

For those who study the art of eternal life,
the key lies in the elixirs,
and among elixirs, the greatest is the **secret formula**,
the **secret** of divine elixirs.
The Dao is the same, yet the **virtue/power** differs—
one swears to take them together,
and may attain them by righteous means,
but cannot suppress them by force.

In ancient times, the Great Yu did not compel **Bocheng Zi Gao** (伯成子高),
for he honored his superiority.
Confucius did not borrow from **Zixia** (子夏),
for he protected his shortcomings.

Lush fields, shallow waters,
vast wildernesses and hidden marshes,
where foxes and deer roam,
and rugged cliffs and secluded peaks abound—
these are the paths and dwellings of the immortals.
If one were to keep foxes and deer in splendid halls,
they would surely break free.
If one were to dismiss the immortals with high honors,
they would abandon their labors in resentment.

Thus, to study the **orthodox scriptures**,
it is as if one faces a true immortal.
To receive the **true secret formulas**,
it is as if one gains their very essence.

Even if false teachings should come,
and **Anqi** (安期) or **Zhengzi** (争子) arrive with contrary words,
the **orthodox scriptures** and **secret formulas** cannot be fully discarded—
there will always be minor differences.

I humbly pray that the **Sage-Sovereign** (圣主)
will carefully examine and choose the correct path to follow.

I have heard that if one trims the grass in spring,
even the **zhi** (芝, sacred mushrooms) will flourish.
If one disturbs the nests of cranes and phoenixes,
even they will not gather there.

**The Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon—Secret Formulas, Volume Two, ends.**
**The Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon—Secret Formulas, Volume Three, begins.**

To seek the **Dao** with clarity and receive the **secret formulas** without relying on the **True Persons’** methods—
I have heard that a teacher is not always constant, yet one should follow the good and take them as teacher.
Among three walking together, one must follow the virtuous.
Confucius’ **Dao** is unified in its essence.

The **Yellow Emperor** surveyed the methods of the world, seeking nothing he did not investigate.
If the **True Persons’** **Dao** and **secret formulas** are not passed down by **True Persons** themselves,
and the **Primordial Sovereign’s** scriptures are not taught by the **Primordial Sovereign**,
how different is it from **Bai Zi** attending upon **Confucius** to study with him,
or **Yu’s** governance awaiting **Gao Yao** to assist in harmony?
Wasting time and energy in such ways will never yield results.

Thus, the **Nine Cauldrons’ Dao** and the **methods of longevity**—
if pursued in this manner, it is no different from courting death.

Life is precious to cherish, death is dreadful to fear.
Each lost day is like a swift river’s passage—
morning dew vanishes by evening light,
and sighs of regret come too late.

Now, if one merely encounters those who know the methods,
points out their intent, and relentlessly seeks them out,
then verifies themself while forming bonds with trustworthy companions,
and remains steadfast in their covenant—
this alone is sufficient for self-realization.
There will be no need for **True Persons** or **Divine Women** to lend their aid.

After the elixir is complete, one’s intestines cleansed and the medicine taken,
**Jade Maidens** may attend, or **Azure Dragons** come to escort.
Before its completion, no such signs are heard.

Thus the **Primordial Sovereign** said:
*"Beware of revealing the divine elixir to others,
lest they mock the **Dao** and slander the **True**."*

If the **elixir scriptures** are passed to the unworthy,
misfortune will surely follow.
Only those of sincere faith may be granted a share of the elixir’s composition—
never should the scripture itself be given away.
This is the way of the **True Persons**,
who guard their secrets as fiercely as they pass down oral **formulas**.

If one claims to have seen a **True Person**,
or that a **master of the methods** attained the **Dao** without their aid—
as with **Shang’s** encounter with **Peng Zu**,
or **Zhou’s** meeting with **Lao Zi**,
**Qin Shi Huang’s** vision of **An Qi**,
or **Han Wu’s** reliance on **Shao Jun**—
none of these truly attained the **Dao**.

Those who study the **Dao** most abhor idle chatter,
desiring neither to be seen by the vulgar nor to mingle in worldly affairs.
They walk hidden paths, sit in secluded places,
and scorn defamation, savoring solitude in their pursuit of the **Dao**.
Since tastes differ, slander is inevitable—
they regret not fleeing distant roads to avoid suspicion,
or keeping a thousand miles between themselves and doubt.

Yet what do **True Persons** seek to attain?
They tread through flames unburned, walk upon dark waters unshaken,
soaring with wings in the void, riding clouds in wind-driven chariots,
ascending to the **Purple Palace**, descending to **Kunlun’s** peaks.
If questioned by a passerby, they conceal their true nature,
moving in step with others, appearing as ordinary mortals—
how could one discern them? How could one ever recognize them?

Only those like **Zi Jin**, who rode his white crane,
or the **Yellow Emperor**, who was startled by the red dragon,
or those with scaled bodies like serpents,
or those clad in golden carriages with feathered robes—
unless one’s vision is piercing, one cannot witness their deeds;
unless one’s hearing is profound, one cannot grasp their words.
Since the vulgar cannot see or hear, they multiply their slanders—
thus the **True Persons** grow ever more reclusive.

What common folk cherish, the **Noble Ones** hold in contempt.
What common folk despise, the **Perfect Ones** value most.
Even great scholars and accomplished men
do not wish to mingle in the dust of the world.
How much more so the **Divine Women** and **True Persons**,
who rush not into human affairs!

The vulgar will find fault—
how else could they err so greatly?

Though mortal eyes may perceive a hundred paces,
they cannot see clearly—
yet they claim what they see exists and what they do not see does not.
But how many unseen things truly exist in the world?

It is like using a ladle to measure the sea and declaring the waters exhausted—
how deluded they are!

If **True Persons** are unseen, it does not mean they do not exist.
Nor can one seek what cannot be sought by mere presence.

Those who grasp the **Law** need not await the **True Persons**.
One who knows the **Law** knows the oral **formulas** and receives them.

I, your humble subject, have opened **Master Qiu’s** transmission of the *Spring and Autumn Annals*,
and those who study the **scriptures** know that praise and blame lie in a single character.
**Master Kong’s** elucidation of the *Zhou Yi* shows that those who observe the **trigrams**
know that fortune and misfortune rest in a single symbol.
Even the **Confucian classics** cannot be fully understood without the **Law**—
how much more so the **Dao of Immortality** and the divine elixir,
which cannot be exhausted by mere scriptural study!

Thus the **Yellow Emperor** ascended **Kongtong** to seek the **Dao of Nature**,
and crossed **Wangwu** to obtain the **scriptures on elixir refinement**,
recording them in the *Plan of the Methods* and passing them down through oral **formulas**.
The **formulas** vanish with speech, the methods do not follow the scriptures.
Thus, though many seek, few attain—
though rare, the **Dao** is never entirely lost to humanity.

Once the **Law** is obtained by one, the body is no longer that of a common man.
The **Supreme Sage**, mindful of future generations who are easy to teach and trust,
causes them to reflect and attain it themselves,
freeing them from the calamities of death.

The vulgar do not believe, calling it empty words—
this is how the **True Persons** are slandered by those who defame the ancient sages.

Thus, to refine the divine elixir,
one must never let the unbelieving know of it—
for if they do, the medicine will fail.
This is a great taboo, not a minor restriction.

All such failures stem from not possessing the true **formulas**,
and thus the transformations cannot be completed.
Once the attempt is made and fails, slander arises.

It is like a farmer whose crops fail due to drought or flood,
yet he declares farming impossible.
But when the rains come and the grains grow,
he calls it a miracle—
just as the **scriptures** and **formulas**, if true, will yield the divine elixir.

The **formulas** have two forms:
One is the **written formula**, which can be transmitted in ink and paper.
The other is the **oral formula**, which cannot be spoken aloud.

Thus the *Yijing* says:
*"The written word does not exhaust speech,
and speech does not exhaust meaning."*

One’s conduct and practice of the **Dao** can be fully transmitted,
but the transformations of **yin-yang** cannot be articulated in words.

**Cinnabar** is naturally red, yet when refined, it becomes **mercury**.
**Mercury** is pure white, yet when refined again, it turns into elixir.
Those with shallow understanding cannot fathom this.

It is like burning **barite** to make it golden,
or turning **white lead** into fire-like brilliance—
those who claim no such **Dao** exists
are no better than the vulgar for their lack of pursuit.

The vulgar fear failure, dreading to be laughed at by common men.
They do not realize that if they succeed,
the wise will scorn them—
all because they did not obtain the true **scriptures** and **formulas**.

If transmitted to the wrong person, it brings blame and calamity.
Thus, the **Dao** is concealed and cannot be heard.

Therefore, **Ge Hong** said:
*"Within a single age, no more than two or three may attain it.*
*And again: Within the eight extremes of the world, how few will truly know it.*
*Secret formulas are difficult to hear, and those who obtain them are few.*
*They must first take an oath before transmission can occur.*
*Countless methods exist for the elixir of immortal life, yet without this formula, none can succeed.*

*The **Dao** is supremely secret—gold cannot buy its transmission.*
*If one transmits, they must first impart it orally from the original scripture,*
*never revealing it all at once.*
*The oath is sworn upon the **Alliance Scripture**, using eight *liang* of yellow gold,
forty *chi* of yellow cloth, eight *liang* of white silver,
and forty *chi* of white silk as tokens of faith,
with a limit of transmitting to only one person within a hundred years,
sealing the oath with blood.
*If later, one betrays or leaks this transmission to an unworthy disciple,*
*the Celestial Emperor will condemn them,*
*and they shall forever be barred from the Mysterious Path.*
*The Lord of the Great Mysterious will cause the oathbreaker’s heart to falter and mind to stray,*
*their studies ruined, their work undone.*
*The Grand Unity’s Registrar and the Three Heavens’ Commanders will record their transgressions,*
*and they shall be punished in the Great Mysterious Capital.*
*This is the **Dao** of the **Great Clarity’s** elixirs,
as revealed by **Zhang Daoling’s** secret formulas."*

**Hu Gangzi** said:
*"In my youth, I longed for the **Dao** of longevity.
For decades, I endured hunger, cold, and hardship,
traveling far and near, yet found no one who possessed it.
My resolve never wavered, and my dedication only deepened.
The **Great Ultimate** moved by my sincerity
and thus bestowed this formula upon me in the **Wuchang Valley**.
When I followed it faithfully, nothing failed.
From that moment, my **Dao** began.
I have kept it sealed in a jade case,
hidden in a sacred mountain.
If any common person obtains this formula,
whether wise or foolish, if they practice it with precision and devotion,
they shall surely attain the **Dao**."*

**Ge Hong** said:
*"Though I was born in the late age, I admired the ancient ways.
For over eighty years, I collected **Daoist** scriptures,
and though I heard of this formula, my eyes had never seen it.
I sought it relentlessly until my teacher, **Zheng Jun**,
finally transmitted it to me.
Upon receiving it, I purified my mind with fasting and meditation,
and after a hundred days of strict observance,
whatever I undertook succeeded.
I first transformed my breath into **Pure Qi**,
then consumed the **Five Spirit Springs** elixir,
and afterward mastered the **Method of Immortality**.
Only then did I dare to verify its truth—
now, my **Dao** skills are at my command.
If anyone else obtains this formula,
they must keep it in their heart and never speak of it lightly,
lest they reveal it to those unworthy of trust.
To do so would invite disaster—
the gods will not protect them,
and their work will fail.
I now solemnly warn future generations:
*Do not transmit this **Dao** recklessly.*
*This is the core secret passed down through the ages,*
*valued for its essence, not for widespread knowledge.*
*The method of transmission is found in the **Powder Formula**,
which is the **Secret of the Mysterious Pearl**."*

**Hu Gangzi** said:
*"The **Five Divine Metals’ Powder** is not merely for longevity.
Applied to the body, it repels common ailments and wards off all calamities.
This method originates from the **Jade Emperor’s** hidden scriptures,
beyond the reach of the vulgar.
Only those born with the **Dao’s** lineage can ever see it.
I, following the ancient hidden formulas,
now reveal it to future sages.
If one obtains this formula,
they must receive it through proper transmission—
do not lightly impart it to the unworthy.
If they do not follow the correct method,
their work will fail,
and even after ten thousand *kalpas* of practice,
they shall never attain the **Dao**.
The **Powder Diagram** states:
*‘Transmission must not be taken lightly.’*

*The day of transmission must be chosen on a **King-relative day**,
with a fasting altar erected.
Teacher and disciple stand before it,
burning precious incense day and night,
praying to the **Celestial Sovereign** for permission,
declaring their devotion to the **Dao** of longevity.
They recite:
‘For countless *kalpas*, I have cherished the **Dao** of immortality.
Now, through the mercy of my teacher,
I am permitted to receive this formula.
I dare not accept it lightly—
I humbly petition the **Celestial Sovereign** and my teacher,
begging for the transmission of the **Divine Gold Elixir** and the oral formulas and diagrams.
I swear by blood and cast a golden ring into flowing water,
pledging to uphold this method faithfully.
If one does not follow this transmission,
teacher and disciple alike will fail in their work.
This is the formula within the **Powder Diagram**.’*

**Hu Qiu Master** transmitted to **Ge Xian Gong**:
*"Your fate is aligned with the **Dao**—your name is recorded among the immortals.
I now bestow upon you the **Ten-Thousand-Gold Formula** and the methods of **Dao** cultivation.
Follow them precisely.
If you transmit this further,
only those who dwell in secluded mountains,
untainted by worldly desires,
shall be entrusted with it—
swear by blood and cast a golden ring,
erecting an altar to seal this oath.
Never transmit it recklessly.
To betray it to the unworthy will sever your name from the **Dao’s** records,
thin your virtue, and bring ruin to your descendants.
Beware—do not transmit it lightly.
This is the **Ten-Thousand-Gold Formula**."*

**The Scholar’s Annotation**:
*"The **Five Metals**, **Three Mercuries**, **Nine Leads**, and **Eight Stones** are all toxic.
Without the ancient formulas,
even if one claims newfound knowledge and transmits a few dozen phrases,
the result will be meaningless.
Thus, **Hu Gangzi** warned:
*The **Five Metals** are all fire-toxic.
If their poison is not refined into powder,
even if they transform into divine elixirs,
the lingering toxicity will, in time,
kill those who consume them if they violate even minor prohibitions.*

*Therefore, the complete formulas—including diagrams, methods of subjugating poisons,
and the powder-making process—are recorded here
to guide future practitioners.*

*The **Huzi Ten-Thousand-Gold Formula**,
*The **Five Metals Powder Diagram Formula**,
*The **Hidden Pearl Secret**,
*The **Zhang Tian Shi’s Oral Formula**—
these four formulas are treasures of the ancients.
Even if one encounters a single scroll of them,
they will still fail to grasp their true beginning and end."*

The text is garbled and confused,
asking for the inclusion of all methods.
Even if common folk were to know them all,
they would still fail to understand their proper use—
thus, the **Huzi Ten-Thousand-Gold Formula** is solemnly passed down through countless ages.

**Receiving the Oral Formula and Ritual Method:**
First, lay out the ritual implements,
and arrange the seat properly.
Take a white silk cloth four *chi* five *cun* in size as a base,
a measure of clear wine—one *dou*—
and seven slices of dried deer meat, or of beef or mutton,
each slice three *cun* square.
Place seven wine cups on a tray or table before you,
and set the meat slices behind each cup.
Place a token of faith to the left of the wine cups.

Burn incense and kneel respectfully, saying:
*"With utmost reverence, I invite the Sovereign of the Jade Court of Supreme Clarity,
the Lord of the Supreme Dao,
the Lord of the Great Constellation Emperor,*
*the Nine Elders of the Supreme Mysterious Celestial Capital,*
*and the Divine Lord of the Supreme Unity, who records and governs fate.*

*Descend to bestow upon this humble person of [certain] prefecture and [certain] district,*
*[certain] surname and given name,*
*and allow me to partake of your teachings.*

*[Alternative reading:] Partake of the incense offering.*
*Though I am but a mortal of low understanding,*
*I have long harbored the Dao’s verdant essence.*
*Now, by the grace of my master,*
*I have received the Great Formula,*
*—which I have kept secret in my heart,*
*without ever revealing it.*

*Though I know the heavenly prohibitions are most grave,*
*I cannot allow the Dao’s sacred path to remain forever concealed.*
*Now, here is [certain] surname and given name,*
*though dwelling among the vulgar,*
*whose heart reveres the Dao’s gate.*
*He does not prize gold and jade,*
*nor does he seek worldly glory and splendor.*
*He aspires only to the Mysterious Way,*
*and yearns to ascend the Purple Clouds."*

「故臧削自身，以備信物。
Thus, I have disciplined my body and purified my essence to prepare for the sacred substances.

诣臣某請受大訣，某不敢自專，輒敢啟白，唯願照知。
I, [certain] surname and given name, humbly seek to receive the Great Formula, yet I dare not keep it to myself—so I boldly present it, hoping only that you may recognize its truth.

石照明為之訖，乃再拜，上香酒三。
When the [ritual] of Stone Illumination is complete, I bow again and offer three libations of wine and incense.

上香酒訖，乃曰：勞屈玄尊，來臨下土，枉蒙降顧，心喜意悅，當聽某所陳，慈恩相欲，君以醉饱。
After offering the wine and incense, I say: *"I am honored by your labor, O Revered Daoist Master, to descend and visit this mortal realm. Though I am unworthy of your grace, my heart rejoices and my spirit is delighted. I shall now present my humble words—may your compassionate kindness accept them, and may you be sated by my devotion."*

持其酒食，請收餘福，見物永書。
I hold forth the wine and food, praying that you may gather the remaining blessings and forever inscribe this offering in your sacred records.

訖，乃再還，取酒脯，共所受人飲食之，勿與他人食。
When done, I return once more, take the wine and preserved meat, and share them with those who have received [the teachings], ensuring no others partake.

黄帝九鼎神丹經訣卷之三竟
*[End of] The Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Formula, Volume Three.*

黄帝九鼎神丹經訣卷之四
*[Beginning of] The Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Formula, Volume Four.*
*On Warding Off Malevolent Spirits, Guarding the Spirit, and Preserving the Body.*

臣按：凡學長生，須事神丹。
I, your humble servant, observe: *"To study longevity and transcendence, one must attend to the Divine Elixir.*

若不得金丹大藥，而但能饵草木之藥者，可以赊死，不得仙也。
If one cannot obtain the Golden Elixir, the Great Medicine, but merely ingests herbal remedies, one may only delay death—not attain transcendence.*

或但服藥，而不得房中之要，則終無久生之理矣。
Or if one takes only the medicine but does not grasp the essentials of the Chamber of Vitality [房中術], then one can never achieve lasting life.

或曉帶神符行禁，加思神守真一，則止可內疾不起，風濕不犯。
Some may know how to wear talismans, recite prohibitions, and meditate on the One True Qi, yet they can only prevent internal ailments from worsening and ward off wind-dampness [風濕].

若卒有惡鬼強邪，山精水毒害之，則便死也。
But if malevolent spirits, fierce demons, or mountain and water poisons assail them, they shall perish.

或不得入山，令山神為之作禍，則妖魅試人，猛獸傷之，蛇蝗螫之矣。
Or if one cannot enter the mountains, the mountain gods may bring misfortune—then demons will tempt them, fierce beasts will harm them, and serpents or locusts will sting them.

臣按：房中陰陽之道，高可以愈小疾，次可以免虛損。
I, your humble servant, further observe: *"The Way of Yin-Yang in the Chamber of Vitality is profound—at its highest, it can cure minor ailments; at its lesser, it can prevent depletion of vital essence.*

必不能移災解罪，去禍召福，安身全神，長生久視者也。
Yet it cannot truly avert disaster, absolve sins, banish calamity, summon blessings, ensure bodily safety, or preserve the spirit for eternal life and prolonged vision.

人問謂黃帝以千二百女升仙，便以黃帝單以此事長生也。
Some ask why the Yellow Emperor ascended with twelve hundred women, and thus assume that his transcendence depended solely on this act.

而不知黃帝於荊山之下，鼎湖之上，飛九鼎神丹成，乃乘龍登天也。
Yet they do not know that beneath the Jing Mountains and above the Cauldron Lakes, the Yellow Emperor refined the Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir and ascended to the heavens upon a dragon.

黃帝自可有千二百女耳，而非得仙之所由也。
The Yellow Emperor could indeed have twelve hundred women, but this was not the means by which he attained transcendence.

凡養性之保命者，雖服千味之藥，三牲之膳，而不知房中之要者，亦無所益。
Those who seek to nourish their nature and preserve their lives, even if they consume a thousand flavors of medicines and the three sacrificial meats [三牲], yet do not understand the essentials of the Chamber of Vitality, gain no true benefit.

若縱情肆欲，不知能節宣，則伐命本也。
If one indulges in unrestrained desires, failing to know moderation and release, they harm the very root of their life force.

是玄素喻之水火，水火殺人，又能生人，在於用也。
This is like the interplay of water and fire in the Mysterious and Subtle Way—water and fire can both kill and sustain life, depending on how they are employed.

明自古合作神丹，必依名山。
From ancient times, the refining of the Divine Elixir has always depended on sacred mountains.

臣按：昔者黃帝受丹經於王屋，訪至道於崆峒，然后於刑山之下，鼎湖之上，飛化九轉。
I, your humble servant, note: *"In ancient times, the Yellow Emperor received the Elixir Formula from the Rong House [王屋], sought the Supreme Way at the Kunlun Peaks [崆峒], and then beneath the Xing Mountains and above the Cauldron Lakes, he ascended through nine transformations.*

道成仙去。
Thus, his Way was perfected, and he departed as a transcendent.

又昔之左元放，於天柱山中，精思而感神人，授之以金丹仙經。
And in the past, Left Primordial [左元放] in the Tianzhu Mountains concentrated his thoughts and was visited by a divine person, who taught him the Golden Elixir Transcendent Formula.

會漢末大亂，不遑合作，而避地江束，志造名山，以修此道。
When the chaos of the late Han Dynasty arose, he could not attend to refining the elixir, so he fled to the Jiang Bundle region [江束] and resolved to construct a sacred mountain to cultivate this Way.

乃以《九鼎神丹經》等，授弟子葛仙公。
Thus, he passed on the *Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Formula* and other teachings to his disciple, Ge Xian Gong [葛仙公].

又以其法，授弟子鄭君。
And he also taught his methods to his disciple, Zheng Jun [鄭君].

鄭君家貧，無以買藥。
Zheng Jun was poor and lacked the means to purchase medicines.

而葛洪者，鄭君之弟子，親事勤苦矣。
Yet Ge Hong, Zheng Jun’s disciple, was diligent and labored earnestly in his service.

鄭君乃於馬迩山中立壇，盟授洪丹經，並具諸口訣，訣不書也。
Zheng Jun then established an altar in the Maqi Mountains and solemnly transmitted the Elixir Formula to Hong, along with all the oral incantations—though these incantations were not recorded in writing.

洪得此道二十餘年，資無擔石，無以為之始。
Hong possessed this Way for over twenty years, yet his resources were meager—he could not even begin to refine the elixir.

鄭君謂洪日：吾承先師左君之誡曰：諸小山中，不可居作金及神丹也。
Zheng Jun told Hong: *"I have inherited my master Left Primordial’s warning, which states: ‘In minor mountains, one must not dwell to forge gold or refine the Divine Elixir.’*

且小山之中，無有正神，皆是木之精，千歲老物，血食之鬼，此輩皆是邪氣，不念為人修道作福，但欲於祸人也。
Moreover, within minor mountains, there are no true deities—only the spirits of wood, ancient trees, and blood-feeding ghosts. These beings are filled with malevolent qi and do not consider aiding mortals in cultivating the Way or bringing blessings; they only wish to harm them.

夫齋潔之士，雖以術數辟身，而鬼魅或能壞人藥也。
Even the most ascetic and pure among us, though they may use talismans and prohibitions to ward off spirits, may still have their medicines spoiled by malevolent ghosts and demons.

今合醫家佳藥好膏，皆尚不欲令鵷犬，及婦人小兒等見之。
Now, when combining the finest medicines and ointments from the physicians’ arts, one must not allow even dogs and parrots—or women and children—to see them.

如藥被見者，用便不驗。
If the medicines are seen by such beings, their efficacy will be lost.

又染彩物者，遇惡目見之，皆失其色也。
Furthermore, if colored substances are exposed to evil gazes, they will lose their potency.

配神仙長生之大藥乎。
How much more so when refining the Great Medicine for transcendence and longevity!

以古之道士，合作神藥，必入名山無人之地，終不止於小小凡山中，正为此也。」

Moreover, according to the Daoist scriptures, the mountains where one may refine transcendental medicines through profound contemplation include **Huàshān (華山)**, **Tàishān (泰山)**, **Huòshān (霍山)**, **Héngshān (恒山)**, **Sōnggāoshān (嵩高山)**, **Shàoshì (少室)**, **Tàibái (太白)**, and **Zōngnán (終南)**.

Within these mountains reside **orthodox deities (正神)**, where **Earthly Immortals (地仙)** dwell, and **lingzhi (芝草)** grows—capable of warding off great calamities and floods, not merely suitable for refining medicines. If a practitioner of the Dao ascends them, the mountain deities will surely bestow blessings upon them, ensuring the medicines are perfected.

The scholar reflects: The true nature of Heaven and Earth, the auspicious and inauspicious interplay of **Yin and Yang (阴阳)**, is indeed difficult to discern, yet it cannot be said that such forces do not exist. Thus, the Yellow Emperor and the Grand Historian all placed their trust in them.

Additionally, the **classics and traditions (经传)** speak of **political cycles (政历)** and the **auspicious timing of firmness and softness (明时刚柔之日)**, where only favorable days yield success, a principle long established.

Therefore, sovereigns appoint the **Grand Historian (太史官)**, bestow titles and honors upon him, and when conducting rites at ancestral temples or **sacrificial offerings to Heaven and Earth (郊祀)**, they carefully select the most propitious days. Yet, those who claim to be virtuous or ordinary, who boast of transcending the mundane, would shamefully neglect such auspicious days in their movements and dwellings—are they not blinded by their own views?
