Therefore, *Hújiāngzǐ* established that all five types of gold possess poison; if not fully refined to remove the poison and made into powder, even if one pretends to achieve transformation and concocts the *Great Elixir of the Divine Dan*, its lingering toxicity will, upon prolonged ingestion or slight violation of prohibitions, inevitably kill. Hence, *Hújiāngzǐ* left behind records on hammered gold, and now we extract their essentials, listing them as follows:

Hammered gold may be found either in water or within mountains. That found in water or on mountainous terrain beneath water resembles *millet husks*, *millet grains*, *dates*, or *glutinous rice grains*, buried one *cùn* (寸) to seven *cùn* deep in sand, stone, or earth—this is the *gold of the north-south flowing waters*, located on the eastern bank. Buried five *cùn* to nine *cùn* deep, this is called the *gold of the east-west flowing waters*, found on the southern bank and produced—all of which are the finest, superior gold.

That found in mountains is uniformly round, with veins facing the sun, buried nine *chǐ* (尺) to ninety *chǐ* deep in mixed sand, stone, and earth, displaying a red-yellow hue, fine and smooth, heavy and dense. When broken, it does not shatter; when melted by fire, it turns white like silver. After being stirred with medicines and subjected to the *Eight Winds* (八风) furnace with stone-washing, this is called the *gold of the east-west mountains*. In the northern shaded regions, it grows with water and sand intermingled, buried in stone and earth—its depth varying as above. With veins facing the sun, buried seven *chǐ* deep, its form and quality resemble the previous, and this is called the *gold of the south-north mountains*. That found in the western shaded regions is called the *second-grade gold*. It is then stirred white and subjected to the *Eight Winds* furnace with stone-washing, refined as before.

If hammered gold appears in water or on mountainous terrain but is exposed on the surface, not buried in the *yin-yang* (阴阳) regions of the west, south, or north, and has sharp edges—whether large or small—with a greenish-yellow hue, it is all of *iron nature*, resembling gold yet unfit for use.

**Method for Refining Water-Sourced Hammered Gold:**
Use sweet clay to fashion a crucible, dry it with smoke, and place pinewood charcoal in the furnace. Then, immerse the hammered gold in the crucible and ignite the furnace fiercely. Next, add salt powder and stir it in. When fully melted, use a *jīng* (荆) branch to skim away impurities. Pour out the molten gold and repeatedly stir in salt. Skim away all impurities until the grease and membrane are exhausted. Hammer and break it, then filter with iron vinegar to make it into fine shavings. Mix with equal parts cow dung ash and salt, and place it back in the furnace with cow dung fire. Temper it in sand and repeatedly melt and hammer until it becomes soft. Then, apply a coating of equal parts *huángfán* (黄矾) stone and *Hútónglǜ* (胡同律), melt it with fire until red, and cease. Repeat the burning four or five times until it becomes superior red gold. Apply the remaining medicine.

Other methods, though varied, are all fallacious—deceiving only the ears. If one seeks to make thin gold sheets or gold paste for ornamentation, melt one *jīn* (斤) of gold with equal parts *stone sulfur* (石硫黄) and *copper acetate* (曾青), each one *liǎng* (两), in a crucible and stir. It will then soften and be malleable as desired. If the impurities persist even after one round of tempering with cow dung ash, repeat the process until all impurities are removed.

**Subsequent Method for Tempering with Tin:**
Use equal parts *huángfán* (黄矾) stone, *Hútónglǜ* (胡同律), and salt, mixed with vinegar to form a paste. If these are unavailable, simply melt the gold from the mountains and refine it.

**Method for Hammered Gold:**
Take two *liǎng* each of *gold essence* (金精), *stone gall* (石胆), *cinnabar* (朱砂), *realgar* (雄黄), *stone sulfur* (石硫黄), *raw saltpeter* (朴硝), *calcined sand* (炮砂), and *white alum* (白矾), and one *liǎng* of *qílín scales* (麒鳞竭). Grind the *qílín scales* into powder, soak them in vinegar within porcelain, and place them in a furnace with chaff fire—do not let them boil, only simmer until they are decomposed, from *Chén* (辰) hour to *Wǔ* (未) hour. Remove and mix with five *liǎng* each of *honey myrobalan* (蜜陀僧) and *purple quartz* (紫石英), and one *jīn* of salt.

Grind all twelve medicinal substances into powder. In a separate copper vessel, melt eight *liǎng* of *mercury* (水银) with vinegar, applying a small, intense fire beneath. In another iron vessel, melt tin and pour it into the mercury, where they will combine harmoniously. When the vinegar is nearly exhausted, add another *dǒu* (斗) of it. Repeat this until two *dǒu* of vinegar have been used. Then, take all the medicines, place them in a porcelain vessel, and mix them simultaneously with the mercury to form the elixir in half a day.

Grind the fine hammered gold into fragments, resembling *glutinous rice grains*. Combine ten *jīn* of hammered gold with two *liǎng* of medicine and ten *liǎng* of *huángfán* (黄矾) stone powder, and place them in the *Eight Winds* furnace with *chengliǔ* (程柳) wood charcoal. Stir both hard and soft gold evenly, ensuring the fire penetrates fully, until its force is exhausted. If the gold is not fully refined, subject it to another round in the furnace—there will be none that fail to refine. Use fine sand in a basin to collect the refined gold, resembling *millet husks* or *fine sugar crystals*, which must be kept separate from the gold.»

「Take one *dòu* of cow dung ash, half a *shēng* of salt powder, and two *liǎng* of refined gold sand, mix them thoroughly, and combine with *xuánjīng* water to form a paste like a chicken egg. Dry it by fumigation, then return it to the cow dung fire. If it is well-done, stop after one round. If not, repeat the process until it is ready before consumption.

To further refine it, take the residue from the crucible, melt it in a basin, pour it into a thin layer of fat membrane, and flatten it. Mix equal parts of *hútónglǜ* (胡同律) and *huángfán* stone powder with vinegar to form a thin paste, apply it, and burn until the color emerges like the method for *shuǐjīn* (水金). This yields the finest gold.

For coating objects with thin gold paste, follow the previous method: for every *jīn* of gold, use one *liǎng* each of *huángfán* and *céngqīng* (曾青), melt and stir them in a crucible until they become pliable and malleable for use.

If the gold lacks sharp edges (*wúlěngjiǎo* 無楞角), add one *liǎng* of the previous medicine and ten *liǎng* of *huángfán* stone powder for every ten *jīn* of gold. If the gold is not genuine, forcing its refinement is merely wasted effort.

When the medicinal *qi* is exhausted and the *xīnghuà* (星化) essence dissipates, it becomes iron—regrettably, not a single *zhū* (铢) remains. Only true substances yield results.

If *qílín* (麒麟) scales are unavailable in the medicinal division, substitute them with *zǐjīn* (紫金). This also works.

---
**Method for the Eight Winds Furnace (*Bāfēng Wòlú* 八风沃炉) and Refining Tin Ash**

First, refine lead and tin twenty times in a sweet clay crucible. Use three *jīn* of refined tin in a cast-iron pot, melt it until it glows red and boils, then add one *jīn* of crushed gold-tin mixture. Skim off the dross and pour out the liquid.

Prepare fully charred firewood ash. Build a square furnace with clay bricks, lining it with refined ash as a mold. Place the gold-tin mixture in the center, cover it with an iron lid, and arrange hard charcoal above. Punch a hole in the furnace top and a small vent at the front. After a short time, the tin and gold will separate—take the gold, which resembles silver. Mix it with refined *qīhuáng* (雌黄) and good wine, boil it in a copper vessel to restore its original nature. If not fully refined, flatten it, refine it again, and extract the color as before.

Once the true tin is refined, place it on the iron lid, mix equal parts of *hútónglǜ*, *huángfán* stone, and salt with vinegar into a paste, and coat the tin ingot. Surround it with cow dung fire on all sides until the tin is fully consumed, leaving only gold. Transfer the gold to a cast-iron pan, mix it with *huángfán* stone and water, boil it for half a day, then melt and cast it into an ingot.

The dross from the furnace must also be refined using the same method and proportions.

---
**Purification of Tin by Submersion (*Xī Tóu Niúzhī* 锡投牛脂) Method**
Immerse tin in cow fat, red soil, then in *pútāo* (蒲挑) juice and mustard seed broth, followed by pear tea ash liquid, black *xǐ* (盥) rock wine, and *làngyánzi* (浪岩子) barley wine—each immersion seven times yields refined tin.

---
**Method for *Chìyán* (赤盐, Red Salt)**
Grind one *jīn* of *huángfán* stone and eight *liǎng* of rock salt into powder, melt them in an iron vessel until the color turns fully red. Let it cool to form *chìxǐ* (赤盥), then grind it into powder for use.

---
**Huzi’s Refining Method**
The medicinal division requires *jīnjīng* (金精), *céngqīng*, *zhūshā* (朱砂), and *xiónghuáng* (雄黄). If not fully refined, using them wastes thousands of *jīn* without gaining even a fraction of true gold. *Shídǎn* (石胆) must also be refined to extract its essence.

For *jīnjīng* and *céngqīng*, place one substance in a porcelain vessel, soak it in three cycles of *zuǒwèi* (左味) for 200 days, then dry and grind it finely for use.

For *zhūshā* and *xiónghuáng*, soak them in porcelain with good spring wine for 100 days, dry, and grind finely for use.

---
**Refining *Shídǎn* to Extract Its Essence**
Build two square clay furnaces, two *chǐ* apart, each lined with fine clay and vented on the sides. Place a copper basin in one furnace, seal it tightly with clay. In the other, burn *shídǎn* until its essence vaporizes and condenses into the copper basin. Once cooled, open the furnace and use the refined essence in any elixir—it enhances all medicines.

---
**Hujiangzi’s Six Gold Furnace Methods**
There are six furnace methods for refining gold, depending on its nature and quantity. Only one method is needed—no need to perform all, as that wastes effort. The two most effective methods are illustrated as before.

---
**Extracting Silver from Ore**
If the silver is already bright white, roast it with *bái fán* (白矾) and *shípào* (石炮) powder to refine it. If it remains impure, mix one *jīn* of crude silver with one *jīn* of refined lead, then filter the ash to produce superior white silver.

---
**Mold for Ash Refining (*Huīzhú* 灰逐) in a Clay Furnace**
Build a clay furnace chamber three *chǐ* high, with adjustable length. Inside, create a mold to hold the refined ash, ensuring it is fully compacted and neither too wet nor too dry. Press the ash firmly, then carve the desired shape with a knife. Sprinkle a thin layer of salt powder over the ash where the metal will flow, cover it with yellow clay, and arrange charcoal above. Seal the furnace with clay, leaving ventilation holes at the top and sides. Poke small holes at intervals to monitor progress with an iron hook, skimming off dross as it rises.

Once the fire penetrates, the tin and gold will boil and swirl, separating completely. When the tin is fully consumed and the silver stops moving, a purple-green luster emerges. Strike the surface lightly with a rod, dampen it with water, and the silver will solidify. Lift the "dragon head" mold, use an iron spoon to collect the silver—this is called *lóngtóu bái yín* (龙头白银, Dragon-Head White Silver).

---
**Clay Furnace Mold and Tin Dross Refining Method**
Hammer an iron mold to the desired size, with staggered holes (each fitting an arrow) to prevent clay leakage. Shape the mold like a tortoise shell, line it with refined ash, and compress it evenly. Cover with salt powder, arrange the ash, and monitor as before. Follow the same refining steps.

「Only when the fire beneath the iron mold is made fierce does the tin descend rapidly and separate. Next is the method for refining tin dross from the mold:

Hu Gāngzǐ says: When refining silver, there are three methods. First, gauge the amount of dross and make one furnace accordingly—this avoids unnecessary effort. Now, I present the two most essential methods, setting the mold as before.

**Method for expelling tin from the mold’s center:**
After the silver is refined, quickly mix oil and sulfur powder, pour the fat through the silver-refining holes into the mold’s center. When flames rise, use an iron rod to scrape beneath the dross holes, stirring vigorously within the mold. The tin will reemerge, flowing downward into clusters.

**Method for steaming and refining the dross within the mold:**
The refined silver dross must be steamed to remove its slippery residue, then hammered until thoroughly mellowed—this yields far more silver. If the dross is not refined well, the silver yield will be much less. If the mold cracks mid-process, the tin will spill out, and the silver will be lost. Thus, one must strike and refine it meticulously, using the finest charcoal ash from burned mulberry bark, which also works well.

**Method for refining silver with medicinals:**
Prepare the following:
- Raw realgar (雄黄) – 1 liang
- White quartz (白石英) – 1 liang
- Roasted sand (炮砂) – 1 liang
- Steamed *zhōngwǎn* stone (戎盥石胆) – 1 liang
- White alum (白矾) – 1 liang
- Green vitriol (青矾) – 10 liang

The secret is: For refining silver, it is specifically said to use raw realgar. If one follows the refining method for gold, which includes realgar, it must be roasted like cinnabar (丹砂). It is known that realgar lacks fixed properties—raw realgar produces a silver hue, while roasted realgar yields a golden one.

Grind the above seven medicinals into fine powder. Take four liang of mercury (水银) and two liang of tin (锡), place them in a small crucible. Pour vinegar over the mercury, apply intense fire beneath the tin, melt the tin in an iron vessel, and pour it into the mercury mixture. Boil with two *dòu* of vinegar until it is fully spent, then transfer it into a porcelain container. Mix all seven powders together at once, grinding them thoroughly until they harmonize.

When the tin in the mold’s center ceases to move and the purple-green luster (文园) appears, scatter this refined powder into the mold like dates. The tin must then become lively again, and the purple-green luster must vanish—this ensures rapid extraction of the tin.

**Refining gold and silver with charcoal:**
Gold requires charcoal from willow wood, pine, or *wú* wood, as well as dried cow dung—all must be firm and slightly damp in nature. When burned, they will refine the gold.

Only green wood charcoal, when dry, can be used directly for refining gold. When applied to the *lóngtóu* (Dragon-Head) furnace, the gold will flow out effortlessly, requiring minimal labor and yielding the most gold.

For silver, copper, and iron, use charcoal from hardwood. For tin, burning pine wood or hardwood charcoal also works.

**Method for producing a silver-white medicinal:**
Take white plums (白梅子) and black plums (乌梅子) from Sichuan, steam them until tender in a copper vessel. Use one *dòu* of water, two *shēng* of plums, one *shēng* of vinegar, and one *shēng* of salt powder, boiling them together until thoroughly cooked. Take the refined silver, hammer it thin, heat it until red in the fire, and press it into the plum juice. The silver must be fully immersed in the juice.

Repeat the process—boil, heat, and immerse—for about half a day. The silver will become lustrous, and its surface will turn entirely white. If the fire is not adjusted properly, there is another method: mix roasted sand with water and immerse the silver directly—it will turn white.

**Softening the superior gold:**
To soften the superior gold (上金), dissolve it in *jīng* wine (荆酒) for ten days, allowing it to permeate thoroughly. In one day, it will become supple and smooth. If one prepares it as a gold elixir (金液), softening it first is even better.

**Refining gold method:**
Take unused gold, dissolve it in sweet wine, and immerse it for three hundred cycles. It will no longer boil, and when held, it will ooze between the fingers—this is called refined gold. Only those who can meticulously refine their elixirs will attain *Tàiqīng* (太清, Supreme Clarity).

The refining of silver is the same. With this softened substance, hammer it thin, prepare it as a gold elixir, and apply it with great care.

**Refining gold and silver elixirs:**
Dissolve newly refined gold and silver in clear wine, pure fermented wine, or genuine honey, for two hundred cycles. They will become supple and smooth, and when held, they will ooze between the fingers. Even if steeped for many days, they remain suitable for elixirs.

Dissolve and immerse them in guess oil (猜脂) for two hundred cycles—they will also form supple gold. Hammer it thin, cut it finely, and mix it with non-toxic mercury to form a paste.

For every one liang of gold, mix with six liang of mercury, adding half a small bowl of cooked barley. Grind them together in an iron mortar with a pestle until finely pulverized. When the mixture is sufficiently refined, pour it into a basin and remove the stones with water and sand. Examine it carefully, ensuring no gold is lost with the stones.

Wrap the paste in two layers of cloth and twist to remove half the mercury. Take the remaining mercury paste, place it in a porcelain container, and gradually add white salt powder. Grind it until it breaks apart, adding salt until it reaches about half a small bowl, then stop grinding. Sift the residue, regrind it until fine, and then place it in an earthen pot, covering it with salt powder.

After half a day of steaming, the mercury will fully evaporate. When the salt is removed, the gold will naturally turn into powder.

Take one liang of this gold powder and mix it with five liang of refined cinnabar (丹砂). Choose cinnabar that is bright and translucent.

Pour vinegar over it, simmer with gentle fire, and continuously add vinegar to prevent it from running dry. Use an iron vessel—this process will take thirty-six days.

When refining is complete, grind it again with water, collect the fine particles, and mix them with date honey (枣膏) to form pills.

**Method for making date honey:**
Take three *shēng* of large, dried dates, add six *shēng* of water, and boil until the dates are thoroughly softened. Add another three *shēng* of water, boil until the mixture totals nine *shēng*, then strain out the dregs and clarify it until it reduces to three *shēng*.

Add six small bowls of refined lamb marrow (羊髓), simmer gently until it thickens like syrup—this is the date honey.

This honey can also be taken long-term, filling one’s body and enhancing beauty. Divide it into three portions, and take one portion every nine days.

Alternatively, mix this honey with the earlier medicinals, form pills the size of small beans, and take three pills daily for thirty days. This will eliminate cold and heat, allowing one to command spirits and deities.

Gold, once softened, loses its toxicity—even in small amounts, it is feared no longer.»

Silver also follows the method of softening gold. If it is inferior gold, take robust *jīng* root (荆根), boil it into a decoction, and ferment red glutinous rice into wine. Soak the gold in this wine, and it will dissolve.

If gold filings are soaked in it, and realgar (雄黄) is added to this wine, they will also dissolve. Why limit this to softening gold alone?

Another method: Take fine magnetite (磁石) that attracts iron, crush it, soak it in pure vinegar, then remove it and soak it again until it is thoroughly refined. Sift it through a fine sieve, then take the gold filings—still toxic when raw—and refine them. Place them in the palm, grind them, and they will dissolve instantly.

Drinking the elixir of this stone’s essence once, twice, or even three times—without hunger or thirst—grants longevity and eternal youth.

The scholar notes: According to the *Gold Powder and Gold Water* prescriptions, taking five *liǎng* or more ensures a lifespan equal to the heavens and earth. Yet, one must strictly abstain from conjugal relations and avoid meat. Cultivate the essence with disciplined practice—preferably in secluded mountains. This is valued by commoners, not by emperors.

How could it compare to the *Taiyi Golden Elixir* or the *Yellow Emperor’s Nine-Tripod Divine Pill*? The latter requires precise timing—when to ascend, when to pause—unhindered by family obligations or official duties.

*Conclusion of the Ninth Scroll of the Yellow Emperor’s Nine-Tripod Divine Pill Canon*
*Beginning of the Tenth Scroll of the Yellow Emperor’s Nine-Tripod Divine Pill Canon*

「Thus, the refined alchemy strictly regulates *yin* and *yang*, subduing and mastering the medicinal *qi*.

The scholar notes: Master Peng once said: "The sages of antiquity all relied on elixirs to preserve their bones and attain longevity. Later scholars, however, claim that elixirs rot the bones and shorten life—this is the difference between past and present. It stems from the purity and depth of ancient practice, while later generations grew decadent and superficial, failing to grasp the true methods. Though they may begin with a desire for life, they lack the perseverance to sustain it. Without first cultivating and refining the heart, how can one regulate the nature of the medicine?

Even if one follows ancient annotations and prescriptions, blending them together, the resulting concoction may resemble an elixir, yet its poison remains untouched. Taking it would lead to death—hence the saying, 'shortens life.'

The scholar further notes Master Peng’s words: 'Though one may hear of gold and cinnabar elixirs, if the fire and medicine are not first subdued and mastered, then the essence will scatter and vanish, leaving only dross. Where is the proof? Thus, one must first master the fire.'

Now, the scholar reveals the method: The divine elixir is the quintessence of superior stone medicines. For instance, when cinnabar is crushed, its radiance pierces the eyes—this is its essence. Like the Dao’s profound and mysterious depths, within it lies precision. Like its joyous and hazy brilliance, within it lies substance. It cannot be seized hastily nor sought leisurely. It seems both present and absent—haste brings no success, for its acquisition has its own method.

Compare this to milk fed to a cow: it becomes cheese, then clarified butter, and finally ghee through gradual transformation. Though it originates from milk, it is neither cheese nor clarified butter nor ghee at first. Yet one cannot say it is without these stages, nor can one say it is entirely absent. Skillful extraction yields them; clumsy attempts fail. The distinction between skill and clumsiness lies in the art of guiding the essence—urgency causes it to disperse, while haste without restraint leaves it unrefined. Once scattered, there is no way to retrieve it, unlike the essence of medicine, which can be recovered if lost. Hence, it is said: 'Only dross remains, no essence remains.' If the essence is lost, how can it be transmuted into the divine elixir?

**Method to Prevent Scattering in Alchemical Refinement**

When refining all stones, crush them like peas, or into fine grains like evening dew, or into powder like hemp seeds. Place them in a silk pouch within an iron pot, and immerse them in *jiǔ* (fermented liquor). When the liquor is infused, have someone carefully tend the fire—extinguish it immediately upon boiling, and keep the pot five inches above the heat. Ensure the fire is even, not lopsided, so that the medicinal *qi* rises straight and gently. If the fire is too fierce, the *qi* will scatter wildly; if too weak, the *qi* will stagnate. Maintain a moderate, balanced heat—like the gentle warmth of the human body—so as to adjust it properly.

Thus, the *Canon* states: 'All flying refinements must be moderate and warm, not so hot as to scald the hand. When the medicine turns white like snow, this is the nurturing method.' It is like the month of spring when the sun warms the earth: all things flourish, sprouting and growing in harmony. If one were to prolong the immersion like the *Yǔshuǐ* (Rainwater) season in a cold pool, or force excessive heat like a blazing fire in the *Qīngmíng* (Clear and Bright) season, the plants would either wither or burn. One does not straighten crooked branches by uprooting and replanting them; nor does one cleanse unclean roots by washing and reseeding them, for such actions sever the vital flow of life. Instead, the proper timing must be observed—like one who stokes the fire, then rides the heat to its peak. Those who dread cold plunge into boiling water to warm themselves both violate the natural rhythm of life and stray from the Dao of refinement and cultivation. The method is exhausted here.

The scholar has heard that Master Peng’s method involves regulating each medicine according to *yin* and *yang* principles, then combining them. Once the combination is complete, the elixir is formed—whether in large or small doses—all attain perfection. Taking it grants transcendence.

Those who seek the Great Dao and Great Elixir but fail to obtain this method will labor endlessly, waste vast wealth, and end as scattered bones.

The scholar notes: The *Yì* (Classic of Changes) says: "Two females dwelling together is called *gé* (revolution), while *yáng* and *yīn* meeting is called *tài* (great harmony). Thus, heaven and earth intermingle in *yīnyūn* (misty vapors), and all things are transformed into purity. When male and female unite in essence, all things are born anew. The unfathomable interplay of *yin* and *yang* is called *shén* (divine), while their balanced alternation is called the Dao.

Thus, they can mold all substances, nurturing life within the cauldron. This is the divine function of creation and the marvelous power of *yin* and *yang*. The secret essence of the divine elixir shares this principle.

*Tàiyīn* (Great *yin*) is lead, while *Tàiyáng* (Great *yáng*) is cinnabar. These two substances interact to form the greatest medicine. The Nine-Tripod method, the Dao of longevity, and the fundamental principles of refinement all center on these two substances.

Hence, the *Song of the True Person* declares the Nine-Tripod as first among all, establishing the supreme status of external alchemy:

*"Father dwells on the Divine Mountain, Mother on the River,*
*Their origin lies in South Yue, also in Ba.*
*They emerge from Wuling, meeting at Changsha,*
*With ancestors and kin in Yuzhang’s home.*
*A Daoist guides me to wander Five Hua,*
*Where Ziming pairs lead with vermilion powder.*
*Transformed, they yield countless black and yellow essences,*
*Like flowing pearls illuminating the inner chambers of the River.*
*Combined with the masculine *qi* of water and cinnabar,*
*They merge in harmony as one family.*
*Oysters and red stones keep them pure,*
*Frost and snow, violet hues, bloom like flowers.*
*When their natures resonate in balanced harmony,*
*At dusk, they stir—O’Zang, the finest.*
*Playful radiance, no fading brilliance,*
*Uniting *yin* and *yáng* without excess.*
*Two *qi* generate the child, with added sand,*
*Feathers swept, earthworm essence blended.*
*Whether a single grain or a pound—none is lacking,*
*Consumed with millet and sorghum, their essence ascends.*
*Sitting, observing heaven and earth from afar,*
*Suddenly crossing ten thousand *lǐ* to traverse rivers.*
*Riding the Dragon as horse, the Dragon as chariot,*
*Its light like the sun and moon—what more could one desire?*
*All celestial sages gather in reverence,*
*Spiritual tortoises paired in procession, turning at leisure.*
*Boya strums his zither, the Jade Maiden sings,*
*Her emerald waist sways in dance, their sorrowful harmonies blend.*
*By ingesting this elixir, the body attains perfection,*
*No malevolent *qi* arises, no illness prevails—*
*Thus, one achieves eternal youth, with no other means."*」

「This is the supreme utterance of the True Person. The *Húzǐ Gē* further states:
*"Grasses obtain yin and yang, their essence and qi remain forever verdant.
Stones obtain yin and yang, their essence and qi retain their form.
Heaven obtains yin and yang, their essence and qi perpetually generate.
Thus, all that transform the myriad things,
None fail to take yin and yang as their parents.*

The yang qi is Heaven, the yin essence is Earth.
Heaven’s qi is refined as spirit, Earth’s essence as treasure.
These two substances form the elixir—
Ingest it and attain longevity.

The five stones are:
*Dānshā* (cinnabar), the essence of the Great Intestine’s yang;
*Císhí* (magnetite), the essence of the Great Yin’s yang;
*Zēngqīng* (orpiment), the essence of the Minor Yang’s yang;
*Xiónghuáng* (realgar), the essence of the stone’s yang.
They absorb the true qi of yin and yang,
Align with the five directions’ true positions,
Mutually restraining, yet unstirred—
Refined and detoxified, thus granting immortality to those who consume them.

When refining *fúliàn* (mercury), one must use yang months, yang days, and yang hours.
If other methods are employed,
Even if the poison is not entirely exhausted,
Ask only for the three yangs—
Though minor techniques may be lost, the poison will be fully dispelled.

*Qiān gōng* (lead and mercury) are one—
The essence and qi of yin and yang.
If not refined at the three yangs,
The essence of the moon’s and sun’s yin qi
Cannot be controlled.
*Huángbái* (gold and silver) are the essence and qi of the Great Yang.
*Zuǒ wèi* (left flavor) is the morning yang’s vital fluid.
*Jīn zéi* (right flavor) is the evening yang’s sinews and marrow.
Using the three yangs’ flavors and qi
To govern lead and mercury—
It is infallible in eliminating poison.
The common folk do not understand this,
Mixing and consuming them recklessly—
It is fatal, indeed. One must be cautious.
Simply boiling them in wine
Only distances one further from the Dao.

All this pertains to the principle of yin and yang restraining each other.

**Taboos and Prohibitions in Refining Medicines**
The Classics say that when refining all medicinal stones,
One must observe strict fasting and abstinence,
Avoiding women, the six domestic animals, mourning, and childbirth.
According to my observation:
The True Person’s elixir of flight forbids fools, women, children,
Envious and deceitful individuals, and those prone to gossip.
For those who do not believe in the Dao,
Even if they witness it with their own eyes,
The divine medicine will not manifest.

Do not allow women, friends, or guests
To pass near the refining area.
Seek a secluded, quiet place—
A deep mountain cave or stone chamber—
Where no human voice or presence disturbs.
Once the divine medicine is perfected,
The entire household ascends to transcendence.

According to my observation:
The Yellow Emperor had one thousand two hundred women,
Yet even before his ascension,
At the foot of the Jing Mountains and above the Ding Lake,
He refined nine elixirs to completion,
Rode the Dragon and ascended to Heaven.
At that time, the furnace fires required human labor—
His attendants and servants—
Were they not women and close subjects?

Furthermore, in ancient times,
The Han Palace Attendant *Chéng Wěi* (程伟) was skilled in *Huángbái* (gold and silver) alchemy.
When he took a wife,
She came to know the marvels of the art.
*Wěi* would fan the charcoal to stoke the fire,
While the crucible contained *shuǐyín* (mercury).
He would press the tripod’s lid,
Yet the gold would not form.
His wife said:
*"I wish to attempt just one *liǎng* (两).
She took out her pouch’s medicine,
Added a small amount,
And in the time it takes to eat a meal,
The mercury transformed into silver."
*Wěi* was greatly startled and exclaimed:
*"The Dao is near you! Why did you not inform me sooner?"*
His wife replied:
*"Its attainment requires one with destiny."
Wěi employed every means to pressure her,
Demanding the secret method.
She said:
*"If you proclaim the Dao and align with its transmission,
Even if we meet on the road, I will pass it on.
But if you are not the right person—
One who speaks falsely while claiming sincerity—
Even if I were cut into pieces,
The method would never be revealed."*
Wěi persisted in threats,
And his wife, enraged, went mad,
Stripped naked, smeared herself with mud,
And died, her spirit ascending.

From this, it is evident:
A man who attains the Dao
Cannot succeed before a woman does.

Thus, *Xuánnǚ* (玄女), *Sùnǚ* (素女), *Qīngyāonǚ* (青腰女), and *Xīwángmǔ* (西王母)
Are all women who have ascended as immortals.

The Celestial True Person
Even employs *yùnǚ* (玉女) as attendants.

Hence, those called *yùnǚ* (玉女)
Are mortal women who, through elixir consumption,
Have attained transcendence.

Therefore, the Yellow Emperor’s *Nine Tripod Divine Elixir* states:
*"For those refining the divine elixir,
Who wish to obtain True and Pure (virtue),
With pleasing appearance and harmonious complexion,
Whose heart and body are devoted solely to the Dao,
Let them share the elixir with their master,
And sacrifice to her as the *Xuánnǚ* (玄女).*

To attain immortality,
One must share a single purpose with their master.
To transcend the world,
One must share a mutual covenant with their master."」

To seek ascension to Heaven,
One must first master the **Twenty-Four Virtues of the Sage**.

Together, they must recite the **Golden Scripture**,
Yet still the path to immortality remains unobtained.

Again, the scripture says:
*"Those refining the elixir must not exceed three in number.
Now, since the labor of distillation
Has yet not entered the **Divine Tripod**,
Therefore, the strict prohibitions are not yet enforced.*

The **breathing and condensing fire** must be regulated with precision.
If one is not of **upright heart and complete nature**,
Lacking **refined intention and keen insight**,
Speaking no idle words, acting no unworthy deeds,
Neither hasty nor sluggish,
Nor claiming false purity,
They shall not be entrusted with this task.

If one is a **condemned outcast**,
Whose six senses are impaired—
Deaf ears, blind eyes,
Or limbs crippled by pain or injury—
Though they may walk in **auspicious virtue**,
They are still unfit for this labor."

**Market Elixir Method**:
At **auspicious virtue grounds**,
Sit or stand in reverence—
Do not dispute rank with others,
Nor purchase goods from those clad in **mourning attire**.

On days of **auspicious virtue**,
Bathe on **child/rat and midnight/ox days**,
After seven days of fasting,
Then recite the **Heavenly Virtue Method**:
In the first month, **shen (申)**;
In the second month, **shen (申)** again—
To align with the **twelve celestial stems**.

For the **auspicious virtue method** of elixir purchase:
On **jia (甲) days**, virtue lies in **shen (申)**,
On **yi (乙) days**, virtue lies in **geng (庚)**,
And so forth in this manner.

**The Yellow Emperor’s Nine Tripod Divine Elixir Scripture** concludes its tenth volume,
And begins its eleventh volume.

**The Art of Refining Mercury for Longevity and Detoxification**

The method for **mercury (shuǐyín) longevity** and detoxification refinement:

The subject notes: In his later years, **Ge Hong** served as a disciple of **Zheng Yun**, while his fellow disciples all engaged in menial labor. Yet Ge Hong, weak and unable to endure hardship, could not contribute meaningfully—he only performed humble tasks like sweeping dust, holding candles, and copying old texts.

Zheng Yun said to Ge Hong: *"Reading books yields wisdom in every volume, but one must select the most refined teachings and apply them judiciously. There is no need to exhaust oneself memorizing everything, wasting time and energy. Once the **Golden Elixir (jīndān)** is perfected, these lesser tasks will no longer be needed."*

Yet the essence of the elixir lies in **mercury**. The subject notes: Among all **mercury**, the finest is the **Fuliang (涪陵) self-sufficient, unrestrained mercury** found in **Qingbai (青白) form** within the **Liu Sha (流沙)** waters. This mercury resembles tin, is exceedingly soft, and even dissolves when heated in **qi**. If such mercury cannot be obtained, refined **gold and silver** must be used instead—this is the best alternative. However, mercury derived from **cinnabar (zhūshā)** is also acceptable. **Heaven-born mercury** is now extinct.

The subject further notes: Mix **cinnabar and mercury** in equal parts—adjust quantities as needed—and refine them in an **iron vessel** or **sweet clay crucible (gān’ōu)** over charcoal. When the flame reaches **one chi five cun** in length, the mercury will emerge. Collect it in a **ling water basin (língshuǐpén)**, then gather it with paper.

The subject further notes: Place **raw bamboo tubes** filled with **cinnabar** (or **red cinnabar**) in the earth, covering the mouth with **mica (yúnmù)** to level with the ground. Leave only **three to four cun** of soil above the tube, then ignite it with **husk ash**. After **three days**, the mercury will form. If not yet complete, ignite again and wait another three days. Repeat this process until the mercury is fully refined. **One jin of cinnabar** yields **one jin of mercury**. If the mercury is insufficient—perhaps only **two or three liang**—market mercury may be impure. Such inferior mercury, though a source of longevity, must still be refined with proper elixir methods. Without self-refinement, it is inadequate.

The subject notes: According to the *Bencao* (本草), **mercury** is **spicy and cold**, toxic, and capable of treating **ulcers, scabies, and paralysis**, inducing **abortions**, repelling **lice**, and dissolving **gold, silver, copper, and tin**. It can also **reforge and transmute** back into **cinnabar**. Prolonged ingestion grants **immortality**. Another name for it is **gōng (汞)**.

The **raw cinnabar soil (生符陵平土)** emerges from cinnabar, yet fears magnetite. Now, mercury exists in both raw and refined forms. The so-called **raw cinnabar soil** is that which issues from within cinnabar’s core, or separately from cinnabar earth—both appearing **greenish-white**, most **potent**.

That which comes from **cinnabar** is obtained by burning **unrefined cinnabar powder**, yielding a **white, turbid** substance, inferior to the raw. It can **dissolve and transmute gold and silver into mud**, hence its use in **alchemical transmutation**. For **elixir work**, it is prescribed in **Daoist scriptures**. When mixed with wine and exposed to sunlight, ingestion grants **longevity**.

When burned, it ascends as **flying ash on the crucible’s rim**, named **vermilion powder (朱粉)**—commonly called **mercury ash**—most effective against **lice**.

The subject notes: **Hujangzi** states that mercury has **three origins**:
1. **Hermaphroditic mercury (雄汞)**,
2. **Feminine mercury (雌汞)**,
3. **Divine Flying Mercury (神飞汞)**.
Their uses differ, and their preparation varies. **Divine Flying Mercury** is easiest to subdue by fire, while **Hermaphroditic and Feminine Mercury** resist fire more. For **ascending to the heavens, transcending the void, and attaining longevity**, **Hermaphroditic Mercury** must be used. For **crafting elixirs, summoning spirits**, **Feminine Mercury** is required. For **transmuting copper and iron, reversing the Five Metals**, **Divine Flying Mercury** is employed. Each has its purpose—**do not mix them arbitrarily**. The uninitiated, ignorant of this, fail in their work, defying the **Sage’s prescriptions**, yielding no results. When used correctly, their effects are flawless.

This single substance is the **foundation of Daoist cultivation**; guard it carefully, for even **ten thousand gold pieces** cannot compare to its worth. Common folk understand neither its essence nor its diagrams. Even fewer grasp its intent. Moreover, this method is **jealously guarded by true immortals**, concealed and never revealed. **A hundred stone of gold, ten thousand baskets of pearls**—none would trade for this method. Yet if one **values longevity over all treasures**, and **reveres Daoist cultivation**, they must **pledge their blood in a binding oath** before its secrets may be disclosed.

---
**Method for Hermaphroditic Mercury (雄汞) Longevity Elixir**
Take **ten jin of cinnabar**, one *he* of **ghee**, and forge an **iron crucible**, round, one *chi* in diameter, half a *cun* deep, level and even, ensuring no high or low spots. Seal it tightly, then level its rim. Take **four green lotus petals**, matching the crucible’s mouth, and coat the interior with ghee. Place the **sifted cinnabar** thinly within, ensuring the ghee’s vapor permeates it. Seal with a **ceramic lid**, then caulk the rim with **sheep’s wool and thin mud**, preventing gas escape.

First, ignite **rotted grass**—let it burn for the duration of a meal. Then, kindle **softwood**—**segmented wood or willow**, free of worms and rot—**dampened repeatedly with soaked cotton** to prevent cracking from dryness.

After lighting, **do not stamp the ground or pace violently nearby**, lest the mercury descend into the flames.

From **Chen to Wu hour**, await its descent—either immediately or after a night’s rest. Retrieve it with a **broken hair sack** into a **fresh basin**, wrapping **three to four liang of fresh cotton** in **soft reed bark**, binding it tightly like a **mortar pestle**. Within the basin, crush it thoroughly, extracting all residue.

The powder is separately wrapped, formed into **Six-to-One Mud**—**most secret**.

Those refining mercury must consume **dog meat and wine**. If they abstain, the **mercury’s qi will clog the five viscera**, causing inability to eat or drink, eventually harming them. **Beware.**

From **one jin of cinnabar**, yield **twelve liang**. The **upper cinnabar** yields **ten liang**, the **lower** **eight liang**. This method is **invaluable**; **do not divulge it**.

Initially, **ten bundles of rotted grass** suffice.

---
**Method for Feminine Mercury (雌汞)**
The subject notes: To craft this mercury, mix **one *sheng* of dog fat** with **ten jin of cinnabar** into a paste, filling the crucible. For **Divine Flying Mercury**, grind **ten jin of cinnabar**, **one jin of raw sulfur**, **forty *zǐ* pods**, **one jin of rock salt**, **one jin of turmeric root**, and **one jin of *hútónglǜ* (胡同律)**, sifting each finely. Combine with **cow dung juice** into a paste, coating the crucible **one *cun* thick**. Seal tightly, ignite with kindling, and collect as before.

The **cow dung juice** must be **prepared in the twelfth month**, stored, and warmed with water before use. **Spring cow dung** is weak—its green grass impairs efficacy.

**Obscure terms clarified:**
- **"Yīnshòu xuánjīng zhī"** (阴兽玄精汁) = **cow dung juice**
- **"Shèngwúzhī"** (圣无知) = **red stone alum (赤石脑)**
- **"Qūyuánsù"** (屈原素) = **hútónglǜ (胡同律)**
- **"Hēigāosūn féi"** (黑膏孙肥) = **dog fat**

The subject’s method aligns with **imperial alchemical standards**, hence its omission from older records. All other procedures follow similarly.

「Purification of Mercury with Vinegar

Take **one jin of mercury (水银)**, wrap it in **two layers of silk (帛)**, twist and strain out the dregs, then mix with **three sheng of white salt (白盐)**. Gently knead it until the **mercury (汞)** appears a pure, settled white. Use an **iron vessel (铁器)** to heat it, allowing the **poisonous essence (姻)** to emerge—this is the **resting phase (休)**. Pour it into a **cauldron (釜)** for further processing. When the **poisonous essence (姻)** again emerges, boil it in **three years’ aged vinegar (大醋)**, three sheng at a time, with **gentle fire (微火)**. Complete a **stone’s measure (一石)**, then let it steep for **seven days (七日)** before examining its effects.

If additional substances are introduced, intending to incorporate them into **great elixirs (大丹)**, they must all undergo this same purification method. The method of mixing **vinegar with salt** to achieve verification, or using **oil, honey, and vinegar**, is as stated above.

**Selecting the Proper Time for Mercury Purification**
The subject notes: **Mercury (水银)** is toxic, and **lead (铅)**, aligned with **Too-Yin (太阴)**, cannot act alone—it must always be paired. If not subdued, the **two poisons (二毒)** cannot be fully dispelled. Thus, one must choose **times of Triple-Yang (三阳)**, using **Triple-Yang medicines (三阳之药)**, to subdue **lead and mercury (铅汞)**. This ensures their complete elimination without fail.

Commoners, failing to comprehend, act recklessly—merely mixing them without proper method will kill those who consume it. Simply boiling with **vinegar alone (醋)** is too distant from the **Dao (道)**. Hence, **Triple-Yang times (三阳时)**—specifically **odd-numbered days and odd hours (奇日奇时)**—are most emphasized, particularly **the Fifth Day of the Fifth Month (五月五日)** and **the Seventh Day of the Seventh Month (七月七日)**, as the **Way (道)** holds.

**Triple-Yang Medicines (三阳药)** refer to the **refined essence of the Great Yang (太阳之精气)**, which are **yellow and white (黄白)**. The **morning dew of the sun (朝阳之津液)** is **Left-Flavor (左味)**. The **evening sinews and marrow of the sun (夕阳之筋髓)** are **Golden Thief (金贼)**.

If the **medicinal properties (药味)** are mismatched or the **timing is incorrect (时节)**, even with ten thousand methods of treatment and refining, the **poison will remain (毒不尽)**. Thus, the **Subdued Mercury by Fire (伏火水银)** method states: Use **three years’ aged vinegar (大醋)**, add **fine, aged yellow sand (秾沙)**, and boil it for **one hundred days (百日)**.

Another method says: Use **yellow aged sand (黄秾沙)**, which is **flowing yellow (流黄)**; or **white aged sand (白秾砂)**, with the **two substances equally divided (二物等分)**, and boil the **mercury (汞)** in the **vinegar (醋)**. Observe and test it after **three sets of seven days (三七日)** to discern the **strength or weakness (力强弱)** of the process.

Another method says: Mix **vinegar with salt**, add a **small amount of saltpeter (硝石)**, and boil the **mercury (汞)**. Further, add a **touch of cinnabar powder (胡粉)**, and the **mercury will become white like silver snow (汞即白如银雪)**, suitable for casting into pills.

To incorporate it into **various great elixirs (诸大丹)**, grind the **medicinal residues (药屑)** into powder and add them **after refining (入飞)**.

Another method says: Place the **purified mercury (上汞)** into an **iron vessel (铁器)**, pour over **aged, bitter wine (淳苦酒)**, and boil with **gentle fire (微火)**. As the **bitter wine evaporates (苦酒消)**, replenish it continuously, ensuring it never runs dry. After **thirty-six days (三十六日)**, the **mercury will congeal and dry (汞凝乾)**, making it usable. Without this, the process is merely self-torture.

Another method says: **All refining processes (一切调炼)** must maintain **constant, moderate heat (恒令媪热)**, never so intense that it **scalds the hands (汤人手)**. The **mercury will then appear white like snow (药即白雪)**. Though these methods omit mention of **yellow, white, and Left-Flavor (黄白左味)**, their **principles of nurturing and timing (将养节候)** are still worthy of adoption, hence they are not discarded.

The **authentic method (正诀)** follows below.

**Subduing Mercury with Fox’s Just Child (狐刚子伏水银)**
Take **two jin of mercury (水银)**, in the form of **dark pearls (玄珠)**. Mix with **gold flakes (金屑)** and **silver flakes (银屑)**, along with **vinegar (醋)**, to produce **yellow and white (黄白左味)**. Boil for **thirty days and nights (三十日，三十夜)**, carefully monitoring so the **liquid never runs dry (勿使汁尽)**. The **mercury will then congeal white like snow (凝白如雪)**.

If one intends to make **elixirs (丹)**, follow the **three sets of thirty-six stone’s measures (三十六石)** of **water (水)** for boiling and refining. If the **poison remains (毒未尽)**, remove it, then place the **mercury into the cauldron (入釜)** and immediately form the **elixir (丹)**. If it does not congeal, boil further until it **congeals white like snow (凝白如雪)** as the limit.

The **methods for crafting divine elixirs (所造神丹节｀度)** follow their respective **seventy-two elixir methods (七十二丹诀)**.

**Method of Refining with Gold Dark Pearls (金玄珠法)**
Take **one jin of dark pearls (玄珠)**, with **two and a half liang of gold (金二两半)**, undergoing **fifty refines (五十炼)**. Use **five liang and two and a half fen of lead essence (铅精五两半)**.

Place the **gold flakes (金屑)** into the **cauldron (铛)** at once, and boil them in **yellow and white (黄白左味)**. After **fifteen days and nights (十五日，十五夜)**, carefully monitor so the **liquid never runs dry (无令汁尽)**. The **mercury will congeal white like silver (凝白如银)**.

If the **poison remains (毒未尽)** and one wishes to incorporate it into **elixirs (诸丹)**, boil it again in **three sets of thirty-six stone’s measures (三十六石)** of **water (水)**, refining, removing the **poison (去毒)**, and adding it **after refining (入飞)**. If it can be mixed with **gold powder (金粉)**, then the **pills and ointments (散丸膏)** are made from **dried yellow mercury (黄乾伏)**.

**Method of Refining with Silver Dark Pearls (银玄珠法)**
Take **one jin of dark pearls (玄珠)**, with **one liang and two and a half fen of silver (银一两半)**, undergoing **fifty refines (五十炼)**. Use **six liang and two and a half fen of lead essence (铅精六两半)**.

Place the **silver flakes (银屑)** into the **cauldron (铛)** at once, and boil them in **yellow and white (黄白左味)**. After **nine days and nights (九日九夜)**, carefully monitor as before, ensuring the **outer impurities are fully removed (表裹彻净)**. The **mercury will congeal white and luminous (凝白光明)**.

If one wishes to make it **pure white (作白)**, boil it in **water of the Sunstone (誉石水)** for **half a day (半日)**, then in **water of the White Alum (白矾石水)** for another **half day (半日)**. Dry it, then subdue it to make **white mercury (伏作白)**—this will succeed.

To incorporate it into **various powders (诸粉)**, remove the **poison (去毒)** first, then add it **after refining (入飞)**.

**Method of Refining with Nine-Elixir Lead Essence and Dark Pearls (九丹铅精玄珠法)**
Take **two jin of dark pearls (玄珠)**, with **twelve liang of lead essence from Nine-Elixir (九丹铅精十二两)**. Boil in **yellow and white (黄白左味)** for **seven days and nights (七日七夜)**. The **mercury will congeal white and fully purified (凝白彻净)**, then dry and subdue it to remove the **poison (去毒)**.

Combine with **all other medicines (合诸药)**, and it will become **River Chariot (河车)**.

With **the eight kinds of methods (八种)**, **elixir and lead (丹铅)** can be refined from **one to nine (从一至九)**, selecting as needed. When layered upon **various elixirs (覆籍诸丹)**, none will fail to form. Transformations are possible at will—incorporating **copper or iron (铜铁)** as desired.

**The seventy-two divine alchemical methods (七十二丹神器)** all use this process, adjusting **depth and quantity (深浅)** according to the **seasonal transformations (华应)**.

**Authentic Method for Subduing Mercury with Mulberry Ash (煮伏水银诀)**
Take **four liang of mercury (水银)**, with **one liang of silver (银一两)**, forming a **mercury-silver paste (银汞泥饼)**. Place it in an **iron container (铁函)** with **mulberry ash (桑灰)**, which must be **finely sifted and white (细筛白诤)**.

The subject notes: The **above methods (上件诸法)** all use **fewer days (日数)**. People often follow them, but if verification fails, they abandon the process. This occurs due to **excessive vinegar and intense fire (醋多火急)**, **liquid depletion and mercury drying (汁尽汞乾)**, **mismatched medicinal properties (药味差违)**, or **improper seasonal transformations (华池失法)**.

Now, the **cauldron (铛)** should be **five fen thick (五分)**, ground smooth and even. Do not place **any base layer (元布案)** inside the **cauldron (铛)**. The **mulberry ash (桑灰)** should be **seven fen thick (七分)**. Mix it thoroughly with **vinegar (醋)**, ensuring **even saturation (浥浥)** and no **uneven distribution (无置高下)**. Spread it **four times evenly (四布平停)**.

Do not press it firmly, lest it **crack or split (拆莹)**. Ensure **uniform diffusion of qi (气均赓)** and **steam permeation (熏润)** to subdue the **mercury (水银)**.»

「Make a wooden stake, using silk as its base. On the silk, spread **water silver** and the other medicines evenly—namely **stone-flow yellow (石流)**, white arsenic (黄白), **arsenic sulfide (确砂)**, rock salt (石盐), **lodestone (磁石)**, **bitter salt (卤咸)**, and **barite powder (胡粉)**—each weighing one *liang* (两). Mix with six *liang* of **mulberry ash (桑灰)**, sift through a fine sieve, and apply it uniformly over the **water silver**, making it two *fen* (分) thick. Saturate it with **vinegar (醋)**, ensuring it remains **consistently moist like porridge (恒使如粥)**, neither too dry nor overly excessive, and always keep its **qi balanced and upright (气调直)**—if it bubbles violently, that is **excessive fire (火急)**.

Replace the **ash and medicine** in the **cauldron (铛)** daily. Use **special paper (盖)**, which strictly avoids dust and impurities; the added ingredients must not be **tossed in carelessly (例不玲投)**. Retain the mixture as per the above method, until it reaches **one hundred days**, when the **water silver** will be fully transformed.

Once the cooking is complete, crush and dry it for **oral ingestion**. The method for **dry ingestion of *xuanzhu* (玄珠)** follows:

Use an **iron pot (熟铁锅)** weighing eight *jin* (斤), initially forged into two halves, each weighing four *jin*. At the center of each half, carve a hole the size of a **chicken egg (鸡子)**, wrapping the edges four times with a strip of metal, then weld them shut, making the pot **half a *cun* (寸) thick** overall. On the **greenish-black surface (车窠展绿)**, drill a hole as thick as an **arrow shaft (箭竿)**. At the hole’s edges, make the metal **thicker for secure fastening (务欲钉牢)**. Pour the **mercury (水银)** into the pot and seal it with a weld; verify its **tightness by tapping (勘可旁量)**, ensuring absolute **leak-proof integrity (必须牢密)**.

Pound the **medicines into fine powder (细药)**, then apply **four layers of sweet clay (甘泥)**, each coating **half a *cun* thick**. Leave it exposed for **five to six days**, until thoroughly dry. Then place it in a **charcoal fire (炭火)**, arranging the **ash bags (排囊)** and gradually blowing until the pot glows red, lasting **one meal’s time (一食时)**. After removing the **ash bags**, let the fire extinguish naturally; wait through the night until the next morning. From **Chen (辰)** to **Si (巳)**, adjust the heat as needed. When the pot emits a **shaking sound like broken tiles (去土摇铁如瓦砾声)**, weigh it again—its weight should remain **unchanged (秤铁复本是不耗)**. If the sound is lost, the weight has been **consumed (即本耗)**.

When the process is complete, **chisel open the pot** to remove the **water silver**. Dry and store it properly, then **refine its toxicity (诀须去毒)**.

To **remove *xuanzhu*’s toxicity (去玄珠毒)**:
First, prepare **yellow alum (黄矾) water**—one *dou* (斗). Place it in a **copper cauldron (铜铛)** and cook the **water silver** within, using **five *jin* above and two *jin* below** (上可五斤，下可二斤), until the **alum water is fully consumed (令矾石水尽)**.

Next, **burn cow dung** without leaving any ash, then **grind lodestone into small beans (磁石破如小豆)**. Boil the **dung ash** until it reaches a **rolling boil (极沸)**, and use this **hot decoction to wash the *xuanzhu* powder twice (淋二灰)**. Collect the **liquid residue (取汁)** in the **cauldron**, then cook the **water silver** for **one day and night (煮玄珠一日夜)**. Afterward, use **three cycles of refined *huangbai* (黄白) medicines** (黄白左味) to **recook it for another day and night (更煮经一宿一日)**.

Upon completion, add **three cycles of fine wine (好酒)** and **honey (蜜)**, cooking again for **one day and night (更煮经一宿一日)**. Finally, take **pure ghee (真酥)** and cook it for **three nights (更煮之三夜)**. Remove the **water silver**, place it in a **copper vessel (铜器)**, and cover it tightly. Bury it in **millet (黍米)** and **steam it for three days and nights (蒸之三日三夜)**—this will **fully eliminate its toxicity (出其毒皆尽)**, allowing it to be **incorporated into any medicine (可以入万药)** or used for **immortal elixirs (服饵神仙)**. When **yellow and white arsenic sublimate into smoke upon heating (作黄白入火飞)**, this marks the **ultimate attainment of the Dao/Way (此是道之至极毕矣)**.

The phrase **"three cycles of fine wine (三转好酒)"** refers to **dogwood wine (牡荆酒)**. The term **"three cycles of *huangbai* (黄白左味)"** means **three cycles of the *huangbai* medicines (黄白左味)**. When cooking **water silver** with **alum water**, both the **vessel and the mercury** must be **refined (镕)**. If the **water silver** does not **dissolve (消)**, you may instead make it into **cauldron cakes (铛饼子)**. If it cannot be crushed, **sift it finely and cook it**, or apply the **steaming method** as well. A **five-*jin* cauldron (五斤铛)** can hold **two *dou* of finely processed *xuanzhu* (二斗细理者)**—all **water silver** detoxification methods converge here, with no other variations.

Only the **Taixuan Master’s formula (太玄君诀)** states: **"Do not ask if it is dry; just ingest *xuanzhu* (玄珠)."** If you ingest *xuanzhu* **while moist**, seeking to **remove its toxicity**, even **one *liang* of sweet yellow (甜黄)**—a type of **yellow earth (一名玄黄土)**, sourced from the **Western barbarian lands (西方胡国)**—will prevent the **water silver’s essence from dispersing (玄珠精不能散去)**. Even **lodestone fears it (磁石亦以为畏)**, and **Mieduo Seng (蜜陀僧)** serves as its **commander (臣将)**. If you use **yellow cinnabar (黄丹)** or **barite powder (胡粉)** to **restrain the water silver’s essence**, it is merely **common practice (俗间杂用)**, not the **authentic formula (正本诀)**. Similarly, using **yellow arsenic sulfide (黄秾沙)** or **rock salt (石盐)** is also **not the orthodox method (非正本口诀)**.

The **alternative method for moistening and subduing *xuanzhu* (湿伏玄珠法)** uses **hooked lead (以钩铅)**:

First, take a **well-refined iron cauldron (好细理铁铛)**, capable of holding **three to two *sheng* (升)**. Shape it like the **"turtle method (鳌法)"**, leaving a **long opening (长开口)**. When the **mercury is first sealed (及突融先伏)** and you wish to **combine the medicines (及欲合药)**, it becomes the **"River Cart (河车)"**.

Form the **water silver into cakes (玄珠作饼)**, place them in the **cauldron**, and cover them with **lead powder (银粉为覆藉)**—or, if **lead powder is unavailable**, use **cinnabar lead powder (丹铅粉)** instead. The method is detailed in the **ninth *Si* (巳) section**.

Add **five *sheng* of oil (油脂)** and **one *sheng* of honey (蜜)**, then **mix and cook the *xuanzhu* cakes**. Some say the process lasts **thirty days and nights (三十日夜止)**, while others claim **three days and nights suffice (三日夜罢)**. The **earlier method for detoxifying copper and iron (前去毒煮法)** requires **one day and night (用一日夜)**. This **moistening and subduing method (湿伏法)** now employs **oil (油脂)**.

The **method for producing *longsheng* water silver (出长生水银)** uses **one *ge* (合) of ghee (酥)** to **coat the cauldron (涂釜)**, then **boils the water silver** while **covering with a clay-honey mixture (堵脂和朱为泥)**. In the **earlier detoxification method**, **wine and honey (酒和蜜)** are used, whereas in this **moistening and subduing method**, **oil and honey (油脂和蜜)** are applied—this is the **distinction (别矣)**.

This is called the **"moistening and subduing technique (湿伏之功)"**, differing from the **"River Cart method for copper and iron (立变铜铁也)"**.」

「Thus, the **mercury refined by the moistening and subduing method (湿伏之汞)**—when combined with **remaining subdued fire elixir (余伏火药)**—can produce **the elixir’s true formula (丹方)**. If one instead **refines the *xuánzhū* (玄珠) with herbs (药)**, stirring and mixing them until completion, that is **the River Cart method (河车之法)**, not the **genuine subdued *xuánzhū* (真伏玄珠)**.

The **Scribe notes (臣按)**: To **forge *huánghuā* (玄黄) from mercury** or to **attempt the Great Elixir (大丹)**, one must first **distill it in an empty cauldron (空煮取拟)**. If not distilled, **mercury can be paired with *jiǔdān* lead (九丹铅精)**, but **it must be refined with fifty-fold smelted lead (五十炼铅精)** and **gold and silver (金银)** to **bind and retain (拘留)** it properly.

**End of the *Eleventh Scroll of the Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon (黄帝九鼎神丹经诀卷之十一)**.
**Twelfth Scroll of the Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon (黄帝九鼎神丹经诀卷之十二)** begins with the **method for combining *jiǔdān* lead (合九丹铅法)** and the **powers of refined lead (铅力功能)**.

The **Scribe notes (臣按)**: **Hú Gāngzǐ (狐刚子)** says: *"In combining elixir ingredients (合丹药), lead (铅) is the foundation. If the lead is not genuine (不真), the elixir will never succeed (药无成者)."* Thus it is said: *"Lead (铅), the sinew and marrow of **yin-yang (阴阳)**, the finest medium of **the Seven Treasures (七宝)**—when **unblocked (解)**, all undertakings can be achieved; when **obstructed (迷)**, even a thousand paths are sealed. Hence the saying: **‘Lead surpasses the River Cart, empty (铅绝河车空)’,**—what is made will **never succeed (必无功)**. **‘The power ends with the River Cart, empty (功断河车绝)’,**—all calculations will yield nothing (万计无所出)."* It is further said: *"Do not **break my Cart (莫破我车)**, nor **ruin my return home (废我还家)**. Do not **corrupt my lead (莫坏我铅)**, or **my life will be preserved (我命得全)**."*

The **Cart (车)** refers to the **River Cart (河车)**. Among **the eight River Cart methods (八河车法)**, none can succeed without relying on lead (铅). The **covering and nurturing elixir (丹之覆荐之药)** is what is called the **River Cart (河车)**. Hence it is said: *"Without the eight kinds of River Cart, the elixir has no foundation or refinement (丹无依伏是也)."*

The **Scribe further notes (又按)**: **Lead (太阴)** is the **lead (铅)**, while **the elixir (太阳)** is the **elixir (丹)**. When these two are combined into a medicine (成药), those who take it become **divine immortals (神仙)**. The **refined essence of elixir and lead (丹铅之精)** can **emit flowing pearls of white snow (出流珠白雪)**. When **two waters (二水)** are added and **all is distilled a hundred times (凡百蒸之)**, taking **one *jīn* (斤)** and dividing it into **nine portions (九分)**, repeatedly **transforming and refining (转变不已)**, it becomes **the elixir of the Divine (化神丹)**. Its **powers are profound (功既探)**, and its **efficacy is vast (力亦大)**. Through **nine ascensions and nine descensions (九上九下)**, covering and nurturing **mercury (水银)**, and **transforming mercury into elixir (化汞为丹)** in **three cycles of nine refineries (三作九转)**, it is why **the Sage keeps it secret (故圣人秘之)**, unknown to **ordinary Daoists (凡俗道士)**.

Lead’s refined essence has **thirty-six secret names (秘目)**, listed as follows:
**Thirty-six Secret Names of Elixir and Lead (丹铅秘目三十六名)**
1. **Name of *Huánghuā* (玄黄花)**
2. **Name of *Huángqīng* (黄轻)**
3. **Name of *Lónglín* (龙鳞)**
4. **Name of Subdued Elixir (伏丹)**
5. **Name of River Cart (河车)**
6. **Name of Elixir Essence (丹液)**
7. **Name of *Yìdān* (驿丹)**
8. **Name of *Zhìdān* (制丹)**
9. **Name of *Liàndān* (炼丹)**
10. **Name of *Huángyá* (黄芽)**
11. **Name of *Shìdǎn* (石胆)**
12. **Name of Yin-Yang Parents (阴阳父母)**
13. **Name of *Fēiqīng* (飞轻)**
14. **Name of *Huángjīng* (黄精)**
15. **Name of *Huánglóngfú* (黄龙符)**
16. **Name of *Héshàngnǐnǚ* (河上妮女)**
17. **Name of *Lìzhìshí* (立制石)**
18. **Name of *Gōng* (汞)**
19. **Name of *Huánghuā* (黄花)**
20. **Name of Completed Elixir (成已丹)**
21. **Name of *Zǐfěn* (紫粉)**
22. **Name of *Hóngfěn* (红粉)**
23. **Name of *Liúzhūyè* (流珠液)**
24. **Name of *Zǐmíng* (紫明)**
25. **Name of *Xuándān* (玄丹)**
26. **Name of *Huánglóng* (黄龙)**
27. **Name of *Jīnhuǒfú* (金火符)**
28. **Name of Yin-Yang Essence and Marrow (阴阳之精髓)**
29. **Name of Heaven-Earth Mother (天地母)**
30. **Name of *Yèshénfú* (液神符)**
31. **Name of *Jīnhuā* (金花)**
32. **Name of *Fēidān* (飞丹)**
33. **Name of *Huánghuá* (黄华)**
34. **Name of *Tàiyīn* (太阴)**
35. **Name of *Jīngōng* (金公)**
36. **Name of *Héshàngyóunǚ* (河上游女).

The **Scribe notes (臣按)**: All **these thirty-six wondrous medicines (三十六名妙药)** are achieved through the **power of refined lead (铅精之力)**. Therefore, the **first method of the Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir (黄帝九鼎神丹第一之法)** is called **Elixir Flower (丹华)**. Another name is **Flowing Pearl Nine Refineries (流珠九转)**, which is made by **combining lead with mercury (以铅合汞)**.

Ordinary people **do not know (凡俗不知)**, and thus **they use tin from the market (市锡) as lead (为铅)****. This is like seeking progress by retracing one’s steps at dusk—how difficult it is! (可谓日暮途远，却行求进，不亦难矣.)** The methods for making it now must be **precise and specialized (皆须精专)**, completing **nine transformations (转至九方)**.

**Hú Gāngzǐ’s Method for Nine-Refinery Lead-Elixir (狐刚子作九转铅丹法)**
Take **ten *jīn* (斤) of lead (铅十斤)**, smelt it in an **iron cup (铁杯)** until it becomes **green sand (作青沙)**, then pound it in an **iron basin (铁盆)** with an **iron hammer (铁锤)** until it emits **yellow juice (取黄汁)**. Spread this **juice on fresh tiles (新瓦上暴)**, collect the **yellow powder (黄粉)**, and mix it with **the essence of *xuánzhū* (玄精汁)** to form **a pellet like a rooster’s egg (为团如鸡子)**. Let it dry in the **yin (阴)**, then smelt it in a **revolving furnace (缭炉)** to extract **the refined essence of lead (铅精)**. Return this essence to the **iron cup (铁杯)** and smelt it with **fierce fire (猛火)**. After **one cycle of refinement (一伏时)**, it becomes **lead-elixir (铅丹)**. Repeat this **nine times (如此九转)** to achieve **Nine-Refinery Lead (名曰九转铅)**.

The **sequence of transformations and medicines (转数用药次第)** is detailed in **the Yellow Old Master’s Nine Ascending Elixirs Canon (黄老九飞丹节度中)**.

**Method for *Jiǔdān* Lead and *Xuánzhū* (九丹铅玄珠法)**
Take **three *jīn* (斤) of *xuánzhū* (玄珠)** and **twelve *liǎng* (两) of *jiǔdān* lead essence (九丹铅精)**, and **distill them together in the *Huángbái Zuǒwèi* (黄白左味)** for **seven days and nights (七日夜)**. When the **white congeals and the black disperses (凝白彻挣)**, dry it, **subdue its toxicity (伏去毒)**, and combine it with **other medicines (合诸药)**—thus **the River Cart is formed (即成河车)**.

Among **the eight River Carts (八河之车)**, **lead-elixir ranges from the first to the ninth (丹铅从一至九)**—one may **select as needed (任取其用)**—to **cover and nurture all elixirs (藉覆诸丹)**, and **none will fail (无有不成者)**. It can **freely transform when mixed with copper or iron (随意入铜铁，变化自在)****. All **seventy-two divine elixir instruments (七十二丹神器)** are made using this method, each **according to the refinement of the medicines (各随药转)** and **adjusting depth and efficacy (深浅任量)**.

Though this method is already described in **the *Xuánzhū* Scroll (玄珠卷中)**, the **principles of using lead (用铅之道)** are **reiterated and emphasized (虽重发扬)**. Upon reviewing this text, one understands that **the lead used in the River Cart must be distilled in *Huángbái Zuǒwèi* (黄白左味)**, congealed, dried, and detoxified (煮凝，乾伏并备)**, only then can it be applied.

It is further said: *"Lead-elixir ranges from the first to the ninth—select as needed (丹铅从一至九，任取)."* Common people **do not know (俗人不知)**, and thus **they read *rèn* (任) with a falling tone (去声)**, but **it should be read with a level tone (平声)**, meaning *"capable of (堪也)"*. **The lead must undergo nine refineries (其铅非至九转)** before it is **capable of being used (不堪取也)**.

「Thus it is said: *"The lead-elixir, from the first to the ninth—once refined, it is capable of being used (任取矣)."* When **nine-refined lead-elixir (九转丹铅)** is used for the **River Cart (河车)**, or when applied to **cover and nurture (覆藉)** other elixirs, **there is none that fails (无有不成)**. The **seventy-two elixirs of the divine instruments (七十二丹神器)** all rely on this for their creation, each **adapting to the medicine’s potency (各随药转)**.

**Only nine-refined lead-elixir (非九转丹铅)** is **capable of being used (不堪作玄黄也)** as **Xuanhuang (玄黄)**—the **alchemical essence of lead and sulfur (铅黄花)**. It is further said: *"Though one may freely combine it with copper or iron (随意入铜铁), its transformations are unrestrained (变化自在),"* yet **the method of testing and refining (试药点黄白之道)** is **not achieved (亦非此九转丹铅成者)** unless **this nine-refined lead-elixir (此)** is **properly used (不任用也)**.

**The Method of Extracting Long-Life Lead (出长生铅法)**
I observe: **Though the Dao of lead-elixir (丹铅之道)** is **universally nine-refined (法皆九转)**, its applications **differ in three ways (按其用处，三种不同)**. If one seeks **long life, eternal vision, and transcendence (长生久视，羽化升天)**, **one must forge *xióng* lead (雄铅)**. If one seeks **to summon ghosts and spirits, or to transmute into liquid like water (辟召鬼神，化液作水)**, **one must use *cí* lead (雌铅)**. If one seeks **to transform yellow and white, or to transmute the five metals (变化黄白，回换五金)**, **one must use *shénfēi* lead (神飞铅)**.

Common people **mistake the first refinement (一) as mere crude mixture (混而无二)**, and thus **their applications are disordered (用之错乱)**, their creations **fail (所作不成)**, and they **blame the sages for ineffectual prescriptions (遂怨咎圣人方书无效)**. But **if refined and used correctly (若审而用之)**, **there is no failure (万不失一)**. This method **is unknown to the vulgar (此法俗无有解者)**, and **only those who have seen the *Five-Powder Diagram* (五粉图)** can **barely grasp its minimal proportions (乃能略知少配)**. Hence, **true persons (真人)** keep it **as a guarded secret (宝秘而不传)**.

**This single medicine (此之一药)** is **the foundation of Daoist arts (道术之本)**—**guard it carefully (慎勿轻传)**, for **its worth is beyond gold (万金不泄)**. Even if **one possessed a hundred stones of yellow gold and ten thousand baskets of pearls (假使黄金百石，明珠万筐)**, **one would still not reveal it (亦不传也)**. **If one obtained this method (若得此法)**, **all treasures would be seen as mere soil (七宝视之如土)**—**why need one hoard gold and pearls (何用百石万筐乎)**? Only **those who treasure long life (宝骯长生), cherish the Dao of transcendence (爱慕仙道), and swear solemn oaths (敌血分环，重立信誓)** may **be granted its minimal proportions (乃可略而出之)**.

**This pertains also to the methods of mercury (此言并是汞方之所具载)**. Yet **three leads and three mercuries are but one (然以三铅三汞，一而已矣)**. Hence the prescription states: *"Their functions differ, yet they share no distinction with mercury (功用别能，与汞无异)**."* **Mercury and lead (汞之与铅)** **cannot act alone (终不独行)**—**they must always pair (行必为偶)**. **If refined and used correctly (审而用之)**, **there is no failure (万不失一)**. Common people **often mistake tin for lead (俗人多以锡为铅)**, **far from the Dao (去道远矣)**.

It is further said: **The *xióng*, *cí*, and *shénfēi* leads (雄雌神飞三种)** each **require three refineries (各须三转)** before **their prescriptions take effect (用方有效)**. The **method of refining (转之法)** is **no different from what was stated earlier (用，不异於前)**—**lead, when refined to nine stages (铅至九转)**, becomes **a divine medicine (体为神药)**. **When combined with other medicines (用入余药)**, **none fail (无不效矣)**. Hence, **those who have seen the *Five-Powder Diagram* (惟见粉图者)** know **its profound intent (知少意深)**. **All other sages and immortals (自余仙圣)** keep **this prescription hidden (皆秘此方)**. Thus, **today’s creations (故今所作)** are **often flawed, rarely successful (多败少成矣)**.

**The Method of Extracting *Xióng* and *Cí* Leads (出雄雌铅法)**
Take **a hundred pounds of true elixir (真丹百斤)** and **ten pounds of *Qīngbái Yángqǐ* stone (青白阳起石)**. Further, **grind the *Táo Yángqǐ* stone (梼阳起石)** and **sift it finely (细筛之)**. **Mix it with *Xuanjing* juice (玄精汁)** to form **clusters (作团)**, and **expose them to dry (暴之令燥)**.

**Place them in an iron pot (纳铁锅中)** and **heat with a furnace (以炉鼓之)** until **the juice is fully consumed (待为汁消尽)**. **Pour it into warm ashes (泻於暖灰中)** and **wait for the clusters to be selected (待玲打择)**. **Take them as *Danfù* lead (取之为丹覆)**—**the finest (最佳)**. **The term *Danfù* (丹覆)** refers to **medicines for the alchemical essence of lead and sulfur (入神丹玄黄之药也)**.

**The Method of Extracting *Cí* Lead (出雌铅法)**
Take **a hundred pounds of true elixir (真丹百斤)** and **fifteen pounds of true powder (真粉)**. **Take one pound of *Hào Qīngfān* (昊青矾)** and **one pound of lime (石灰)**—**each ground separately (各别梼)**. **Sift the *fān* and stone finely (其矾石细筛)**. **Combine these four substances (四物合和)** and **roll them into pills with *Xuanjing* juice (以玄精汁丸之)**. **Dry them in the shade (阴乾出之)**—**the method is identical to that previously described (法与前不异也)**.

**The Method of Extracting *Shénfēi* Lead (出神飞铅法)**
Take **a hundred pounds of true elixir (真丹百斤)**, **five pounds of *Hào Huángfān* (昊黄矾)**, **one pound of red rock salt (赤石盐)**, **two pounds of *Yùjīn* root (郁金根)**, and **five ounces of yellow sulfur (黄炮砂)**. **Grind these five substances separately (此五味异梼下筛)** and **mix them with wine and elixir (以酒合丹搜之)**—**do not let them adhere (勿令相着)**. **Expose them to dry (暴之令燥)** and **regrind and sift them (更梼筛之)**. Then **take *Xuanjing* juice (牛粪汁)** and **soak them to form clusters (没之为团)**. **Dry them in the shade (阴乾之)**—**the method is as before (出法一如前诀者)**.

**The prescription calls *red rock salt* (赤石盐) *"the Sage’s Unknown"* (圣无知者)**. **The term *Xuanjing juice* (玄精汁) refers to *cow dung juice* (牛粪汁)**. **The term *Huángshān zhī* (黄山脂) refers to *Hào fān* (昊矾)**. **The term *Huángjīn zéi* (黄金贼) refers to *stone sulfur* (石硫黄)**. **In general, when combining medicines with elixir (凡以药和丹一法)**, the **order is: first *Huángfān* (黄矾), then *Chì Líng* (赤灵)**, then *Yùjīn* root (郁金根), then *stone sulfur* (石硫黄), and finally *Huángdān* (黄丹)**. **After this, moisten them with fine wine (讫，方以好酒润和之)**—**do not let them cling (勿使相着)**. **For every fifty pounds of *Huángdān* (黄丹)**, **use five *dàshēng* (大升) of clear wine (可用清酒五大升)**. **Spread them on a high rack with reed mats (於高架苇箔)**, **cover with thick paper (上铺厚纸)**, **seal with fish scales (糊鱼鳞)**, and **press in two layers (相压两重)**. **Expose them for about one day (暴可一日许)**. Then **soak them in cow dung juice to form clusters (然用牛粪汁没之为团)** and **dry them in the shade for ten days (於架箔上阴乾十日)**.

**Another method (又法)**: **First weigh the elixir (先秤丹知斤两)** and **the medicines separately (又别秤药知斤两)**. **Then match their proportions (即以药对丹)**—**adjusting for excess or deficiency (多少相配)**. **Sift them through a fine sieve (以赢罗筛)**. **Layer them alternately—one layer of elixir (布一重丹)**, one layer of medicine (一重药)**—**until all are exhausted (重重相次并尽)**. Then **mix them with wine (然后以酒搜之)**.

**The First Refining of Lead (鼓出铅诀第一转)**
Take **the medicines used (以所用味之药)**—**each ground separately and sifted finely (各异梼下筛)**—**and mix them with wine as previously described (以酒如上法合没)**—**do not let them adhere (勿令相着)**. **Spread them to dry (摊暴令乾)** and **regrind them, sift them finely (更梼下筛)**. **Combine them with cow dung juice to form clusters (以牛粪汁和搜为团)**. **The cow dung should be collected and stored in the twelfth month (其牛粪以腊月收贮)** and **steeped in boiled water (以燸水浸独)**. **Take the juice to form clusters like the yolk of an egg (取之团如鸡子黄)**—**if larger, they are harder to dry (若更大者难乾)**. **Dry them in the shade for two weeks (二七日阴乾之)** and **place them in an iron pot (纳铁锅中)**. **The pot’s base is seven inches long (长七寸)**—**its thickness varies: six and a half *fēn* (分) at the bottom (底厚六分半)**, five *fēn* in the middle (以下五分)**, and four *fēn* at the top (以上四分)**—**its width is three and a half inches (明问三寸半)**. **Heat them with a furnace (排炉出看)** until **the juice is fully consumed (尽消为汁)**. **Then pour them into warm, fine white ashes (方泻着暖灰中)**—**sifted and spread evenly on a clean surface (其灰唯细筛白者)**—**three to four *fēn* thick (厚三四分)**. **Roll the edges with dry clay (四畔以乾泥卷绕灰)** to **prevent the lead juice from spreading (不使铅汁流溢四散)**. **Press the clusters with your hands (以手摸铅)** and **wait for their selection (待玲打择)**. **The wine used should be one *dǒu* (斗) per hundred pounds (率百斤)**—**or **two *dǒu* if using *Xuanjing* juice (若玄精汁，二斗即可)**—**to yield **a hundred pounds of refined lead (团得百斤丹)**.

**The Second Refining of Lead (鼓出铅诀第二转)**
Take **the refined lead from the previous stage (上件铅)** and **roast it in an iron bowl (於铁杯中炒之)**. **The bowl’s base is three feet long (长三尺)**, **one inch thick (厚一寸)**, and **one foot deep (深一尺)**—**with slightly flared edges (两头得稍绰)**.

So **the length is three feet and five inches (上长三尺五寸)**, **the width one foot and two inches (阔一尺二寸)**, **shaped like a trough (如槽之形也)**.

**Rub and wrap it until it is extremely smooth and pure (摩裹令滑极净)**, **lest it crackle or emit a bright glow (勿使嘶莹)**.

**Stir it with a long, blunt sword and an iron rake (以长钝剑铁篦搅之)**, **roasting until all the sand is exhausted (炒令并作沙尽)**, **from dawn till noon (从旦至午)**. **When it becomes fine powder (看成细末)**, **continuously scrape it out (续续掠出)** and **place it in a cold vessel (置冷器中)**—**a thick iron basin or pan (其器是厚铁盆擭也)**.

**Add clear water (着清水)**, **stirring with a long iron rake (以长铁篦搅之)**. **Have two or three people take turns stirring (使两三人更互搅)**, **without pausing (勿令住手)**, **until it forms a juice (使成汁也)**.

**Similarly, when roasting lead in the iron bowl (然於铁杯中炒铅)**, **you may also alternate helpers (亦得换人)**, **but must not pause (不得住手)**.

**If there is any interruption (若有问断)**, **the sand must be remelted again (其沙复镕)**. **Place the iron bowl over a charcoal fire (铁杯之下然以柴火)**, **for if the fire is too weak (火玲不得)**, **the sand will not melt completely (沙成)**, **and if the fire is too fierce (大热)**, **it may melt uncontrollably (恐镕不止)**. **Observe the fire carefully at the moment of operation (临事看火)**, **neither too slow nor too rapid (勿令缓急也)**.

**Collect the yellow juice from the crucible (接取坩徒黄汁)**, **place it in a porcelain container (置瓷子中)**—**pierce holes in the bottom with a water drill (着水钻腹作孔)**—**wait until the juice settles and clarifies (候徒澄清)**. **Pour out the water through the holes (倾孔去水)**, **and evenly extract the clarified juice with a smooth iron rake (以滑铁篦匀率出澄徒)****, placing it on fresh tiles (置新瓦上)**.

**Previously, lay two layers of paper on the tiles (预於瓦上铺两重纸)**. **Spread the tiles evenly in the sun (以瓦凡平布烈日之中)** and **expose them for one day (暴之一日)**. **The lead will then harden and crack on the tiles (丹在瓦上硬裂乾定)**. **Collect it with a fine sieve (收取梼筛)** and **put it back into the iron bowl (纳铁杯中)**.

**Stir and roast it again with the iron rake (还以铁篦搅炒令赤)** until it turns **red (赤)**, **over three days and nights (三日夜)**. **Do not use intense fire (不得猛火)**; **once the lead is red, it is complete (丹赤即成)**—**the days are not strictly counted (不拘日数也)**.

**The Third Refining of Lead (鼓出铅诀第三转)**
**For all cases of using wine to extract medicine (凡以酒搜药)**, **or using *Xuanjing* juice to mix with the lead (及以玄精汁拌丹)**, **it must be done in a straight-mouthed, deep copper basin (皆於直口深铜盆中)**. **The basin must be smooth and pure (盆须滑净)**; **do not use tiles or flared-mouthed vessels (不得辄用瓦器，及绰口者)**.

**Otherwise, the medicine may scatter (恐药飞散)**, **the wine juice may be wasted (消耗酒汁)**, **and the proportions may be lost (致失准则)**. **The remaining methods are as before (余法如前)**. **The amount of medicine used is adjusted according to the increase or decrease of the lead (其用药随丹增损)**—**to determine the strength, weakness, or quality (以为多少衰降臧之也)**.

**The Refining of Lead with Cow Dung (牛粪取汁鼓铅法)**

In all cases where the juice of pressed and strained cow dung is used, it must be thickened to the consistency of congee. Thus, the common method of refining lead to make it white in color involves taking any quantity of fine wine and mixing it with white cinnabar (白炮砂) in the wine. The cinnabar should be gradually melted until it is fully dissolved, and this wine-cinnabar mixture is then blended with the dung juice to achieve the consistency of thin congee. After spreading it on a heavy cloth (厅路重布) and pressing, the resulting dung juice is used to mix with the medicinal elixir (药丹), moistening it thoroughly until it forms clusters like rooster eggs (团如鸡子)—it may also be left unclustered.
