Then, it is exposed to the sun to dry, placed in a furnace, and melted. After a short while, the lead emerges and is poured into a cow’s gallbladder (泻牛胆中). This process is repeated five times, and the lead will become white.

If white honey (白蜜) is used to submerge the elixir, like a strong paste, and then exposed to the sun as before, its potency will also be preserved. If the elixir hardens and the lead does not emerge, the white cinnabar must be removed. Though this lead may appear white, it is not the true method. If the refined lead from the nine transformations (九转丹铅) is not pleasing to the eye—its color being greenish-black and its texture soft—then its transformative power is beyond ordinary understanding (神化之力，不知所以然而然者也).

**The Nine-Transformation Divine Elixir of the Supreme Daoist (太极真人九转丹)**
**First Transformation (第一转):** Take five hundred *catty* of barite powder (胡粉), and mix it with twenty *catty* of rock salt (石盐) in one *dou* of water. Then, add one *dou* of cow dung juice to form clusters like rooster eggs (丸如鸡子) and dry them in the shade (阴乾). Place these in a furnace, refine them briefly, and the lead emerges—this is called *powder-lead* (粉铅), known as *Earth’s Essence* (地之精也). Take five *catty* of yellow cinnabar (黄丹), mix it with cow dung juice, form clusters like rooster eggs, and dry them in the shade. Place these in a furnace and refine them briefly, and the lead emerges—this is called *cinnabar-lead* (丹铅), known as *Heaven’s Essence* (天之精也).

**Second Transformation (第二转):** Take the previously refined *Heaven’s* and *Earth’s Essence* (天地之精), blend and roast them until they become a greenish-yellow powder like fine sand (水色青沙). Then, mix thirty *catty* of refined *stone alum* (石盥) with eight *dou* of hot water, and add salted water (日咸水). Grind this mixture in salted water until it turns a yellowish-brown powder like soil-colored sand (土色黄沙), then pulverize it finely and place it in a wok (铛器). Burn it for three days and three nights until it transforms into red sand like fire (火色赤沙), matching the color of fine cinnabar (与好丹色同). The process is complete.

**Third Transformation (第三转):** Take the refined cinnabar from the previous step and mix it with one *dou* of the milk of a firstborn son (首男乳). If firstborn son’s milk is difficult to obtain, yellow cow’s milk (黄牛乳) may be used instead. Add one *dou* of cow dung juice, thirty *catty* of refined rock salt (石盐明诤者), and eight *dou* of hot water, blending them thoroughly to submerge the cinnabar. Form clusters like rooster eggs, dry them in the shade, and refine them as before. The remaining steps follow the same method.

**Fourth Transformation (第四转):** Take the refined *Heaven’s* and *Earth’s Essence* from the previous three transformations, forming the elixir. Use twenty *catty* of fine, translucent, and radiant vermilion (朱砂), cook it in wine for twenty-one days (三七日), then pound it in a mortar and mix it with the medicine. Again, blend it with *Earth’s Strong Juice*—that is, cow dung juice (地强汁)—and form clusters like rooster eggs. Dry them in the shade, place them in the furnace, and refine them as before. All subsequent steps follow the same method as the nine transformations, but the medicinal ingredients differ.

**Fifth Transformation (第五转):** Take five *catty* of realgar with the color of a rooster’s comb (雄黄色如鸡冠者), boil it in genuine cow tallow (真牛酥) for seven days, then expose it to the sun. Mix it with the medicine as before. Then, combine one *dou* of wine and one *dou* of cow dung juice, blend them with the medicine to form clusters like rooster eggs, and dry them in the shade. Refine them as before; the remaining steps follow the same method.

**Sixth Transformation (第六转):** Take twenty *catty* of orpiment (雌黄) and five *catty* of *Wu* yellow alum (吴黄矾石), mix them with cow’s milk and hemp seed juice (麻子汁), and boil them for three days and nights. Dry them in the shade, pound and sift them, then blend with the medicine. Form clusters like rooster eggs with cow dung juice, dry them in the shade, and refine them as before.

**Seventh Transformation (第七转):** Take five *catty* of refined *stone green vitriol* (石曾青), along with one hundred cloves each of *dried ginger* (香附) and *white ginger* (白附), using fresh ones for better results. The remaining steps follow the same method as above.

**Eighth Transformation (第八转):** Take three *catty* of *martial salt* (戎盐), three *catty* of *crude sodium sulfate* (朴硝), and three *catty* of *mirabilite* (芒硝). Pound and sift them together with the medicine, then blend with cow dung juice to form clusters like rooster eggs. Dry them in the shade and refine them as before.

**Ninth Transformation (第九转):** Take the elixir from the previous eight transformations and place it according to the method on the *vital points of a person’s body* (其人生命上) and on *royal officials* (王相上). Establish an altar and perform rites of exorcism and sacrifice (立坛醮祭) as per the *Daoist Canon of the Divine Elixir* (丹经), maintaining purity through fasting and abstinence (洁清斋戒). Place the *Five Sacred Talismans of the Spirit Jewel* (灵宝五符) in the five cardinal directions, the *Twelve Divine Seals* (十二神印符) at the *hour of the day* (辰上), and the *Eight Sacred Talismans* (八灵符) in the eight cardinal directions. Cover the *Heavenly Gate* (天门), seal the *Earthly Portal* (地户), pass over the *Celestial Canopy* (华盖), and enter the *Yin realm* (阴中). Grind five *catty* of white jade into powder (为粉), and one *catty* of gold into flakes (为屑). Use the heart and liver of a green goat (青羊心肝各一具) to mix with the medicine and plaster the furnace. Blend the mixture with cow dung juice like rooster eggs and place it on the *vital points of a person’s body*. Dry it in the shade. When the *Heavenly Heart* (天心) aligns with the *Day of the Heavenly Heart* (天心日) and the *Hour of the Heavenly Heart* (天心时), place the refined elixir in the *Nine Palaces* (九宫) and mix it with the medicine. The attendant should remain in the *Central Palace* (中宫) tending the furnace.

First, it is said: *"The miraculous emergence from the palace is the finest."* After three days and nights, the elixir is complete. Form it into pills with white honey (丸以白蜜), and take two pills daily, each the size of a millet grain (如黍米粒). This can make one a *Supreme Daoist* (真人矣). Keep this secret and do not divulge it.

The scribe notes: Though this method involves nine transformations and adds hidden secrecy, the lead refined through nine transformations becomes a divine medicine (体为神药). Furthermore, the use of five *catty* of white jade as powder and one *catty* of gold as flakes—these two rare treasures—mixed and plastered onto the furnace, along with the heart and liver of a green goat (which are extremely difficult to obtain), and the milk of a firstborn son (首男乳汁) requiring ten *sheng* of measurement, is merely exaggerated for effect. The true method is to use obtainable medicines and complete the nine transformations. With this refined lead and elixir, fulfilling the *Nine Cauldrons* (九鼎), the Dao becomes even more wondrous, and its power even greater. Thus, the full account of its efficacy is presented, though it need not be laboriously detailed here.

**The Daoist Canon of the Divine Elixir of the Yellow Emperor (黄帝九鼎神丹经诀) – Volume Twelve Complete, Volume Thirteen**

**The Function and Potency of Cinnabar for Immortalizing the Dao (明丹砂功力能人长生之道用)**

The scribe notes: Medicines from grasses and woods can treat and cure illnesses but cannot achieve true longevity (不可以致长生也). Medicines from metals and minerals can certainly extend one’s lifespan and also eliminate a hundred evils (兼能除百邪也). Now, grasses and woods—being light, fragile, and easily damaged—cannot endure long. Boiled, they rot; buried, they decay; burned, they turn to ash; and left idle, they spoil.

「不能自坚，岂能坚人乎。不能自生，岂能生人乎。若丹砂之为物也，是称奇石，最为上药。细理红润，其质贞固坚秘，积转逾久，变化逾妙。

**The Daoist Canon of the Divine Elixir of the Yellow Emperor (黄帝九鼎神丹经诀) – Volume Twelve Complete, Volume Thirteen**

**The Function and Potency of Cinnabar for Immortalizing the Dao (明丹砂功力能人长生之道用)**

The scribe notes: It cannot fortify itself, how could it fortify others? It cannot sustain its own life, how could it give life to others? As for cinnabar (丹砂), it is called a wondrous mineral (奇石), the supreme among all medicines (上药). Its fine texture is vibrant red, its essence pure and enduring, firm yet mysterious—with time, its transformations grow ever more marvelous. It can ascend as powder (飞为粉), condense into essence as snow (精为雪), transmute into true mercury (为真汞), and become the elixir of return (还丹). It can repel fire (拒火) and dissolve into water (化水), yet when refined, it remains undiminished (消之可以不耗), and when buried, it does not spoil (埋之可以不坏). Its spiritual efficacy is wondrous and mysterious; I cannot fully describe it. To grasp its essence is to achieve full vitality (全生), but to fail in its method is to harm one’s lifespan (失法则伤寿).

**The Nature and Properties of Cinnabar for Healing (丹砂性味主疗)**

The scribe notes: The *Bencao* (本草) states that cinnabar (丹砂) is of sweet taste and slightly cold in nature, non-toxic, and governs the treatment of bodily ailments in the five viscera (五藏), a hundred diseases (百病), nourishes the spirit (精神), calms the soul and vital essence (魂魄), augments *qi* (氣) and illuminates the eyes (明目), harmonizes the blood vessels (通血脉), and alleviates vexation and thirst (止烦懑消渴). It also replenishes vitality (益精), enhances complexion (悦泽人面), wards off malevolent spirits and impurities (煞精邪恶鬼), dispels internal afflictions, intestinal pain (除中恶肠痛), and poisons such as scabies, eczema, and sores (毒气疥瘦诸疮). Prolonged consumption grants divine insight (通神明), prevents aging (不老), lightens the body (轻身), and achieves transcendence (神仙). It can transmute into mercury (化为汞), be ground into powder (调作末), and is known as true pearl (真珠), its luster resembling cloud mother (云母), and the best is that which can be broken apart. It grows in the valleys of the **Fengling Mountains (符陵山)**, and should be harvested at the **Yuan season (元时)**.*」

**On Cinnabar (丹砂) and Its Properties**

Cinnabar (恶磁石) fears saltwater. When it transforms into mercury (化为汞) and is called *true pearl* (真珠), it is also known as *golden sand* (金沙). The *Fengling Mountains* (符陵) refer to *Fuling* (涪陵), bordering the southern reaches of *Bajun* (巴郡)—now known as *Yuan* (元复采者).

**Sources of Cinnabar (丹砂出处):**
According to *Bencao* (《本草》), it is found in *Fuling* (符陵). Yet, since it is mined from the southern prefecture of *Bajun*, it is also called *Basha* (巴沙). Now, it is still harvested there, as well as in *Wuling* (武陵) and the *Xichuan* (西川) regions among the non-Han peoples. In ancient times, the *Ba* region was accessible, hence its name *Basha*. Daoist scriptures also use *Yuesha* (越沙), which comes from *Lindeng* (临邓) in *Guangzhou* (广州). These two sources are both excellent, provided their luster is bright and radiant.

If it resembles *cloud mother* (云母) in flakes, it is called *cloud mother sand* (云母沙). If it appears as *purple stone* (紫石) in larger forms, it is called *horse-tooth cinnabar* (马齿砂). All are of good quality and may be used in medicine, though they are not the finest material for refining.

If it forms large, smooth, bean-like masses, it is called *bean sand* (豆沙). If it is finely powdered and fragmented, it is called *powder sand* (末沙). These two varieties are inferior and are only suitable for grinding into vermilion (可磨作朱). Mining cinnabar always involves digging deep pits—even within the same prefecture or county, its quality varies. The methods for selecting and refining it are meticulously recorded, for the elixir of longevity is not fully detailed in *Bencao*.

Yet, though cinnabar is mined in *Ba* and *Chu* (巴楚), the finest today comes from *Maya County* (麻阳县) in *Zhenzhou* (辰州). When broken, it emits a fiery glow, with sparks resembling fireflies. When held to the light, it shimmers like moving luminous sand. If its texture is fine and it emits a brilliant white radiance when struck, it is called *cinnabar* (丹砂). The most superior is bright red, followed by purple, with muddy red being the lowest grade.

Heavenly cinnabar, already infused with fire, is rarely seen—even if obtained, it must first be subdued by fire. There is a variety from *Xingzhou* (兴州) that is dense and heavy, red in color, resembling cinnabar in appearance. When broken, it looks like iron; when burned, it turns red; when left exposed, it darkens; when heated, it does not melt—this is the true essence of cinnabar.

**Refining Methods for Cinnabar (丹砂调炼法):**

1. Take the finest cinnabar, grind it into powder, and place it in an iron vessel with the finest vinegar (上上醋). Simmer it over low heat, adding vinegar as needed without letting it run dry. After thirty-six days—or longer if it has not yet been subdued by fire—test it by burning. If it does not melt, it is refined. If not subdued, extend the process to a hundred days.

2. Use a *dou* (斗) of fine spring wine, place it in a porcelain jar, and add ten *liang* (两) of cinnabar in a silk pouch, ensuring it does not settle at the bottom. Replace the wine every ten days. After a hundred days, dry it in the sun and use it for longevity.

3. Another method: Take luminous, translucent cinnabar, boil it in wine for twenty-one days or more, then test it by fire to ensure it is subdued.

4. Another method: Crush cinnabar into bean-sized pieces, mix it with wine, and place it in a bamboo tube, then boil it in a pot. After half a day of heating, test its subduction by fire. If not yet refined, add water and boil again.

5. Another method: Take the finest cinnabar, place it in an iron vessel, and simmer it gently. Gradually add vinegar while stirring with a tool to prevent settling. For every *jin* (斤) of cinnabar, use a *dou* of vinegar. Once the vinegar is fully consumed and the cinnabar is extracted, dry it in the sun, place it in a sweet clay crucible, and refine it in a furnace. If it does not vaporize, it is complete. If it does vaporize, boil it for three more days and test again, repeating until success.

6. Another method: Take the finest cinnabar, crush it into bean-sized pieces, and place it in a copper vessel with strong vinegar. Simmer gently, gradually adding vinegar while stirring to prevent settling. Once the vinegar is fully consumed, dry it in the sun, then refine it by fire. If it does not vaporize, it is complete.

7. Another method: Take luminous, translucent cinnabar, grind it finely, and place it in a new earthenware bottle, sealing it tightly. Boil it in a pot for a hundred days to remove toxicity. This refined cinnabar is suitable for longevity. Alternatively, place it in a bottle with wine, which also prevents water contamination. Mixing it with wine ensures proper absorption into the bottle or pot.

8. Another method: Take bright, translucent cinnabar, grind it finely, and boil it in vinegar for a hundred days. When refined by fire without melting, it is called *subdued by fire* (伏火). This is used for alchemical transformations, not longevity.

**Reflections on Refining (臣诀者按):**
Though there are many methods for refining cinnabar, the key lies in ensuring it is *subdued by fire* (伏火). Ancient practitioners considered the varying intensity of fire, hence the use of prolonged boiling. They also accounted for human impatience, setting a limit of a hundred days. For longevity elixirs, it must be boiled in fine wine. For alchemical transformations, it must be boiled in strong vinegar.

When boiling in iron with wine, constant stirring is required. If placed in a bottle, it must be sealed tightly. After fully consuming the vinegar, remove and dry it, then test for subduction by fire. New bottles are preferred for longevity preparations, while copper or iron vessels are used for alchemical work. These methods are infallible.

**Alternative Method for Consuming Cinnabar (服丹砂别法):**
Take two *jin* of cinnabar, grind it into powder, sift it through fine silk, and place it in a copper basin. Pour strong, bitter wine over it until it forms a paste. Leave it in a dry, elevated place to dry. Repeat the process, using three *dou* of wine for every *jin* of cinnabar. After thirty days of drying, the mixture will turn purple—this is the completed medicine. It will not stain the hands when handled and will be malleable like honey.

Form it into pills the size of sesame seeds. Take three pills daily with spring water upon waking. After one day, intestinal parasites will be expelled. After six days, all bodily ailments will vanish. After sixty days, one will gain supernatural vision, regrow black hair where gray has been, and regenerate fallen teeth.

**Methods of Consuming Cinnabar (服丹砂别法):**

Before taking this medicine, one must first observe a thirty-day fast and purification, bathing with water infused with five kinds of fragrant aromatics before ingestion.

**Method of Consuming Cinnabar (服丹砂法):**
Take one *jin* of cinnabar, pound it into powder, and sift it. Add two *sheng* of refined lacquer and three *sheng* of strong, bitter wine, blending these three substances harmoniously. Simmer gently over fire until it can be formed into pills the size of sesame seeds, to be taken three times daily.

After ten days, all hundred ailments will be cured, and the Three Vermin (*sān shī*) will be expelled.
It is also said: After a hundred days of consumption, the skin will grow firm; after three years, longevity will be prolonged.

The scholar notes: Cinnabar alone, taken in isolation over time, still yields benefits as described above.
When the poison is removed by steaming in a clay vessel, and it is combined into the Great Elixir (*dà dān*), its efficacy is greatly enhanced.

Now, examining the previous methods of cinnabar alone and the two methods of blending with lacquer—all using refined vinegar, none mentioning wine—it is evident that the efficacy may be doubted if wine is omitted.

Additionally, there is a method where cinnabar is steeped in a clay bottle without needing vinegar.

According to the alternative method of blending cinnabar with lacquer, take one *jin* of true cinnabar, one *dou* of clear wine, one *jin* of white honey, and one *sheng* of refined lacquer. Steep the cinnabar daily in wine and honey, soaking and drying repeatedly until it can be formed into pills, then cease.

Another prescription: Blend cinnabar with clear wine, place it in a bamboo tube, and steam it for several days, as with the method of steeping and drying cinnabar. Form the mixture into pills with white honey.

Yet another method: Mix cinnabar with the juice of mulberry roots, place it in a bottle, and immerse it in boiling water for two days and nights. Then blend with refined wine and form into pills with white honey.

In all the blending methods above, first harmonize the cinnabar with wine until perfectly adjusted, then add the lacquer and steam it over the gentlest flame possible. Once it can be formed into pills, stop.

In the consumption method above, form the pills the size of sesame seeds. Initially, take two pills, twice daily. After forty days, the Three Vermin will depart; prolonged consumption leads to longevity and immortality, where one’s shadow is no longer visible at midday.

Thus, it is known that among all methods of refining cinnabar to remove its poison, none surpass the use of fine wine.

Some methods involve storing cinnabar in a new clay bottle, others in a bamboo tube. In either case, it must first be blended with clear wine.
It can be steamed or steeped; however,
Steaming requires continuous fire for a hundred days, and bamboo tubes may rot.
Steeping for a hundred days poses difficulties in maintaining uniform moisture due to varying hand dryness—how can it compare to storing it in a new clay bottle?
The wine’s vapor permeates and clarifies the cinnabar; the bottle absorbs and evenly moistens it, constantly nourishing it without effort. A single steaming session suffices to complete it.

The scholar notes: Among all minerals, only cinnabar and realgar are superior. Their refining methods are not overly difficult; combining them first to safeguard one’s life and vitality is also the foundation of essential elixirs for prolonging existence. Though not yet attaining the Great Elixir, no other supplementary medicines or tonics can rival this.

Moreover, the spirit of cinnabar is called mercury (*shuǐ yín*). When mercury is blended with cinnabar in equal parts and pounded together, placed in a copper vessel, and steamed for a day and night, it emerges as a watery substance. When placed over charcoal and heated, it becomes water—thus, it should appear purple-red. Form into honey pills the size of a bean, and its potency after a hundred days will be similar to that of cinnabar.

**Conclusion of *Huángdì Jiǔ Dǐng Shén Dān Jīng Jué*, Volume 13.**
**Beginning of *Huángdì Jiǔ Dǐng Shén Dān Jīng Jué*, Volume 14.**

**Refining Realgar (雄黄) Method**

The efficacy of realgar lies in its power to attain longevity. According to my study: realgar and orpiment share the same origin, for orpiment transforms into realgar. Orpiment is called the great medicine of Heaven and Earth, and after eight thousand years, it transmutes into realgar—also known as *Dì Nán Jīng* (帝男精, "Imperial Male Essence"). After another thousand years, it further refines into gold, named *Zhēn Rén Fàn* (真人饭, "True Person’s Nourishment"), making it the most divine of stones.

For those who seek only to preserve their teeth from falling, prevent their hair from graying, strengthen sinews and bones, lighten the body, and sharpen vision, no remedy surpasses this elixir. It repels tigers, wolves, and a hundred poisons, keeping them at bay. When immersed in water, it fears no water dragons, and no venomous creatures or malevolent spirits dare approach. It also wards off the Five Weapons, possessing great might. It sharpens the senses, commands the spirits of a hundred beings, and is a singular marvel of divine transformation—the supreme elixir of longevity, the essential remedy for ailments, and the means to restore youth. No substance is beyond its influence.

In ancient times, the *Yuánqiū* (圆丘) altar was plagued by great serpents, yet it also bore fine medicines. When the Yellow Emperor prepared to ascend there, Master Guāngchéngzǐ (广成子) instructed him to wear realgar, and all the serpents departed. This demonstrates its immense power. Moreover, in the Daoist scriptures, realgar stands alone as the greatest of medicines.

**Realgar’s Therapeutic Uses**
According to the *Běn Cǎo* (本草): Realgar is bitter, sweet, and of a neutral, cold nature, with toxicity. It treats cold and fever, rodent paralysis, carbuncles, boils, hemorrhoids, dead flesh, scabies, hidden sores, eye pain, nasal polyps, severed sinews, shattered bones, wind accumulation in the joints, malignant abdominal pain, ghostly possession, malevolent spirits, evil *qi*, venomous creatures, and the poisons of the Five Weapons. It repels all serpents and viper venom, enhances complexion, and when refined and ingested, lightens the body and grants immortality. When taken as a medicine, it ascends directly to the brain, overcoming ghosts and spirits, prolonging life, and sustaining the body without hunger. It is also called *Huáng Shí* (黄食石, "Yellow Nourishment Stone").

**Realgar’s Sources**
According to my study: Realgar grows in the valleys of Wúdū (武都) and the slopes of *Dùnhuáng* (炖煌, *Dunhuang*). It may be gathered at any time, with the finest specimens resembling a rooster’s comb in color—firm, odorless, and solid. Those that are dull, black, or hollow are inferior.

The realgar from *Dùnhuáng*, located thousands of miles west of *Dòngzhōu* (冻州), is considered the most vital and rare of medicines. In the past, it was valued equally with red gold. Now, under the enlightened rule of the Holy Dynasty, with the world unified and no rebellions, treasures no longer hide in the earth, nor do mountains conceal their riches. The cliffs of Wúdū collapse daily, yielding realgar like the sun’s rays, transported to the capital without cost—its value exceeding even that of laborers’ wages, reduced to the price of tiles and stones. This is the blessing of a sage ruler in harmony with the Dao, a divine medicine of fortune, arriving without seeking.

Realgar of a murky red hue is inferior. Only the pure, bright red is supreme.

「**Methods for Refining Realgar to Remove Its Toxicity**

The humble servant observes: Though realgar is a supreme medicine for longevity (*chángshēng*), it possesses great toxicity. If its poison is not fully removed, it cannot be used in the *Great Elixir* (*Dà Dān*). The toxicity of mineral medicines intensifies with fire; even a hundredfold submerged fire (*fùhuǒ*—a method of detoxification) fails to eliminate the poison entirely.

Ordinary people, failing to grasp its true nature, mistakenly believe that substances which replace fire are free of toxicity—a grave error indeed. Therefore, one must first boil and refine it before subjecting it to fire.

This process resembles the detoxification of cinnabar (*gōngzhú*), for realgar can be refined either with vinegar or oil. Depending on its intended use, the methods differ, as detailed below.

**Method of Refining Realgar with Alcohol and Boiling in Vinegar**
Take the finest realgar, ten *jīn* in weight. Remove its stony veins (*shípài*), crush it into pieces the size of small *mùzi* (a measure, roughly a pea), or grind it into powder like sand, or pulverize it into dust like flour. If refining with oil, crush it into *mùzi*-sized pieces. If refining with alcohol, crush it into powder, then soak it thoroughly in good-quality wine within a copper vessel. Stir until fully saturated, then add more wine until two *dàn* (a measure, roughly 100 liters) are used.

Next, boil it with oil. After removing the oil, crush it into powder, and incorporate it into the *Great Elixir*. Alternatively, refine it with bitter wine until complete.

For those who wish to take it alone: Grind it into fine powder, place it in a bamboo tube, and add one *jīn* of *shìyú* (a type of salted brine or mineral solution). Cover the tube with a stone lid, seal its mouth tightly, and steam it in sand for seven days and nights. When removed, if there is liquid, drain it. The residue that does not dissolve in water should be placed in a silk pouch, stored in a honey jar, sealed securely, and buried in horse dung for seven days. When the process is complete, the medicine is formed, known as *Zǐgōng Fēi Dān* (Purple Palace Flying Elixir). Roll it into pills the size of white honey beans (*báimì*), and taking them over time will extend one’s years.

**Method of Refining Realgar with Vinegar**
Refine realgar with vinegar: Take one *jīn* of the finest realgar, crush it into powder, and mix it with good-quality bitter wine. Combine thoroughly in a copper vessel and simmer gently over low fire (*huǎnhuǒ*), never with fierce flames, until one *dàn* of wine is fully consumed. The refined mixture will resemble glue.

*Formula’s Note:* This "bitter wine" is not vinegar but rather a strong, aged wine.

After boiling, crush it into powder and place it in a bamboo tube. Steam it for one day and night. When the vapor turns greenish-red (*qīngchì*), remove it and place it in water. The residue will clump like cotton; roll it into pills the size of *wúzi* (a measure, roughly a walnut). Take one pill before meals, three times daily, and one will attain the state of the *Immortal* (*shénxiān*).

If realgar is mixed with lacquer (*qī*) for ingestion, use good-quality clear wine instead. Simmer it gently over low fire until it thickens like glue. For one *jīn* of realgar, use two *jīn* of lacquer, ensuring the lacquer is fresh and green. After boiling and straining, discard the dregs (*zhé*), and blend the mixture in a copper vessel until thoroughly combined. The medicine is now complete.

Roll it into pills the size of millet grains (*shúmǐ*), and take three daily. If rolled into smaller pills the size of adzuki beans (*xiǎodòu*), take one daily. Before ingestion, chew the pill and swallow the juice, discarding the residue. After fourteen days, all ailments will be cured. After twenty days, the skin will become supple and the dead flesh will slough off—this is the effect of the medicine’s power.

Walking at night will be like daytime; movement will be swift as a flying dragon. In cold weather, the body will feel warm; in heat, it will feel cool. After a hundred days, the intestines will be firm and strong, the skin and blood vessels resilient, and the bones, joints, ears, and eyes sharp and clear.

By three hundred days, one may gradually increase the dosage to swallowing pills the size of millet and sorghum grains (*shúsu*), with three pills as the daily norm. This method is divine and secret; do not casually divulge it.

Though called the *Lesser Elixir* (*xiǎodān*), it surpasses all other minerals and superior herbs of the earth. Before the *Great Elixir* is complete, one must first use this medicine to fortify the marrow (*guīsùi*), sustaining oneself.

If this refined realgar is to be incorporated into the *Great Elixir*, it must be boiled for a full hundred days, never stopping until it thickens like glue.

**Method of Refining Realgar for Longevity Medicines**
After soaking and removing it, let the realgar dry thoroughly in the sun. Grind it into fine powder for use. Select the brightest, most luminous red pieces, crush them into powder, and place them in a new earthenware bottle. Soak the powder in wine, seal the bottle tightly, and boil it in a steamer for a hundred days. Alternatively, place the wine in the pot and boil the bottle within it—this method is superior.

This is for use in longevity medicines and elixir preparations. Take one *shēng* (a measure, roughly 3.78 liters) of good spring wine, pour it into a porcelain jar (*bìgāng*), and place ten *liǎng* (a measure, roughly 37.5 grams) of realgar in a white cloth pouch within the jar. Replace the wine every ten days, continuing for a hundred days total.

**Method of Refining Realgar for Transmuting Copper and Iron**
Take the finest realgar with a rooster-crest hue (*jīguān sè*). In a copper vessel, boil it with good, pure vinegar for a hundred days. Test its detoxification by submerging it in fire without residue (*wúyīn*—indicating complete removal of toxicity). When successful, it is called *Fùhuǒ* (Subdued Fire). It can then be used to transmute and perfect metals instantly.

**Method of Heavy Refining with Oil: Removing Realgar’s Impurities**
Take the finest realgar with a rooster-crest hue, select its purest parts, and remove the stony veins. Crush it into pieces the size of small *mùzi*. Boil these in an oil wok (*yóuchuán*).

First, refine it thoroughly with wine for a full day. Then, boil it in oil for nine days and nights without pause. Carefully monitor the heat—if the oil is too hot, the *fat flame* (*zhīyàn*) will rise, and if the heat is too slow, the poisonous *qi* will not dissipate.

Cover the wok with an earthenware lid and wait until the steam can be held in the palm (*tǎngshǒu*—a test for proper heat). When the days are complete and the oil is extremely hot, pour it out carefully, ensuring all oil is drained. The realgar will then solidify into a mass that does not fall. Pour it out while still very hot, straining the oil evenly. Use a silk pouch, each capable of holding two *jīn*, with five pouches totaling ten *jīn*, each pouch nine *cùn* (a measure, roughly 30 cm) long.

Alternatively, fashion a *soil cauldron* (*tǔ’áo*) from clay, one *chǐ* (a measure, roughly 30 cm) high, with an eight *cùn* mouth facing upward. On all four sides of the cauldron’s top, firmly attach small clay basins (*huò*), shaped like earthenware jars (*tǔ’ōu*), and fill them with sand. Place the realgar pouches on the sand, ensuring each pouch is spaced one *cùn* apart, and fill the cauldron with sand until it is level with the pouches’ tops. Below the sand, arrange seven bundles of firewood, and observe the pouches until the fat is fully absorbed by the sand.

**Method of Relocating Refined Realgar’s Toxicity**
After steaming and refining with sand, place the realgar in a new earthenware bottle. Wrap the bottle tightly with sweet clay mud (*gāntǔ ní*), half an inch thick, and bake it until dry. Seal the bottle’s mouth with a competing substance (*zhēngwù*—likely a stopper or sealant), and weigh it down in a fixed location. First, mold a clay shape resembling the bottle or jar.

The mouth of this clay shape should be thick like the side of a palm, and its height like a clenched fist. Fill it with white sand, pressing it firmly until full. Place it in a furnace and dry it thoroughly.

**Method of Transmuting Realgar’s Toxicity with Lacquer**
Take the refined realgar from the sand-steaming process, wrap it in a white cloth pouch, and place it in a new earthenware bottle. Seal the bottle tightly with clay mud, ensuring it is half an inch thick, and bake it until dry. Use a lacquer (*qī*) mixture to cover the bottle’s mouth, and weigh it down in a fixed location.

First, mold a clay shape resembling the bottle or jar. The mouth of this clay shape should be thick like the side of a palm, and its height like a clenched fist. Fill it with white sand, pressing it firmly until full. Place it in a furnace and dry it thoroughly.

「Then, invert the bottle’s mouth over the clay shape, plug the bottle’s mouth with disordered hair, and spread a layer of paper on the sand. Secure it with small iron nails across the mouth to block the hair, ensuring the oil vapor descends and the medicine does not spill chaotically.

Once the bottle is settled, wait until it is thoroughly dry, then fill and tamp it with horse dung. Ignite the fire from above, allowing it to burn downward so that the bottle’s oil vapor drips onto the sand and gradually dissipates. After a day and night, when the vapor has subsided (*when the bottle is clear*), retrieve it.

While still hot, use tongs to hold the bottle upright, remove its mouth, and pierce a hole the size of a *Confucius* (小孔). The medicine inside the bottle will appear like turbid water. Cast it into vessels of any desired shape or size—this is called *wu yin* (無姻), a substance that repels evil.

If the vapor is not fully exhausted, break the bottle and collect the residue. The oil will be gone, and only the medicine remains, with all toxic vapors eliminated.

To consume it directly, those who immediately obtain it should sift it into powder, take three *turns of snow* (三转雪), steam it for three days, and form it into pills with white honey. Then, swallow it like a pea-sized pill.

Take three doses daily, gradually reducing the amount, to expel the three kinds of worms (*三虫*) and achieve longevity (*longsheng/long life*).

Mixing it with refined pine resin (*song zhi*) is also beneficial. This method can be used to produce multiple doses for consumption.

**Method of Refining Pine Resin**
If using mulberry ash (*sang hui*) or lime juice (*shi hui zhi*), boil it repeatedly, then rinse with water until all bitterness is removed.

**Method of Refining Orpiment**
According to my notes: The method of refining orpiment (*qí huáng*) differs little from that of realgar (*xióng huáng*). However, as *Bencao* (《本草》) states: Its medicinal efficacy differs from realgar. When making *Da Dan* (大丹, Great Elixir), this substance is especially required, hence its inclusion here.

Orpiment (*qí huáng*) is sweet, spicy, and balanced in nature, yet has toxicity. It treats malignant sores, baldness, ringworm, and scabies; kills poisonous insects and mites; alleviates itching; dispels all malevolent *qi*; removes nasal polyps; cures lower-body sores; eliminates white patches on the skin; revives deadened flesh; and counteracts dizziness and evil *qi*, neutralizing the venom of bees and snakes.

When refined, it lightens the body, prolongs life without aging, and fills one’s mind with clarity (*nǎo mǎn*—lit. "brain full"). It is mined from the same mountains as realgar, both found in the valleys of *Wudu* (武都), specifically in the yin-facing slopes. Where there is gold, the essence of gold refined by heat produces orpiment.

It can be gathered at any time. From *Wudu’s* *Chouchi* (仇池), it is yellow with a slight reddish hue. If sourced from *Funan* (扶南) or *Linyi* (林邑) in the south, it is called *true Kunlun* (真昆仑), yellow in color like gold, yet with a luster resembling mica, highly prized by painters.

Yet in alchemical practice, it is often combined with realgar in sublimation, sharing its yin-yang distinction. When used alongside realgar, the orpiment from *Wudu* is superior.

The best quality contains white, firm, and lustrous veins within its fracture.

---
*(The following is the end of Volume XIV of the *Huangdi Jiuding Shendan Jingjue* (黃帝九鼎神丹經訣). The next volume, Volume XV, discusses the essence and spiritual potency of various stones.)*

---
*『列』* is supplemented according to the text’s meaning.

**On the Virtue and Power of Stone Orpiment**

**Stone Orpiment’s Efficacy**
The scribe notes: Stone orpiment can transmute gold, silver, copper, and iron. Daoist scriptures frequently employ it. When burned, it yields a violet vapor, while its yellow and white residues are essential for cutting substances—thus its necessity in alchemical methods. When submerged in mercury, it is called *huángníngshā* (黄秾沙). With nitre, it transforms into liquid. This method derives from the *Thirty-Six Water Methods Scripture*.

Another method: grind stone orpiment into powder, place it in a bamboo tube, and thin its outer layer. Bury it in horse dung for twenty days, and it will liquefy. This liquid, when applied to elixirs, is called *liúhuáng yè* (流黄液). To refine it, take the finest *guāngmíngshā* (光明砂), steep and decoct it in wine, then grind it. Mix with orpiment in a copper vessel, simmer gently, and boil in repeated batches—this yields the best result. After seven to eight days, its color changes; by ten days, it becomes paste-like, forming pills the size of *wútóng* seeds (梧桐子). Take three daily, gradually increasing to forty. With prolonged use, one achieves lightness and may ascend to Dao.

This is the virtue and power of orpiment.

**Stone Orpiment’s Therapeutic Uses**
The scribe notes: Stone orpiment is sour and warm, with toxicity. It treats:
- Female genital parasites,
- Ulcers, hemorrhoids, and malignant blood,
- Rigid sinews, baldness, abdominal masses,
- Pathogenic *ling* (玲, a TCM term for stagnant or harmful energy),
- Inverted breathing and upward-rising *qi*,
- Weak, painful legs lacking strength,
- Nasal polyps and malignant sores,
- Lower-body ulcers, wound healing, and scabies eradication.

Folk remedies favor it for leg weakness and *ling*-related ailments. The scribe further notes: *Shíliúhuángdān* (石流黄丹) is the red essence of stone, akin to but distinct from orpiment itself. It seeps between cliffs, and when damp, may be pill-formulated; when solid, it is powdered. This singular stone encompasses one hundred twenty varieties, though their names exist without visual confirmation—yet it ranks among the supreme Daoist elixirs. The Five Sacred Peaks possess it, with *Jīshān* (箕山) being most abundant. Folklore claims *Xǔ Yóu* (许由) consumed it to attain longevity, thus rejecting imperial offerings and declining Yao’s abdication.

**Origins of Stone Orpiment**
The scribe notes: Orpiment grows in the valleys of *Shùhǎi* (束海, modern Xu Province), *Mùyángshān* (牧阳山), *Tàishān* (泰山), and the *Héxī* (河西) mountains. It is the essence of alum stone. Though *Shùhǎi* belongs to Xu Province, *Jīshān* also yields it. Today, the finest comes from *Fúnán* and *Línyí* (林邑), resembling a parrot freshly hatched—named *Kūnlún huáng* (昆仑黄), deep in hue and superior. This variety is prized in folk remedies for leg weakness and *ling*-related disorders. However, for high-alchemy (*dàdān*), *Línyí* orpiment cannot surpass that of Xu Province or *Jīshān*. Since the south lacks alum, its classification as "alum essence" remains unclear.

**Refining Stone Orpiment for Longevity Elixirs**
The scribe notes: The *Jiǔxiāo Jūn* (九霄君) prescribes a nine-fold lead elixir, incorporating orpiment into longevity formulas. The four key ingredients—*zhūshā* (朱砂, cinnabar), *xiónghuáng* (雄黄, realgar), *cíhuáng* (雌黄, orpiment), and *liúhuáng*—are each decocted separately in wine over gentle heat. For every five *shāng* (升) of wine, steep five *liǎng* (两) of powder, ensuring gradual saturation without abrupt addition. This prepares the elixir for longevity.

Alternative method: crush orpiment to the size of large beans, place in a bamboo tube with vinegar, and boil for three days and nights, resting halfway before adding water. Though effective for transformation, wine decoction surpasses it.

**On the Virtue and Power of *Céngqīng* (曾青) in Longevity Elixirs**
The scribe notes: *Céngqīng* ranks among the supreme Daoist elixirs. Prolonged consumption lightens the body and prevents aging. It transmutes copper, iron, and lead into gold.

**Therapeutic Uses of *Céngqīng***
The scribe notes: *Céngqīng* is sour, slightly cold, and non-toxic. It treats:
- Eye pain and excessive tearing,
- Wind-induced numbness, joint mobility,
- Dissolving masses and stagnations,
- Nourishing the liver and gallbladder,
- Alleviating cold-heat imbalances,
- Eradicating white parasites,
- Migraines and brain coldness,
- Abdominal distension and *yáng* deficiency.

**Origins of *Céngqīng***
The scribe notes: *Céngqīng* is found in Shù and Yùe’s valleys, harvested year-round. It shares properties with *kōngqīng* (空青, azurite) but avoids silk moth cocoons. Today, it is sourced from *Shǐxīng* (始兴) and *Wùzhōu* (蔚州), with *Wùzhōu* superior. Inferior varieties come from other regions. Its texture resembles earthworm droppings or *huánglián* (黄连, coptis), with slipperiness indicating quality. Its luster slightly surpasses *kōngqīng*, making it rare and costly. Daoist scriptures value it, though *Táo Yǐnjū* (陶隐居) deemed it scarce. Its gold-transmutation methods mirror those of *kōngqīng*.

**Refining *Céngqīng***
The scribe notes: Steep *céngqīng* in fine wine, place in a copper vessel, and cover with paper under sunlight. In summer, seven days suffice, though prolonged exposure enhances potency. Without sunlight, gentle heat suffices. Dry thoroughly, then grind in a porcelain mortar with a jade pestle until powdered. Mix with concentrated vinegar, adjusting moisture as needed.

Alternative method: seal *céngqīng* in a dense silk pouch, submerge in a porcelain jar with vinegar (ten *liǎng* of *céngqīng* to one *shāng* of vinegar), and suspend the pouch. Replace vinegar every ten days; after a hundred days, use one *dòu* (斗) of vinegar. The pouch must not touch the jar’s base.

Another method: refine *céngqīng* with *jīnjīng* (金精, gold essence) separately in porcelain, grinding each into powder. Steep with *sān zhuǎn zuǒ wèi* (三转左味, a three-fold left-alchemical agent) for two hundred days, dry, and pulverize in a porcelain basin with a jade pestle.

Final method: refine *céngqīng* as with orpiment—crush to bean size, place in a bamboo tube with vinegar, and boil for three days and nights, resting halfway before reheating.

This method is not unknown, but it is a hasty minor technique, insufficient for reliance.

Another method: crush into powder, then boil with *sān zhuǎn zuǒ wèi* (三转左味). For one *jīn* (斤) of *céngqīng*, use a gentle fire to exhaust five *dǒu* (斗) of vinegar, and stop.

Dry thoroughly and grind to completion; it is then ready for medicinal use.

**Refining Magnetite (磁石) Method**
This is also similar to refining *céngqīng*. This is the Nine-Heaven Lord’s (九霄君) Nine-Transformations Lead Elixir method. Though there are authoritative references, it is still inferior to the superior method of refining gold essence with *céngqīng* as described above.

**The Virtue and Power of *Kōngqīng* (空青)**
According to records: *Kōngqīng*, when taken over time, lightens the body, prolongs life, prevents aging, prevents forgetfulness in the elderly, and elevates one’s spirit toward immortality. It can also be used in elixir formulation—when refined, it transmutes lead into gold.

The *Shénnóng* [classic] states: *"It transmutes copper, iron, and lead into gold."*

Its therapeutic uses are also similar to *céngqīng*, with minor variations. The following are recorded as such:

**Therapeutic Uses of *Kōngqīng***
According to records: *Kōngqīng* is of sweet and sour taste, intensely cold, and non-toxic. It treats:
- *Qīngmáng* (青盲, visual impairment from cold)
- Deafness
- Clarifies vision
- Opens the nine orifices
- Circulates the blood vessels
- Nourishes the spirit
- Strengthens liver *qi*
- Treats red, painful eyes and skin ulcers
- Stops excessive tearing
- Facilitates urination
- Promotes lactation
- Unblocks joints
- Dissolves hardened accumulations

**Sources of *Kōngqīng***
According to records: *Kōngqīng* is found in the mountains and valleys of Yìzhōu (益州), as well as in Yuè (越) and Jùn (隽). Currently, the finest quality—deepest in color—comes from Tóngguān (同官). That from Shǐxīng (始兴) is inferior to that of Yìzhōu. In Dòngzhōu’s (冻州) Xīpíng (西平), there is also a *Kōngqīng* mountain with abundant deposits, though they are solid and round like iron beads, lacking hollow cavities. These are excavated from soil and stone without seasonal restrictions.

Now, with the Emperor’s virtuous governance, all things flourish. Thus, *Kōngqīng* is also found in Wèizhōu (蔚州), Jiǎnzhōu (简州), Xuānzhōu (宣州), and Zǐzhōu (梓州). Among these, Xuānzhōu’s is the finest. That from Wèizhōu is dense, block-like, and lacks pores.

**Refining *Kōngqīng* for Immortal Elixirs**
According to records: Crush *Kōngqīng* into powder and refine it like *céngqīng*, steeping it in alcohol for a hundred days before drying and re-crushing. Then mix with vinegar and dry it ten times. Essentially, the process aligns with that of *céngqīng*.

If refining *jiàngfán* (绛矾, red vitriol), simply steep *Kōngqīng* once in alcohol and dry it—no further repetition is needed.

**Refining *Shílù* (石碌) Method**
According to records: In current elixir formulations, this substance is unnecessary. However, the *Tāiyī Shénjīng* (太一神精) method for minor elixirs states: *"If *céngqīng* is unavailable, use *Kūnlún shílù* (昆仑石碌), grind it into powder, and extract its essence for use."*

Additionally, according to the *Běncǎo* [classic]: *"Shílù* grows within *Kōngqīng*, attached to it. It is also called *lùqīng* (碌青), with a sour, cold nature and no toxicity. It strengthens *qi*, treats liver and nasal disorders, stops diarrhea, and is found in mountain caves, colored greenish-white. It is used by painters for green pigments—artisans call it *bìqīng* (碧青, verdigris), while *Kōngqīng* is called *lǜqīng* (绿青, green malachite).

If substituting *céngqīng* in formulations, it must first be water-fly-purified. From ten *liǎng* of refined essence, three *liǎng* can be obtained. However, when refined like *Kōngqīng*, it is suitable only for minor elixirs. For major elixirs, it cannot replace other substances.

**End of Volume Fifteen of the *Huángdì Jiǔdǐng Shéndān Jīngjué* (黄帝九鼎神丹经诀)**
**Volume Sixteen of the *Huángdì Jiǔdǐng Shéndān Jīngjué***

**Volume Sixteen of the *Huángdì Jiǔdǐng Shéndān Jīngjué***

**On Refining Stones for Longevity**

**The Virtue and Power of Magnetite (Císhí 磁石)**
The scribe notes: Magnetite is counted among the Five Stones, the essence of Great Yin. Its taste is pungent and salty, cold in nature, and non-toxic. It neutralizes iron’s toxicity, yet is feared by cinnabar and liquid mercury. It is widely used in elixirs of yellow and white Daoist alchemy.

**Magnetite’s Therapeutic Uses**
The scribe notes: Magnetite treats wind-induced numbness, wind-dampness, aching joints that prevent holding objects, acidity and pain upon washing, dispels intense heat and fullness, cures deafness, nourishes the kidneys, strengthens stomach *qi*, augments essence, alleviates restlessness, frees the joints, dissolves atrophy and rodent ulcers, relieves stiff necks and sore throats, and calms infantile convulsions. When refined into water and ingested, it ensures fertility. It is also called *Xuànshí* (玄石) and *Chǔshí* (处石), with *Cháihú* (柴胡) as its messenger herb, while it is antagonized by peony and *mángcǎo* (莽草) and fears *huángshízhī* (yellow stone pitch).

**Magnetite’s Origins**
The scribe notes: Magnetite grows in the streams and valleys of Mount Tài, and on the sunlit slopes of *Císhān* (Magnetite Mountain) where iron is present. It may be harvested at any time. The finest specimens can suspend and attract needles, with three or four linked strands being optimal. Currently, the best quality is found in *Xiàngzhōu* (Relative State).

**Method for Refining Magnetite into Longevity Elixirs**
Take one *jīn* of magnetite for longevity formulations. Grind it into powder and boil with *zuǒwèi* (left-flavor vinegar) over gentle fire until five *shēng* of liquid remains. Remove and dry it; the residue is unusable.

**Alternative Refining Method**
For magnetite to be combined with *céngqīng* (blue vitriol), boil it in five *shēng* of vinegar. No soaking is required.
Another method states: Coarsely grind magnetite and boil it in bitter wine for three nights, after which it is ready for use.

---

**The Virtue and Power of Alum (Fánshí 礜石)**
The scribe notes: Alum is the essence of Lesser Yin, counted among the Five Stones. When refined and ingested, it grants immortality and eternal youth. In Daoist alchemy texts and yellow-white elixir formulas, it is highly prized. It softens gold and prevents water from freezing.

Also called *Qīngjièshí* (青介石), *Lìzhìshí* (立制石), *Gùyángshí* (固羊石), *Bái fánshí* (白礜石), *Tàibáishí* (太白石), *Zéirǔ* (泽乳), and *Shíyán* (石盐).

**Alum’s Therapeutic Uses**
The scribe notes: Alum’s taste is pungent and sweet, with intense heat and toxicity. It treats cold-heat disorders, rodent ulcers, dead flesh, wind-spleen, abdominal hardness, and pathogenic *qi*. It dispels heat, sharpens vision, descends rebellious *qi*, removes heat from the diaphragm, stops diabetes, benefits liver *qi*, dissolves accumulations, cures chronic alcoholism, alleviates cold abdominal pain, removes nasal polyps, and—when taken long-term—strengthens tendons. It thrives with fire but fears water, is antagonized by *dúgōng* (toad venom), and uses *xìxīn* (fine cinnamon) and *hǔzhǎng* (tiger paw) as messengers.

**Alum’s Origins**
The scribe notes: Alum grows in the mountains and valleys of *Hànzhōu* (Han Prefecture) and *Shàoshì* (Lesser Room Mountain). It may be harvested at any time. The finest specimens also come from *Shǔ Hàn* (Sichuan-Han), *Nán Yě* (Southern Wilds), the borders of *Péngchéng* (Peng City), and the southern walls of *Luòyáng* (Luoyang). Among these, the alum from *Shàoshì* is the hottest. If it resembles yellow clay and is half an inch thick, burning it with charcoal fire for a day and night will cause it to crack open, making it suitable for treating cold obstructions—but it cannot be used in major elixirs. The alum used by Daoists is specifically *Bái fánshí* (white alum), not ordinary alum.

**Method for Refining Alum into Longevity Elixirs**
The scribe notes: Alum is toxic and intensely hot, thriving with fire. Thus, the *Béncǎo* (Herbal Classic) states: It must be fire-refined for a hundred days before ingestion in pill form, as it can kill humans and beasts. If dissolved into water, it effectively neutralizes latent mercury.

**Refining Method**
Take the finest alum, grind it into powder, wrap it in paper to form pellets, and seal it in a kiln with yellow clay (thickened to half an inch). Build a furnace around it with charcoal and ignite for fourteen days. Once the drug has been used for a hundred days, its efficacy is superior. It may then be incorporated into yellow-white elixirs.

**Alternative Method**
Boil alum in *dǔzhī* (stacked fat) for seven nights, dry it, grind it, and soak it in bitter wine until it forms a paste. Mold it into a ball and subject it to fierce fire until it turns into copper. Then grind it into powder, mix it with refined mercury, and use it according to the formula.

**Nine-Heavens Lord’s Nine-Transformation Lead Elixir Method for Refining Alum**
Grind alum into powder, mix it with cow dung juice to form a paste, and place it in a furnace for a day and night. Remove it, pound it in a mortar, and regrind it until it is ready for substitution. Boil it in two *dòu* of water, reducing it to five *shēng*, then let it cool overnight. It should congeal slightly before removal. Use three *dòu* of three-year-old bitter wine, boil it three times, and store it in a sealed vessel with a clay lid. After fourteen days, if the surface forms a two-*fēn* thick crust, use the refined *pǔxiāo* (crude natron) essence to cover the *Tàiyī Zhāohún Dān* (Great Unity Summon-Soul Elixir) and the congealed mercury. Refine this into the essence for longevity elixirs—its potency far surpasses unrefined alum.

---

**The Virtue and Power of Mirabilite (Mángxiāo 芒硝)**
The scribe notes: Mirabilite is refined from crude natron (*pǔxiāo*). Thus, the *Shénnóng Běnjīng* (Divine Farmer’s Classic) lists only natron, not mirabilite—yet mirabilite possesses transformative power. Hence, *Péng Jūn* (Master Peng) says: True natron, military salt, stone bile, and mirabilite—though they may have yin-yang or orthodox variations—exhibit divine efficacy in their transformations. If one seeks immortality without mastering this method, they may waste ten thousand gold pieces yet gain nothing. This is the true essence of Daoist alchemy.

Its therapeutic uses align with those of natron, suggesting mirabilite *is* natron. Thus, the *Shénnóng Běncǎo* does not distinguish between them. The finest quality originates from *Níngzhōu* (Ning Prefecture), white with large grains and an extremely bitter, pungent taste. If refined by physicians, it appears snow-white with fine grains and a less intense flavor. It is derived from natron, and the refined product is superior.

Additionally, according to the *Chūn Huā Huápí* (Spring Blossom Pool) method: Take seven transformations of spring mirabilite, five *dàn* of black-colored stone (from the Five-Colored Mountain Pitch, known as *Hàohuáng Fán* [august yellow alum]), which is not five separate substances. Use five *dòu* of natron and five *jīn* of mirabilite.

Now, examining the two natrons, they are distinguished by their names, while the Five-Colored Mountain Pitch is specified as three *dòu*. Clearly, this indicates that the Five-Colored Mountain Pitch refers to a single substance.

The *Spring Blossom Pool* method states: Each differs in its *dàn* (crude form), placed within spring mirabilite, sealed for three *qī* (sevens) days to complete.

All transformations and refinements into yellow or white forms, altering the Five Metals, employ this *Spring Blossom Pool* method. The most secretive of all, the *Ten Thousand Gold* method, is never transmitted.

But mirabilite is produced by refining natron, and this method uses both substances to achieve their transcendent power—its efficacy is profound. The **therapeutic uses of mirabilite** are as follows:

According to the臣 (*chén*, "this official"): Mirable natron is of bitter, pungent taste, and intensely cold. It treats accumulations in the Five *Zàng* (organs), internal heat with stomach closure, dissipates *bèi* (back) *qì* (vital force) fragments and lingering blood, resolves phlegm-induced blockages and masses in the abdomen, unbinds the channels and vessels, promotes urination and defecation, and regulates menstrual flow and the Five *Lín* (types of urinary dysfunction). **Pteris stone** serves as its messenger herb, while it fears **millet seed** and ginger. If mirabilite is refined into natron, it treats abdominal distension from heat, nourishes the stomach and aids digestion, dispels pathogenic *qì*, and also dissolves in water—its therapeutic effects align with those of true natron. The refining method is detailed within the natron section.

**Sources of mirabilite**: According to the臣 (*chén*): Mirable natron originates from natron, found in the mountains and valleys of **Yìzhōu** (Benefit Prefecture). Natron is also said to share the same mountains as natron, indicating their similar efficacy and origins. Though natron and natron are not identical, they are largely alike with minor differences.

Natron is described as **granular like held salt and snow**, not melting under strong pressure, and when burned, it emits **purple-green, amorous flames**, then turns to ash without boiling or yielding liquid—this is natron. If it boils and produces liquid, it is natron. If carefully examined for color and nature, they should not be hastily distinguished.

Natron grows in the **sunlit slopes of mountains** where there are **bitter, salty waters**. The finest quality comes from **Níngzhōu** (Ning Prefecture).

**Method for refining natron into mirabilite**: According to the臣 (*chén*): Though mirabilite has crude and refined forms, its transformative power and effects are divine. Since it is already derived from natron, it is a substance that has undergone refining—one should not further refine what has already been refined.

Now, the method for refining natron into mirabilite is as follows: Regardless of the natron’s quantity, first sift and grind it. Use **warm water** to extract its essence, clarify the liquid, and boil it—always reducing it to half its volume. Place the residue in a **wooden basin soaked in clear water**, and after a night, it will form—**crystals resembling white quartz in size**, each with eight facets.

Handle it carefully to avoid contamination. Strictly avoid mixing it with other substances or allowing onlookers during the process, as this will disrupt its **refined *qì* (vital essence)**, and the transformation will fail. Only **replacing the clear water** in the wooden basin will hasten its formation. Do not use unclean water; this method’s efficacy depends entirely on the purity of the water.

The official submits that this is what is required to produce the eight varieties of nitre. Among the eight types of nitre, there are *shípí* (石脾) and nitre. It is proposed to refine thirty-six waters, and *shípí* is also a refined substance, yet it cannot stand alone—it must rely on refining crude natron. The text states that mirabilite aids in this process, and only then can the transformation of all waters be fully effective.

Now, when people see in the mirabilite method the phrase *"exhausting its efficacy,"* they mistakenly believe that mirabilite alone can produce water—how greatly they are misled! *Shípí* is a single substance that few recognize. Without it, nitre and its waters cannot be properly formed. Those who can produce it achieve divine efficacy.

Thus, the method’s application—when used to make nitre—is infallible, its Dao/Way complete.

The mirabilite method further states: *"This transforms and produces all external waters, fully effective."*

**Method for Producing *Shípí* (石脾) Powder**
To produce *shípí* powder, refined saltpeter (*róngyán*—戎盐) is required. The method for refining *róngyán* is identical to the true process, and together they form nitre to refine the waters. Though both are included in the nitre methods, they are reiterated here for emphasis in relation to mirabilite.

**Method for Producing *Shípí* (石脾)**
Take one *jīn* of true white alum (*zhēnbái fánshí*—真白矾石) and one *jīn* of *róngyán*. Grind each separately into powder. Place two *shāng* of bitter water in a pot, boil it four or five times, then add the powders and simmer until half remains. Filter out the dregs, then boil again until the liquid is exhausted. When it boils anew, *shípí* forms—a white substance like snow. Using this to make nitre is always effective, its efficacy divine and complete.

**Method for Producing *Róngyán* (戎盐)**
Take any quantity of pure rock salt, melt it in an iron vessel until boiling, then add powdered white alum. Remelt it in brine, then add powdered *gānlíng* (乾灵), covering it tightly. Repeat this threefold refining process to produce *róngyán*—its transformation indistinguishable from the true substance.

**Five-Colored Divine Salt**
Peng Jun says: *"This is the sovereign of all medicines. If one makes the five-colored divine salt, using the essences of the Five Emperors, it becomes the five-colored divine *yàn* (盥)."*

**East Wilds Mirabilite Method**
Take any quantity of *xiánjīng* (咸精, salt essence), place it in an earthen pot with bitter water, and boil it ten times. Strain and clarify, then immerse it in *ruògǔcǎo* (若骨草) brine for two days. Transfer the *ruògǔcǎo* brine to a copper pot and boil until the liquid is exhausted—it will congeal into white mirabilite. If one wishes it to form facets, do not boil the liquid dry. Instead, place it in a clean porcelain vessel and store it in a shaded location for three days—it will crystallize into large, faceted mirabilite.

This mirabilite is indistinguishable from the true substance and can also purify the body.

**Essential Method for *Rògǔcǎo* (苦骨草, *Ruògǔcǎo*)**
The *Rògǔcǎo* is *kǔcān* (苦参, *Kǔcān*). Its bitterness penetrates to the bones, hence its name. Its herb is exceedingly potent and bitter as well.

Mirabilite (*mángxiàn*, 芒硝) is also bitter and pungent. Thus, when it is used in this manner, it is said to also possess potency. However, it can be employed in medicinal preparations for the sovereign, yet it is not suitable for alchemical transformations.

Some may doubt whether *kǔshuǐ* (苦水, bitter water) refers to vinegar, and why it must be so. If one seeks to perform alchemical transformations, it is not possible to refine *pǔmirabilite* (朴硝) and produce the essence of *yuánzhèng* (元正, primordial purity) without it. True substances are far superior in efficacy.

**Method for *Shípí* Mirabilite (石脾硝石法)**
Take *shípí* (石脾, *Shípí*) one *jīn* (斤), mirabilite (*mángxiàn*) one *jīn*, and *pǔmirabilite* one *jīn*.
Though this method is already recorded in the *Shíyàn* (硝石, Mirabilite) Essentials, it is transcribed again here for clarity. The previous volume distinguished true from false substances and included various methods, but in selecting one, errors may occur. Now, *mángxiàn* (芒硝), *róngyàn* (戎盥), and *shípí* (石脾) are all compounded together.

Master Pēng (彭君) further states that their transformative efficacy does not fall short of the genuine essence. He also instructs those seeking immortality to rely upon this method. Thus, the method for *shípí* is appended here.

Grind each substance finely and mix into a powder. Take three *dǒu* (斗) of *kǔshuǐ* (苦水, bitter water), and decoct in a copper pot until ten ebullitions occur. Add the three powders, and decoct until half the liquid remains. Remove the dregs and clarify the mixture. When the decoction reaches a viscous state, pour it into a porcelain vessel and immerse it in a clean porcelain vessel filled with *língshuǐ* (玲水, clear water) for one day—it will congeal into *shípí* mirabilite, resembling frost or frozen dew.

Pour water upon it, and it dissolves instantly. Then decoct again, until it reaches a viscous state, and pour it into a porcelain vessel, immersing it once more in *língshuǐ*. It will again form *shípí* mirabilite. Repeat this process three times. If the method is followed correctly, the results will be evident.

Do not refine it in a filthy place, nor expose it to wind or sunlight. *Shípí* is the congealed *qi* (氣) of yin and yang. The essence of the Five *Yàn* (盥) is prolonged by alum (*fán*, 矾) and nurtured by stone, often found in abundance on *Éyuè* Mountain (峨崛山). Common folk rarely recognize its use, so it is seldom sought. Only those who practice the Dao (道) must employ it.

In the past, it was divided into four regions, and none could obtain it. Thus, ancient alchemists created substitutes, which are indeed superior to the genuine substance. *Shípí* is the congealed *qi* of yin and yang. Bitter water is exceedingly potent, and alum is cold in nature; when these two are decocted together, they congeal under fire. The essence of the Five *Yàn* is derived from *rónglíng* (戎灵, *Rónglíng*), which can be used to make five-colored salt. The sovereign’s method is thus established.

Prolonged by alum and nurtured by stone, it becomes *báifánshí* (白矾石, white alum stone). This is its perfected form.

---
**Essentials of the *Jiǔdǐng* Divine Elixir (黄帝九鼎神丹经诀) – Volume XVI**

**Method for *Xuányellow* (玄黄, *Xuányellow*)**
*Xuányellow* is produced by mixing tin (*xí*, 锡) with mercury (*shuǐyín*, 水银).

Tin is originally derived from *Huángdān* (黄丹, yellow cinnabar), but if its essence is not refined, it is unfit for the cultivation of longevity. Thus, the method for *Huángdān* follows:

**Method for *Huángdān* (黄丹, yellow cinnabar)**
If one obtains *Huángdān* from the market, it may be adulterated with yellow soil, so its quality is uncertain. True *Huángdān* is not self-made by the master. The self-made elixir is red and vivid, with a lustrous radiance that is pleasing to the eye. If it does not meet this standard, it is not genuine.

**Preparation Method**
Take two *jīn* of lead (*qiān*, 铅), wash it clean in any quantity, and roast it in an iron cup until it becomes sandy. Rinse with clean water and place it in an iron sieve, repeatedly washing and sifting until it is thoroughly refined. Drain the water, leaving only the dregs, and dry them in the sun for ten days. Pound into a fine powder, then sift through silk. Place the powder back into the iron cup and roast it for two to three nights until it turns red. This is the refined lead (*dānqiān*, 丹铅).

**Extraction of Lead**
Hu Jiāngzǐ (狐刚子) says: In all elixir preparations, lead is the foundation. If the lead is not genuine, the elixir will fail. The method for extracting lead is as follows: Take *Xuányellow* essence (*jīngzhī*, 精汁) and add a small amount of gold powder (*jīnzéi*, 金贼). Knead it like dough until it is malleable, then dry it in the shade for seven to eight days. Heat it in an iron pot, and it becomes *dānqiān* (丹铅, cinnabar lead), which is then used to make *Xuányellow*.

The lead used for decocting mercury has a separate method, which is detailed under the *Fùshuǐyín* (伏汞, subdued mercury) and *shuǐyín* (水银, mercury) methods.

**Method for *Xuányellow* (玄黄)**
Take one *jīn* of mercury (*shuǐyín*), and decoct it for thirty-six days, or until it congeals with twenty *jīn* of lead. Refine it five times to ensure purity. Place both substances in an iron vessel and heat them fiercely. The lead and mercury will emit their refined essence—a violet substance with yellow brilliance, known as *Huángyá* (黄芽, yellow sprout) or *Lóngqīngfēi jīng* (龙轻飞精, Dragon’s Lightly Ascending Essence).

**Essentials Say:**
Take tin (*xí*) and place it in an iron vessel. Add charcoal fire beneath, and bring it to a boil. Gradually reduce the heat until it simmers, then add mercury (*shuǐyín*) into the vessel. Stir with damp willow wood until five colors appear. Use an iron spoon to skim near one side, then collect the essence, allowing it to flow out before taking it again.

When the fire is hot, the color appears yellow. If the fire is refined (*líng*, 玲), the color turns violet-green, with a faint vapor. If the fire is well-regulated, the color becomes red-violet, resembling gold.

When burned together in shared flame, they assume a single hue, closely resembling gold in form.
Once removed from the fire, they revert to their original nature.

To forge the *Danfǔ* (elixir cauldron), one must first prepare *Xuánhuáng* (玄黄, Mysterious Yellow).
The Nine Cauldrons’ ritual offerings likewise rely upon this substance.
If not pre-prepared in abundance, one will inevitably fall short when the moment arises.
Thus, one must early refine mercury and extract lead.

According to the *Tàiqīng* (太清, Supreme Clarity) ritual offering method, there are also instances where *Xuánbái* (玄白, Mysterious White) must be used as the elixir’s offering. The method follows as below:

---
**Method for *Xuánbái* (Mysterious White):**
In the *Jiǔdǐng* (九鼎, Nine Cauldrons) Eighth Elixir Method, take one *catty* of *Xuánhuáng* or *Xuánbái*, spread it across the cauldron’s base, and place mercury upon it—hence the necessity of its preparation.

Take lead, melt it into a flat plate, and place it beneath mercury—one *catty* of mercury to three *caties* of lead, with six *liǎng* of true gold, dissolving the lead and gold.
Then, introduce the mercury, beating it into a silver plate, and suspend it in the *Huápó* (华池, Flower Pool) for seven days, checking daily.
If no reaction occurs, seal the *Huápó*’s ceramic mouth tightly. When it reacts, collect the flowing white substance, place it in a green bamboo tube, seal its mouth with lacquer, and return it to the *Huápó*. After thirty days, it becomes water.

**Alternative Method:**
Take one *catty* of lead and one *catty* of gold, hammering them into a thin plate like silk.
Place it in a wooden tray, lining the bottom with cloth, and immerse it in the mixture. After thirty days, *Xuánbái* will form in the tray—only then may it be used.
If the *Xuánbái* contains gold, it may be used; if not, it cannot.

The *Tàiqīng* elixir uses *Xuánbái* as the offering gold, while the *Jiǔdǐng* method employs only *Xuánhuáng*.

**Note by the Scholar:**
To concoct the divine elixir, one must first prepare the various waters, refine all mineral poisons, submerge in *Liùyīní* (六一泥, Six-to-One Mud), and boil the subdued mercury. Whatever one handles must be steeped in vinegar for over a hundred days—this is called *chúnyùn* (淳酝, refined ferment). If aged three years or more, it is termed *kǔjiǔ* (苦酒, bitter wine). When medicated, it becomes the *Huápó*.
Ancients kept this secret, calling it the *zuǒwèi* (左味, Left Flavor), seeking the Great Dao.
Those who covet immortality and eternal youth must prepare it; without it, success is rare—hence the prescribed order follows.

---
**Method for Vinegar:**
Take one *dàn* of red *jì* millet, clean and rinsed, and three *dàn* of *bēn* (坩, a type of clay pot).
Cook it thoroughly into rice, then treat it in equal measure—three *dàn* at a time—placing it in a ceramic vessel, sifting and pressing it.
Mix the milled millet rice and *bēn* in equal parts, then layer seven sheets of paper over the ceramic mouth. After each seven days, remove one layer. By the forty-ninth day, all paper is gone.
Initially, the paper is sealed with *Zī* (Zl ］) cords.
After seven cycles of seven days, the vinegar is ready.
Cover the ceramic mouth with fine silk, waiting until full before adding medicine.
To extract the vinegar for medication, collect only the clear liquid.
If the dregs are to be stored, keep them sealed and undisturbed.

The vinegar water should be made with rainwater from the fifth month—most potent.
For large batches (hundreds or thousands of *dàn*), distribute the vinegar evenly across the ceramic base, ensuring it is spread thinly.

**Avoid frequent transfers—each move risks spoilage. Use only a wooden ladle, and occasionally sprinkle with dried thorns to remove hair and impurities.**

---
**From the *Tàiqīng Zhōngjīng* (太清中经, Supreme Clarity Central Scripture) – Method for the *Huápó*:**
The *Huápó* (Flower Pool) is also called *nìshuǐ* (溺水, Urine Water), *Sìhǎishuǐmǔ* (四海水母, Mother of the Four Seas), or *Xuánchí* (玄池, Mysterious Pool).
It exists naturally in the heavens, located at the North Pole.
The human-made method uses five *dàn* of refined *zuǒwèi*, taking three parts and adding one *catty* of honey, five *dòu* of grain.
Soak it in water until sprouted, then dry and sift it, placing it in the *Huápó* and mixing thoroughly.
Wrap thirty *catty* of alum stone in rice husks, soak it within, and seal it for three days—its taste is bitter yet sweet and sour.
Add ten *catty* of saltpeter, completing the mixture.

With five *dàn* of gold and jade water, twenty days of lead and mercury, or a hundred days of gold, silver, pearls, and lead, all will dissolve into water.
Rainwater from heaven used for *zuǒwèi* is especially superior.

**Heavenly Master’s *Tàiqīng Huápó* Oral Instruction:**
As per the original scripture, prepare the *Huápó* by soaking five *dòu* of grain in water until sprouted, drying and sifting it, then placing it in the *Huápó* and mixing with the other ingredients to complete it.
If the grain does not sprout, the pool will fail—this is the essence of the Great Dao.

With *Huápó* water, gold, jade, five stones, lead, and the like, all will dissolve into essence.
Among the thirty-six waters, all require the *Huápó* to transform into water.

---
**Method for Three-Cycle *Huángbái Zuǒwèi* (黄白左味, Yellow-White Left Flavor):**
Take six *dàn* of three-year-aged *kǔjiǔ* (bitter wine) from a refined fermentation.
Add spring wine dregs, stirring and mixing them in.
Take one *dàn* of *shǔmǐ* (黍米, glutinous millet), soak it thoroughly in urine water, and place it inside until fully dissolved. Press out the clear liquid.
Add eight *dòu* of *huángyī* (黄衣, yellow garment—likely fermented grain husks) and five kinds of sprouted grains—each three *dòu*—into the mixture. After twenty-one days, press it out and place it in a large ceramic vessel.
Add one *catty* each of gold and silver filings, two *catty* of green alum stone, ten *catty* of yellow alum stone, and three *catty* of thirty-times refined lead ash, wrapping them in cloth and suspending them within. After seventy days, the lead essence will dissolve into the medicine.

The completed *Huángbái Zuǒwèi* is another name for the *Huápó*—it exists naturally in the heavens.
The five sprouted grains refer to wheat, beans, millet, barley, and rice, soaked in water until sprouted in seven to eight days, forming a bed—collectively called the five sprouted grains.

If one seeks to concoct elixirs or refine gold and mercury waters, subduing the eight poisons and myriad celestial prescriptions, one must pre-prepare ten or twenty ceramic jars. These must be made in advance—never at the last moment, for the medicine will lack potency, and transformations will fail.

**Instruction:**
The *qīngfánshí* (青矾石, green alum stone) is selected from *hàobái fán* (昊白矾, celestial white alum), choosing only the green-yellow variety—this is what the *Běncǎo* (本草, *Compendium of Materia Medica*) calls *yīngyǐfán* (鹦矢矾, parrot-dropping alum).

「Hang it in the midst [of the mixture], after seventy days, the essence of lead will dissolve into the medicine, forming the yellow-white *zuǒwèi*—the method is complete. When the yellow-white *zuǒwèi* is achieved, this is called *Huápí*—it exists naturally in the heavens. The five sprouted grains refer to wheat, beans, millet, barley, and rice, soaked in water until sprouted, then selected and steamed until ripe. The *bùpò mài* (不破麦, unsprouted barley) is used to make the *zuǒwèi*—this is the correct method.

According to the *Húzǐ Xuánzhū Jīng* (狐子玄珠经, *Fox’s Mystic Pearl Scripture*), only the *Xuánzhū* (玄珠, Mystic Pearl) of the yellow-white *zuǒwèi* is employed, which is precisely the *Huápí* described above. All other methods are inferior to this.

The **Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir *Huápí* Method** (黄帝九鼎神丹华池方):
To concoct the *Huápí* elixir and verify the essence of the five stones, preventing their dispersion, take small barley (*xiǎomài*) five *dǒu* (斗, a measure of grain). Soak it, select the sprouted portion, and steam it until ripe. Take *gòu* (够, glutinous rice) five *dǒu*, and green-white stones (*qīngbái shí*) as large as a chestnut, five *dǒu* in total. Take seven *jīn* (斤, a unit of weight) of lead (*qiān*), and refine it into flakes (*xiè*). Take five *jīn* of cinnabar (*dānshā*), finely ground into powder. Take red millet rice (*chìshǔ mǐ*), one *dǒu* as the main ingredient, and cook it into porridge (*fàn*).

First, place the stones (*shízǐ*) at the bottom of the ceramic jar (*cípǐ*). Next, layer the cinnabar (*dānshā*), then the glutinous rice (*gòu*), followed by the barley (*mài*), then the millet porridge (*shǔfàn*), and finally, pour in one *shí* (石, a large measure) and five *dǒu* of water, thoroughly moistening it. Seal the jar tightly. In summer, it takes seventy days to complete; in winter, one hundred and forty days.

Prepare it in a secluded chamber (*shèngshì*), at a auspicious location (*wàngxiàng zhī dì*), ensuring that no parrot (*yīng*), dogs (*quǎn*), women (*fùrén*), or livestock (*liùchù*) witness the process, lest the divine efficacy (*shén gōng*) fail.

The **Jade Candle Five Sprouted Grains *Huápí* Method for Subduing Mercury** (玉烛万金诀伏汞华池方):
Take three *shí* of yellow-white *zuǒwèi*, along with one *jīn* of celestial green alum (*hàoqīng fán*), and one *jīn* each of the five sprouted grains. Take the yellow-white *zuǒwèi* and refine it three times (*sān zhuǎn*), then finely grind it.

Take *qīngshān zhī* (青山脂, green mountain fat), and store it for seven days before opening the seal. Add the five sprouted grains, reseal tightly to prevent leakage, and let it mature in three cycles of seven days (*sān qī rì*), thus completing the process.

According to the *Dān Huápí* (单华池, Single *Huápí*) method, if one seeks to subdue mercury (*fú gōng*), the essential requirement is to use the five sprouted grains *Huápí* method. Any other method will fail to subdue mercury. Common folk, unaware of this, simply boil it in vinegar (*cù*), either for three nights or ten days and ten nights, expending their efforts in vain—there will be no true subduction. Without the five sprouted grains *Huápí*, even if one labors for a thousand days, success will never be achieved.

**Instruction:** This method of the five sprouted grains *Huápí* is made using the yellow-white *zuǒwèi*, clarifying that it is not the vinegar-refined *zuǒwèi*. Moreover, according to the *Xuánzhū* (玄珠) method, all substances refined (*zhì*) are said to be of the yellow-white *zuǒwèi*. Now, using the refined flakes (*jīn xiè*) of this *Xuánzhū*—gold flakes (*jīn xiè*), silver flakes (*yín xiè*), and lead white (*qiān bái*)—along with green-yellow stones (*qīnghuáng èr pān*) of the great *Huápí*, and on days *gēngxīn dǎo* (庚辛卯, the 7th, 8th, and 4th day of the lunar cycle), re-add the five sprouted grains and celestial green alum (*hàoqīng fán*), and let it mature in four cycles of seven days (*sì qī rì*). Then use it to subdue mercury—it will always be effective.

The variations in methods are initially perplexing, but this ensures no mistakes are made. As for the Jade Candle Five Sprouted Grains *Huápí* method, it involves refining the yellow-white *zuǒwèi* three times (*sān zhuǎn*), which is precisely what is described here.

Why? Because the initial method of three refinements of the yellow-white *zuǒwèi* uses six *shí* of aged, bitter wine (*kǔjiǔ*), which has been repeatedly distilled (*chóngniàng*) from three-year-old wine. This is the meaning of the first refinement (*yī zhuǎn*). The term *chóngniàng* (重酿) refers to another name for *chúnzuì* (淳醉, pure intoxicant), as its flavor is not diluted. It is not the common, profit-seeking wine (*súwèn qiú lì zhī wèi*).

Again, it states: Take the pure essence (*shàngqīng*) of the second refinement (*èr zhuǎn*), along with one *shí* of spring wine dregs (*chūnjiǔ zāo*), and thoroughly mix it in after it has been stored for a period. Then take one *shí* of the finest millet rice (*shàngshǔ mǐ*), cook it into a weak, extremely soft porridge (*ruò chī jí làn*), and add it to the mixture, waiting until it fully dissolves.
