This is the meaning of the second refinement (*èr zhuǎn*).

Again, it states: Take this second refinement (*èr zhuǎn*), then press it to extract the pure essence (*qīng*). Add eight *dǒu* of yellow-white *zuǒwèi*, and three *dǒu* each of the five sprouted grains. Store it in a sealed jar for three cycles of seven days (*sān qī rì*), then press it out and place it in a large ceramic jar (*dà cípǐ*). Add one *jīn* each of gold flakes (*jīn xiè*) and silver flakes (*yín xiè*), followed by two *jīn* of celestial green alum (*hàoqīng fán*), ten *jīn* of yellow alum (*huáng fán*), and three *jīn* of fifty-times refined lead white flakes (*wǔshí liàn qiān bái xiè*). Wrap it in cloth and suspend it within the jar. After seventy days, the essence of lead will dissolve into the medicine, forming the yellow-white *zuǒwèi*—this is the meaning of the third refinement (*sān zhuǎn*).

Now, using the third refinement of yellow-white *zuǒwèi*, after the essence of lead has fully dissolved, and the seventy-day process is complete, take one *shí* of the pure essence (*shàngqīng*) and add one *jīn* of finely ground celestial green alum (*hàoqīng fán*), storing it for seven days before opening the seal. Then add one *jīn* each of the five sprouted grains, reseal tightly to prevent leakage, and let it mature in three cycles of seven days (*sān qī rì*), thus completing the process.

This is what is referred to as "reapplying celestial green alum and reinvesting the five sprouted grains," done to ensure its supreme efficacy. Therefore, the *Dān Huápí* (单华池) method, even if practiced for a thousand days without proper observance, will never succeed.

The **Jade Candle Five Sprouted Grains *Huápí*** (玉烛五栽) is also called the *Huápí Xuánzhū* (华池玄珠, *Huápí* Mystic Pearl). The method for subduing mercury (*fú gōng*) is only called *zuǒwèi*, clarifying that it must be refined to the fifth sprouted grain and fourth transformation (*wǔ zǎi sì zhuǎn*) to be the true method.

Again, according to the annotations of the **Yellow Emperor’s Supreme Unity Gold Elixir Returning Elixir *Huápí* Method** (太一金液还丹注释), all failures are due to either the use of false saltpeter (*xiāo shí*), or the *Huápí* method being lost. This is the case.

Again, regarding the **Five Transformations Frost Powder *Huápí* Method** (五转霜粉法之华池), if not done as prescribed, even after ten days or twenty days, or even if one adds hooks and leaves (*gōuliú*), the pills will never form properly. If mixing clay with aged, bitter wine (*kǔjiǔ*), it can also be done according to the gold elixir *zuǒwèi* method, but the wine must not be rushed—it must be aged. The term *bǎi rì* (百日) means it must not be less than one hundred days; three years is even better.

The **Yellow Emperor’s Supreme Unity Gold Elixir Returning Elixir *Huápí* Method** (黄帝太一金液还丹华池方):
Take three *shí* and six *dǒu* of water from the heavens during the fifth month (*tiān yǔ shuǐ*), and make aged, bitter wine (*kǔjiǔ*), using glutinous rice (*mǐ gòu*) as usual for sealing the jar. Within twenty-one days, prepare one *dǒu* and eight *shēng* (升, a smaller measure) of finely ground barley sprout powder (*dàmài xuàn mò luò*).

After seven days, or three cycles of seven days (*sān qī rì*), separate the clear liquid (*qīngdèng*) and store it in a large ceramic jar (*dà cípǐ*), naming it *zuǒwèi*. Again, prepare three *dǒu* of finely ground glutinous rice (*lín mǐ luò*), and first grind ten *jīn* of alum stone (*fán shí*) until it resembles the size of glutinous rice grains (*rú mǐdòu dà*). Wrap the grinded alum in the glutinous rice powder, making about thirty such parcels (*bāo*). Place them in the *zuǒwèi*, and after one hundred days, it becomes the **Yellow Emperor’s Supreme Unity *Huápí*** (太一华池).

Once the *Huápí* is complete, it can be used to soak gold elixir (*jīn yè*), and as a remedy for the eight stones (*bā shí*). The **Eight Stones *Huápí* Method** (八石华池法):
Take two *shí* and one *dǒu* of the third refinement *zuǒwèi*, along with one *jīn* each of purple stone crystal (*zǐ shíyīng*), true stalactite (*zhēn zhōnglǘ*), and special-born *yù shí* (誉石, esteemed stone), one *jīn* of magnetite (*cí shí*), five *jīn* of *qīngyáng shí* (青阳石, green sun stone), one *jīn* and four *liǎng* (两, ounce) of gypsum (*shí gāo*), and eight *liǎng* of *shízhēng zhī* (石亭脂, stone pavilion fat), along with three *dǒu* of the five sprouted grains.

In all cases of the Nine Elixirs, sift the *tāo* (梼) separately, select a day of the *Yin* (寅), and combine them in porcelain vessels, sealing tightly so as not to let the *qi* escape. In seven days, it is complete.

Take gold filings, silver filings, and *huáng yī* (黄衣) and cast them into the Eight Stones *Huápí*. According to the method, when full, it becomes the Yellow-White *Zuǒwèi*. This is the Yellow-White Eight Stones *Huápí*. With this *Zuǒwèi*, one may boil mercury and refine cinnabar (*hédān*), and upon sublimation, it yields the elixir of immortality.

**Qīngshān Zhī *Huápí* Method**
Take two *shí* and one *dǒu* of the third refinement *Zuǒwèi*, that which is the color of amber. Within it, use fifty *jīn* of *Hàoqīngshān zhī* (昊青山脂, Celestial Blue Mountain Fat)—some say thirty *jīn*—sifted and cast into the *Zuǒwèi*, sealed tightly so as not to let the *qi* escape. In forty-nine days, it becomes the Eight Treasures *Qībǎo Water*. Add five *dǒu* of the Seven Treasures, reseal for three times seven days, and place the medicine inside without omission—it will no longer be water. Keep this secret and do not divulge it.

Adding earthly filings of Yellow-White and the like, it transforms into water and elixir with certainty.

**Chūncháo *Huápí***
Take three *shí* of the seventh refinement *Chūncháo*, that which is perfectly black. Within it, use three *dǒu* of Five Mountains Fat (*Wǔshān zhī*), five *jīn* each of *mángxiāo* (芒硝, mirabilite) and *pǔxiāo* (朴硝, crude saltpeter), each sifted separately, and cast into the *Chūncháo*. Seal for three times seven days, and it is complete.

For all transformations and refinements of Yellow-White, or altering the Five Metals, this *Huápí* is used—most secret, worth ten thousand in gold.

The supreme *Huápí* is used to make the *Bǎiqīshuǐ* (百七水, Hundred-Seven Water). All cases of subduing mercury use the Yellow-White *Zuǒwèi*, and one must use gold filings, silver filings, and the like, cast into the *Chūnniàng Huápí* (春酿华池, Spring Ferment *Huápí*) to refine the divine *fēiqiānshuǐ* (飞铅汞, sublimated lead-mercury water).

For all uses of the Thirty-Six Waters, and for all nitrates used in transformations, take the *Huápí* of the Yellow Emperor’s Supreme Golden Elixir (*Tàiyī Jīnyè Huápí*), the *Huápí* of the *Tàiqīng Zhōngjīng* (太清中经, Central Scripture of Supreme Clarity) Divine Elixir, or the *Huápí* of the *Yùshuǐ* (溺水, Urine Water) as well.

If boiling the elixir of immortality’s mercury, use the Eight Stones Five Refined Yellow-White Third Refinement *Zuǒwèi Huápí*.

If one wishes to mix *mòjīnní* (没金泥, gold-sealing mud), take wine aged three years or one hundred days.

The **Jīnhuá Huápí** (金华华池, Golden Flower *Huápí*), akin to the Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir (*Jiǔdǐng Shéndān*), is used in blending, refining, and coating—all applications. Other *Huápí* methods that do not align with this are not recorded here.

**End of Volume Seventeen of the Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Scripture**
**End of Volume Eighteen of the Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Scripture**

The **Lingzhu (钟乳)** and other stones, as well as all copper and iron ores, all possess the use of prolonging life.

**Refining Lingzhu’s Power**
The humble servant notes: Though Lingzhu is not the finest of medicines, it is indeed the essential ingredient for the *Eight Stones Huápí*. Thus, Tao Yuanming (陶隐居) consumed it, thereby extending his lifespan, preserving his youthful vigor, and maintaining his radiant complexion without aging.

**Lingzhu’s Therapeutic Actions**
The humble servant notes: Lingzhu is of sweet and warm nature, non-toxic, and treats:
- Reversed drinking (饮逆),
- Upper respiratory obstruction (上气),
- Brightening the eyes and enhancing essence (明目益精),
- Calming the five viscera (安五脏),
- Unifying the hundred joints (通百节),
- Benefiting the nine orifices (利九窍),
- Promoting lactation (下乳汁),
- Augmenting *qi* and replenishing deficiencies (益气补虚损),
- Treating leg weakness, pain, and numbness (疼玲),
- Rectifying injuries from sexual exhaustion (下宜伤竭),
- Strengthening yang (强阳),
- Conferring fertility (令人有子).

If consumed unrefined, it causes urinary disorders (淋). *Shechuang* (蛇床) serves as its messenger herb, while it is antagonized by *mudan* (牡丹), *xuanshi* (玄石), and *du rong* (杜荣), and feared by *zishí* (紫石) and *suocao* (蓑草).

**Lingzhu’s Sources**
The humble servant notes: Lingzhu grows in the valleys of Shaoshi Mountain (少室山) and Taishan (太山). It may be harvested at any time. It is also known as *Kongru* (孔乳), *Lushi* (卢石), and *Xiashi* (夏石), found in Shaoshi, which connects to Songshan (嵩高山). It also appears in regions like Shixing (始兴), Jiangling (江陵), and the eastern frontier’s renowned mountains and stone caves. The finest Lingzhu is light and thin like a goose quill, shatters like claws or nails, lacks internal striations like wild goose teeth (*yanzhi*), and gleams brightly. Some specimens reach one to two *chi* in length, turning white when washed with aged wine. Though rarely used in Daoist scriptures, it is highly valued in folk prescriptions and commands a high price.

**Refining Lingzhu into the Elixir of Longevity (长生华池法)**

Take Lingzhu, regardless of quantity or thickness—only that which has been washed until its brightness gleams—may be used for refining.
The yellow and red hues are unfit for use.

When refining, place the Lingzhu in a vessel of gold or silver. If no such vessel is available, a large cauldron may suffice. Boil it until the liquid is as viscous as fish eyes, then add water as it evaporates.
For thin specimens, three days and nights suffice. If black-edged or thick like a goose quill, seven days and nights are needed. When the liquid turns yellow, the Lingzhu is ripe. If doubt remains, boil for ten days and nights; the water in the cauldron will turn entirely yellow.
Discard all this water. Drinking it will perforate the throat and cause headaches. Prolonged consumption leads to dysentery, but eating pork may remedy it. If the yellow water is not discarded, the process will fail. Pour in fresh water and boil the Lingzhu again for half a day. If the water remains clear, refining is complete.

If refining is careless and the elixir is consumed, it will cause festering sores on the back. Thus, meticulous refining is essential.

**Method for Grinding the Refined Lingzhu**
Place the refined Lingzhu in a porcelain mortar and grind it with a jade pestle until it shatters. Add a little water during grinding; as the water evaporates, replenish it, always keeping the mixture as thin as diluted ink. The finer particles will float, while the coarse ones settle. Though grinding with a pestle may seem swift, it must be done continuously for five or six days, day and night. Grind it so finely that it resembles human milk. After ten days, the Lingzhu will emit a pure white radiance, most exquisite.
Test a small amount by applying it to your arm—it will adhere like white fish fat on paper, glowing with light even when washed. Only such refined Lingzhu is worthy of consumption.

After thorough refining, strain and dry it in the sun. Once fully ground into fine powder, it may be used in pills or powders as needed.

**Alternative Method:**
To obtain superior Lingzhu, sift it through silk and soak the residue in clear wine for a day and night. Remove the floating impurities, then take the settled portion, dry it, and grind it as before.

Once the Lingzhu is fully refined and ground into powder, mix it with three *dan* of glutinous rice and steam it for optimal effect.

**Another Method:**
After grinding and refining the Lingzhu, place it in a gold or silver basin. For every *jin* of Lingzhu, use two *liang* of saltpeter (硝石), mix them well, and seal tightly to prevent the escape of *qi*. Then steam the mixture.

**Zishíyīng (紫石英)**
The humble servant notes: Zishíyīng is the finest powder of Lingzhu. Consuming it ensures longevity, and holding it in the mouth prevents hunger and thirst.

Zishíyīng is the essential ingredient of the *Bashi* (八石) elixir. Long-term consumption lightens the body and extends life. Its taste is sweet, spicy, and warm, with no toxicity. It grows in the valleys of Taishan (太山). It may be harvested at any time.

The stones from Taishan are of black color, clear and bright. Beneath them lies a root, hence they are called the finest.

There is also *Mian* stone (绵石), which is black but not clear and bright. Another is *Caiyi* stone (材邑石), whose belly encloses something resembling an eye. *Hao* stone (昊兴石) has purple hues on its four edges but lacks luster. *Hui* stone (会稽石) resembles pomegranate seeds in shape and color.

These four kinds of stones were once indiscriminately used by physicians. Now, if one selects the finest, none surpasses Taishan’s rooted stone. It may be added to the *Bashí* (八石) elixir.

**Dai* **Zhe* Stone (代赭石) – One *Dou* (斗):**
The humble servant notes: Dai Zhe is especially crucial for Daoist elixirs. It is also urgently needed alongside *Rong* salt (戎盥) and *Lu* salt (卤咸). Thus, it is a vital ingredient in the Yellow Emperor’s elixirs.

The finest has a vermilion-red hue, like a rooster’s comb, with luster—it stains fingernails without fading. Commonly sourced from the valleys of Qi (齐国), it may be harvested at any time. Also called *Xu* Pill (须丸), from Gumu (姑幕), or *Xu* Pill Strength (须丸力) from Dai (代郡), named Dai Zhe. This is the common usage, but it is coarse.

Its taste is bitter-sweet, cool, and non-toxic.

**Lu* Salt (卤咸):**
The humble servant notes: Lu* salt and *Rong* salt? These are the most prized by elixir artisans. They are also essential ingredients in the Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons (九鼎) elixir.

Their taste is bitter, salty, and cool, with no toxicity. They grow in the salt pools of the He* River (河束). Some say they are the congealed residue beneath boiling salt cauldrons, while others claim they are the great spirit of the He* River, forming like frozen ice, round and firm.

*Hei* salt (黑盥) is likely Lu* salt, and *Rou* salt (柔盥) is probably *Rong* salt. There is also red salt (赤盐), spotted salt (驳臭盐), and *Ma* salt (马齿盐). All four are not fit for consumption; *Ma* salt is the same as *Da* salt (大盥).

**Rong* Salt (戎盥):**
The humble servant notes: *Rong* salt is abundant among the barbarians. When the chieftain from Dong* State (冻州) arrives, the salt he carries is likely this inferior grade. The chieftain from Henan (河南), as well as the Hu* merchants from Dun*huang (炖煌), also bring it.

Its form is in blocks or slices, sometimes like chicken or duck eggs, sometimes like ice flakes. Its color is purple-white, and though its saltiness is unbearable, when tasted, it emits a faint vapor—just like the scent of a *Duan* chicken egg—proving its authenticity. Additionally, within the mud of Lingchi Pool (灵池) in Henan, there naturally exists congealed salt resembling stone flakes. When struck, it breaks into squares of green color, effectively treating horseback sores. This is likely the same as well.

In general, since it is called *Rong*, one should obtain it from Hu* merchants for the best quality.

**To the Right:** Zishíyīng (紫石英), Dai Zhe (代赭), Lu* salt (卤咸), and *Rong* salt (戎盥) are all non-toxic substances used by elixir artisans. As for Lu* salt, once refined by fire, its method is already established. The rest, even if not refined, may still be used without concern.

**Lead* **Cinnabar (铅丹):**
The humble servant notes: Lead cinnabar is born from lead—it is made by smelting and refining lead into yellow cinnabar. Common folk rarely use it, except in the Daoist *Jian* elixir cauldron, where it is refined to become Nine Radiant (九光) elixir.

This is the method for the Nine Radiant elixir. No other changes or refinements are needed. Also called *Qiang* Flower (铅华).

Its taste is spicy and slightly cool; long-term consumption grants divine insight.

**Hu* Powder (胡粉):**
The humble servant notes: Hu* powder is the primary substance for the True Person’s Ninefold Refined Lead Cinnabar (九转铅丹). It is also the first ingredient in the Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons (九鼎) Divine Elixir method, where it is mixed with *Xuan* Yellow Flower (玄黄花) to form a paste. It is indeed of utmost importance.

However, *Bencao* (本草) states: Powdered tin is also called *Jie* Powder (解粉). It further explains: This is the result of refining lead into gold, producing Hu* powder. Its taste is spicy and cool, non-toxic, and those with a golden hue are superior.

**Method to Neutralize Lead Poison:**
From the first to the ninth refinement, the process is the same. Use one *Dou* (斗) of fine spring flower pool (好春华池), one *Liang* (两) of red salt (赤盥), and one *Liang* of vermilion (朱砂). Stir and immerse them thoroughly. Refine the lead thoroughly by frying it until it turns red, then strain it into the spring flower pool medicine. Repeat this nine times—its poison will be fully exhausted.

One *Dou* of spring flower pool and two *Liang* of red salt cannot neutralize one *Jin* (斤) of lead’s poison, so the poison will not be fully exhausted.

**Method to Remove Copper’s Impurities:**
First, pound it into thin sheets. Apply warm glue juice until it is thin and pliable. Burn it in a *Yue* furnace (越宠) until it turns red, then seal it with thick *Ling* paste (灵厚). Place it back in the *Yue* furnace and burn until red, then remove it. Pound and wash it before placing it back in the furnace. Repeat this process twenty times. If done a hundred times, all impurities will be eliminated, and the copper will become soft and pure.

**Method to Remove *Shu* Stone (输石) and Iron’s Impurities:**
Removing impurities from *Shu* stone and iron is also similar to the copper method. Before pounding *Shu* stone and copper into thin sheets, they must first be pre-refined three times. Their bodies will then be more pliable, and their waters must be thoroughly strained, warmed, and not fully poured in, lest they scatter and be lost.

The *Shuo* (铄) method is as follows: Cut into pieces one *Cun* (寸) wide, six to seven *Cun* long, and two *Fen* (分) thick. After burning, pound and apply glue to fully coat them. If they become too hot, fold them; otherwise, they will not complete the hundred-fold process. Ten *Liang* of impure copper can yield five *Liang* or less of pure substance. This method applies similarly.

**Refining Stone Salt (石盐):**
Ten *Jin* (斤) of stone salt must be strained and washed. Boil it with hot water until it dissolves, then let it settle overnight. Take the clear liquid, evaporate it until nearly dry, and spread it out. Place it in wooden containers, drain the water, and dry it in the sun, ensuring no dust contaminates it.

The best stone salt is ground into three *Dou* of powder. Sift it with cold water and quickly strain it out; slow straining will cause it to dissolve.

Again, use water just enough to moisten it, then wait until it fully dissolves before straining. Let it settle overnight, take the clear liquid, and evaporate the water to obtain salt crystals. Place them in wooden containers, tilt the container to drain the water, and dry in the sun—this yields the finest product.

**Refining White Wax (白蜡) Method:**
Take fine white wax from Kunlun (昆仑). In a sweet clay pot, dissolve it by adding vinegar, refining it three hundred times to complete the process.

When mixed and boiled with medicines, it immediately stops hunger. It can also be used to create a longevity-enhancing skeletal structure, and its refining method for copper and other uses is the same.

**Method for Taking White Wax:**

Take three *jin* of narrow-mouthed jar (*狭斗*), two *sheng* of hemp (*胡麻*), and two *liang* of ginseng (*人参*), along with three *liang* of sulfur (*硫黄*). In total, these four substances are each ground into fine powder and formed into cold honey pills (*冷蜜丸*).

After eating, chew a large piece of white wax—about the size of a date—then add this medicine, chewing it like millet grains until it becomes watery. Swallow it immediately. Repeat this three times a day.

In thirty days, the body’s internal and external *qi* will harmonize, and the skin will become smooth and radiant. In a hundred days, one will appear transformed; in a year, the corpse will expel itself (*伏尸自去*), and all ailments will be cured—one will even revert to the appearance of a child.

**Method for Refining Tin (炼锡法):**
This is similar to the method for refining white wax above. The process is nearly identical.

In refining tin, for each *jin* of tin, add one *jin* of salt powder. Stir with damp willow branches until fully dissolved, then pour into a crucible. Repeat the refining process as before. If you wish to extract pure tin directly, pour it into damp earth. If you refine it ten times and obtain pure tin, you must still mix it with salt and refine again.

**Method for Refining Narrow-Long Fungus (炼狭苓法):**
Take the finest, purest white narrow-long fungus (*狭苓*), which is smooth and tender. Boil it in mulberry ash water until it disperses, then pour it into boiling water. It will quickly congeal into a firm, jar-like shape—this is the best form for use.

**Refining Yellow Earth (炼土扶):**
Take the finest yellow earth, which resembles fat or wax in texture. Dry it in the sun, then grind and sift it. Wash it with water as if preparing sweet wine (*甘饮*), stirring it hundreds of times. Let it settle overnight, then remove the upper clear water.

Take the remaining fine sediment, dry it in the sun. The lower layer is then ground and washed again as before.

Break it into pieces the size of plums or cherries, and burn it fiercely for one or two days until it turns uniformly red like cinnabar (*丹*). Let it cool, then grind it through silk sieves—three *jin* of the refined earth mixed with one *jin* of yellow cinnabar (*黄丹*)—this is the finished product.

Another method: Take one *jin* of yellow earth, which is dense and finely textured. Sift it through silk, then boil it in scalding water for three days. This sediment is used as the crude form of *Huangdi’s Nine Cauldron Elixir* (黄帝九鼎丹), specifically as the *Danliu Zhu Dan* (丹流珠丹).

**Method for Warding Off Evil Spirits and Pestilence (辟神虫皇法):**

Collect five *yǔshuǐ* (rainwater from the fifth month), store it in a porcelain vessel. When needed, reheat it—**pests will emerge and foul it**. To prevent this beforehand, take **three to five *dòu* of soft, yellow earth**, place it in the vessel, and seal it tightly—**do not let dust or impurities enter**.

**Method for Extracting Onion Tears (*cōng tì*):**
Pound fresh onions, wrap them in a coarse cloth, and press to extract the liquid—this is called *tì* (tears).

**Method for Refining Date Honey (*zǎo gāo*):**
Take **one *dòu* of dried dates**, add **six *dòu* of water**, and boil until the dates soften. Then add **three *dòu* of water**, boil again until scalding, and reduce the liquid to **nine *shāng* of decoction**. Strain out the dregs, clarify the liquid, and reduce it to **three *shāng**. Add **six *shāng* of ram’s (雄羊) fat**, stir gently, and simmer until it thickens like syrup. If ram’s fat is unavailable, **goat’s marrow** may substitute. Divide into grades—this is *zǎo gāo* (date honey).

**Such honey, when taken long-term, fills the body, bestowing radiant complexion.**

This honey is used in the preparation of **Golden Elixir (Jīnyè) and Elixir Refining**.

---
*Excerpt from the Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon, Volume Eighteen*
*Excerpt from the Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Canon, Volume Nineteen*

**Methods for Detoxifying Poisonous Metals and Minerals in Alchemical Preparation**

**Detoxifying Dan-Yang Copper Poison**
As recorded in the preceding volume, coat copper with salt glue a hundred times, refining it until pure. Then pulverize the refined copper and boil it in **one *dòu* of nitre water** until fully dissolved. Next, boil it in **one *dòu* of green vitriol water** until fully dissolved. Then boil it in **one *dòu* of *róngxǐ* water** until fully dissolved. Again, boil it in **one *dòu* of true wine**, along with ground black pepper, until fully dissolved. Finally, wrap **one *dàn* of glutinous red millet** around the copper shavings, mix evenly with ground black pepper, and combine with sugarcane juice. Steam for three days and nights, then remove. All poison shall be eliminated. This method detoxifies **ten *jīn* of Dan-Yang copper**, rendering it suitable for powdering and alchemical transformation.

**Detoxifying Lead Ore Poison**
Take the finest Persian lead ore of the highest quality. As in the preceding volume, refine it with salt glue a hundred times until pure. Pulverize the refined ore, then apply the same boiling and steaming methods as for Dan-Yang copper—no differences exist.

**Detoxifying Iron Filings Poison**
Refine iron filings with salt glue a hundred times, ensuring all foul vapors are exhausted. Take **ten *jīn* of refined iron filings**, pulverize them, and boil in the following solutions for three days and nights:
1. **Three *dòu* of realgar water**, until fully dissolved.
2. **One day and night** in *róngxǐ* water (prepared as specified).
3. **One day and night** in magnetite water: place **one *jīn* of iron** in a clean crucible, wrap evenly with cloth, and overlay with the powdered iron. Seal tightly, subject to intense fire beneath, then cool and collect the refined essence. Repeat with magnetite water for another day and night—all poison shall be eliminated. Only then may this detoxified iron be powdered or used in alchemical transformations.

---
**Preparation of Special Waters**
*(From the Thirty-Six Waters Canon)*

**Nitre Water Method**
Sift nitre, soak it in brine until thoroughly moistened, then place in a bamboo tube. Seal tightly and bury it **four *cùn* underground** for five days to yield the water. *(Note: Some texts specify four *chǐ* and four *cùn*—verify before use.)*

**Green Vitriol Water Method**
Select blue-green vitriol (**one *jīn***), first moistening it thoroughly with pure wine. Seal it with lacquer in a container, then bury it **three *chǐ* underground** for fifteen days to yield the water.

**Stone Sulfur Water Method**
Take **one *jīn* of stone sulfur**, **one *shāng* of mulberry leaf dew** (collected by a pure-hearted child on a clear morning with washed hands), and **two *liǎng* of nitre**. Seal in a lacquered bamboo tube and submerge in a flower-filled pond for thirty days to yield the water.

**Pure Brine Water Method**
*(This is brine water.)* Prepare refined salt, sift it, and moisten thoroughly with water. Hollow out a bamboo tube, wrap its mouth tightly with silk, then bury it **four *chǐ* and four *cùn* underground**—the water forms in four days.

**These four waters** are used for refining Dan-Yang copper and lead ore.

**Realgar Water Method**
Take **one *jīn* of realgar**, place it in a bamboo tube with **four *liǎng* of nitre**, seal with lacquer, and submerge in a flower-filled pond for thirty days. *(Alternatively, add two *liǎng* each of vitriol and nitre, seal in an earthen jar, and bury for twenty days.)* The resulting water is sweet-tasting and yellow.

**Brine Water** is the same as the **Pure Brine Water** method above, differing only in name.

**Magnetite Water Method**
Take **one *jīn* of magnetite**, **one *liǎng* of雄黄 (*rónghuáng*)**, and **one *liǎng* of stone gall**. Grind them together, seal in a lacquered bamboo tube, and submerge in a flower-filled pond for thirty days to yield the water. *(All sealed containers must be dried in shade with ash-wrapped cloth.)*

**These three waters** are used for detoxifying iron filings.

---
**General Alchemical Principles**
For those seeking to transmute **Divine Elixir (Shén Dān)** into gold or silver, all waters and minerals must be refined with utmost precision—especially copper and iron, which are not naturally occurring but artificially produced.

To transmute copper into gold or silver:
- For gold: Use **detoxified fire-refined copper**, then apply **雄黄 (*rónghuáng*)** to alter its hue before testing with the elixir.
- For silver: First treat copper with **detoxified white wax** (as in the preceding volume) to whiten it, then test with the elixir. Only through such meticulous preparation shall the transformation succeed—this is the mark of true divine medicine.

---
**Ritual Precautions for Elixir Preparation**
Before commencing elixir formulation in the mountains, first summon the mountain spirits to inquire for approval. Only then may the work proceed without flaw. The method is as follows:

1. **Purification and Invocation**
   - Fast for ten days. Write a **one-*chǐ* yellow-and-white talisman**, dedicating it to the mountain’s sovereign deity. Declare your intent to craft **Divine Elixir**, seeking their permission and ritual directives via symbolic characters.
   - On the day of elixir unification, write an **eight-*cùn* white talisman in cinnabar**, encase it in a crimson pouch, and strike it against your chest.
   - Those who ingest the elixir must abstain for seven days beforehand. Upon consumption, they shall attain **spiritual penetration**, able to command ghosts and spirits.

   *(This is the **Taiyi Eight-*cùn* White Talisman**.)* Preserve the talisman with reverence—do not defile it.

**Incantation from the *Taqīng Shén Dān Bǎo Jīng*:**
*"Concentrate and refine the eight stones,
Illumine with five radiances, seven clarities.
Secure the Celestial Treasury’s essence,
Subdue the Fire Spirits’ might.
Through nine transformations, achieve transcendence—
Ascend to the Supreme Clarity."*

After reciting the incantation, seal the talisman in a **green silk pouch** and strike it upon the head.

This talisman subdues and controls the stone *qi* (精), preventing its escape, filling the air with mist and frost, and causing the *shénhuá* (神华) to congeal. The **harm-repelling talisman**—written in cinnabar on white paper—three inches wide, four inches long—must be cast into the hearth. Immediately, the *qi* will be suppressed. If one often sees the divine light and refines the *qi*, all spirits will come and gather, and immortals with jade maidens will appear.

When the **spiritual elixir** is complete, no malevolent ghosts or spirits in heaven and earth can cause harm.

The method states: *"To forge the spiritual elixir of the five stones and their transformations, extracting the essence of the five metals, one must first pay homage to the **Celestial Sovereign Dao/Way Lord** (天上皇道君) and receive the **Five Divine Talismans** (五神符). Then, the five stones and five metals will transform at will, and their essences will compete to emerge.*

**Green Dao/Way Lord Talisman Method** (青帝符法): On days *jiǎ* (甲) and *yǐ* (乙), use white millet grass as the mat, three feet long. Spread a green silk banner one *zhàng* (丈) two feet long upon it. Place two cups of wine and two slices of dried meat on the mat. Use the banner as the ground, and write the talisman in ink—two inches wide, seven inches long—and place it on the mat. The incantation reads:

*'On a fortunate day and auspicious hour,
Your humble servant [name] prostrates twice.
Reverently receiving the Celestial Sovereign Dao/Way Lord’s Green Dao/Way Lord Divine Talisman.
After prostrating twice, burn the talisman and ingest it.*
This corresponds to one talisman image. When copying, ensure meticulous accuracy. The **Red Dao/Way Lord Talisman Method** (赤帝符法): On days *bǐng* (丙) and *dīng* (丁), use white millet grass as the mat, three feet long. Spread a crimson silk banner one *zhàng* three feet long upon it. Place two cups of wine and two slices of dried meat on the mat. Write the talisman in cinnabar—two inches wide, seven inches long—and cast it upon the mat. The incantation reads:

*'On a fortunate day and auspicious hour,
Your humble servant [name] prostrates twice.
Reverently receiving the Celestial Sovereign Dao/Way Lord’s White Dao/Way Lord Divine Talisman.
After prostrating twice, burn the talisman and ingest it.'*

**Yellow Dao/Way Lord Talisman Method** (黄帝符法): On days *wù* (戊) and *jǐ* (己), use white millet grass as the mat, three feet long. Spread a yellow silk banner one *zhàng* two feet long upon the mat. Place two cups of wine and two slices of dried meat on the mat. Use vermilion as the ground, and write the talisman in purple ink—three inches wide, seven inches long—and cast it upon the mat. The incantation reads:

*'On a fortunate day and auspicious hour,
Your humble servant [name] prostrates twice.
Reverently receiving the Celestial Sovereign Dao/Way Lord’s Yellow Dao/Way Lord Divine Talisman.
After prostrating twice, burn and ingest the talisman.'*

**The following talismans are not closely related to the previous five**, yet they are also counted as one talisman. Each must be examined carefully.

**White Dao/Way Lord Talisman Method** (白帝符法): On days *gēng* (庚) and *xīn* (辛), use white millet grass as the mat, three feet long. Spread a plain white silk banner one *zhàng* three feet long upon it. Place two cups of wine and two slices of dried meat on the mat. Use green as the ground, and write the talisman in cinnabar—two inches wide, seven inches long—and cast it upon the mat. The incantation reads:

*'On a fortunate day and auspicious hour,
Your humble servant [name] prostrates twice.
Reverently receiving the Celestial Sovereign Dao/Way Lord’s White Dao/Way Lord Divine Talisman.
After prostrating twice, burn the talisman and ingest it.'*

**Black Dao/Way Lord Talisman Method** (黑帝符法): On days *rén* (壬) and *guǐ* (癸), use white millet grass as the mat, three feet long. Spread a black silk banner one *zhàng* two feet long upon it. Place two cups of wine and two slices of dried meat on the mat. Use black as the ground, and write the talisman in cinnabar—two inches wide, seven inches long—and cast it upon the mat. The incantation reads:

*'On a fortunate day and auspicious hour,
Your humble servant [name] prostrates twice.
Reverently receiving the Celestial Sovereign Dao/Way Lord’s Black Dao/Way Lord Divine Talisman.
After prostrating twice, burn the talisman and ingest it.'*

**The following methods** are the five Dao/Way Lord Divine Talismans, along with the four additional talismans received by **Master Ge Xuan** (仙公葛玄). Write two copies of each: one to burn and ingest, and one to wear upon the head. These are especially useful for alchemists seeking to forge the elixir beforehand, and should be prepared ten days in advance.

**The *Yellow Dao/Way Lord Nine Cauldrons Spiritual Elixir Dao/Way* (黄帝九鼎神一丹经诀) concludes here.** *The *Yellow Dao/Way Lord Nine Cauldrons Spiritual Elixir Dao/Way* (黄帝九鼎神丹经诀) begins anew.*

**Treatise on Taboos and Precautions for Alchemical Fusion**

What is elucidated here is the taboo and precautions for alchemical fusion.

The *Nine Cauldrons* and *Nine Elixirs* do not exhaust the method—there are the *Method for Testing the Cauldron and Refining the Medicine*, and the *Method for True Protection After Ingestion*.

Your humble servant notes: The Great Elixir is the refined essence of metals and stones, the treasure of the True Person. Therefore, those who ingest it attain divine transformation, longevity, and vision; they command spirits and ascend to the Celestial Clarity.

Common folk know only the titles of the elixir classics but do not understand the taboos of alchemical fusion. Even if they obtain the formulas, they will never succeed.

For one who seeks to refine the divine elixir, there are **five taboos, three prohibitions, four failures, and six dreads**. If transgressed, the elixir’s essence will scatter, its spiritual flowers will fall, its divine light will sink, and its frost-mists will be lost. Ingesting it will yield no benefit—this must be heeded with utmost caution.

Thus, the True Persons inquired into their particulars. The Mystic Master replied:

**The Five Taboos:**
1. When refining the medicine and igniting the fire, do not use the **Five Dead Days of Stones**—namely, Spring *Rén-Chén* (壬辰), Summer *Guǐ-Wèi* (癸未), Autumn *Bǐng-Xū* (丙戌), and Winter *Dīng-Chǒu* (丁丑). If the elixir is refined on these days and the furnace lit, the stone’s essence will stagnate, the flowers will not rise, the frost-mists will turn toxic, and ingestion will be futile.

2. When purchasing alchemical ingredients or discussing elixir matters, do not use the **Five Malevolent Days**—namely, the *Nine Turnings* of Spring, the *Cloud Purification* day, and the day the purification begins. Before dawn, pour five *dou* of clear wine into flowing water where the purification is held. If no flowing water exists, dig a well and pour the wine into it to purify the earth’s *qi*, so that those purifying may drink this water. Though no ritual invocation is spoken, it is the intent of offering and sacrifice. The elixir’s sublimity demands such rites—even if only symbolically—to fulfill the lower methods’ requirements. Hence, the Primordial Lord says: *"This is not for sacrificing to ghosts or gods."* It is clear.

Before the medicine is fully refined, sincerity must be upheld. Thus, the sacrifice is merely to express the wish for its completion. If the fusion is already finished and another sacrifice is made, this contradicts reason.

The purpose of sacrifice is either for the Celestial Sovereign to descend directly or for the Jade Maiden to be dispatched to assist. The divine *qi* bestows efficacy upon the medicine, enabling the practitioner to attain immortality and longevity.

When refining the elixir in secluded mountain retreats beside flowing eastern waters, erect a ritual platform and house, and complete all earthenware furnace preparations. Once the medicine’s essence is fully refined and the charcoal is ready, observe a hundred-day purification on the *Day of Opening and Expelling*, with no more than three like-minded companions sworn in secrecy. Only after testing the cauldron’s secrecy may the fire be lit.

Before fusing the medicine, observe a seven-day purification. On the *Day of Opening and Expelling* marked by *Jiǎ-Zǐ* (甲子), perform a sacrifice at the cauldron’s side. The sacrificial method uses five *shēng* of clear wine and white wine, three *jīn* of lamb and deer jerky, two *dòu* of yellow grain rice, two *shēng* of large dates, twenty cooked chicken eggs, and a three-*jīn* carp (head included). Arrange three tables, each with three cups, and burn *lù* incense. After two prostrations, recite:

*"Your humble servant [name] now adjusts the medicine to refine the Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir. May the divine and immortal Jade Maidens—Playful Maiden, Mystic Maiden, and Waistband Maiden—together perfect it. May the Great Dao Lord, the Great Harmony Lord, and the Supreme Lord grant that your humble servant [name], greedy for life and desiring immortality, may successfully complete this divine elixir."*

After pouring the wine and completing nine prostrations, chant:

*"O Great Dao Lord and Mystic Maiden, as you refine the divine elixir, may it neither scatter nor perish—let all its essence submit to the fire. May its hue be flawless, its transformations effortless, its gold and silver fully formed. May ingestion grant eternal life without end, attaining the True Person."*

Then place the actual medicine, dates, and oranges upon the altar and ignite the fire as prescribed.

For the **Great One’s Sacred Seat**, use a new bed three *chǐ* six *cùn* in length, two *chǐ* eight *cùn* in height, covered with fresh mats, facing west. Place a three-*chǐ* crimson silk cloth upon the mat, and set the sacrificial text for the day the fire is lit.

**The Nine Elixirs’ Sacrificial Method:**
At the refining site, construct a yellow-earth altar nine *chǐ* square, fenced on all sides. The central square is four *chǐ*, with gates on all four sides. Place the furnace six *chǐ* west of the altar. On the altar, arrange a mat of white grass, one *chǐ* long, with five layers of mats, one separate piece, and one cup of jerky and wine. To the east, arrange nine layers of mats, two pieces each, with two cups of jerky and wine. Use two *shēng* of yellow millet rice, three *jīn* (or five *jīn*) of beef and mutton jerky, three carp (three *jīn* total), and steam them. Prepare twenty boiled chicken eggs, three *shēng* of large dates, and one pear. If oranges, pomelos, or other red-hued fruits are available, burn incense, pour wine, and prostrate before the seat. Then proceed with the fire-igniting ritual as before.

After the furnace-side sacrifice, place fresh wine and jerky on three new tables, each with three cups of wine and three *jīn* of jerky. From this point onward, always offer wine and jerky at three locations, day and night without cessation. Replace the jerky every three days and the wine three times daily. Each time, pour the wine with the usual prostrations. From the moment the sacrifice is established, continuously burn incense, day and night without interruption, maintaining utmost purity, reverence, and diligence—never neglecting.

When the medicine is complete, perform another sacrifice as initially done, adding three *jīn* of roasted pork on the eastern seat of the altar, one *shēng* of white rice, and one roasted cock. Recite:

*"The divine medicine is now complete. I now request permission to open the cauldron, as desired."*

The sacrifice concludes with the opening of the cauldron.

In all cases of alchemical fusion, one must first ritually offer wine to the Yellow River’s source to subdue the earth’s *qi*. Additionally, a grand sacrifice to the divine must be made to appease the Eight Stones. If a *Nine Elders’ Jade Pass* is obtained, it will inspect the ten thousand *qi*, repel malevolent spirits, avert assassins and thieves, and ensure divine protection. The fire spirits will naturally submit, rendering further ritual offerings unnecessary—success will follow.

The *Nine Elders’ Jade Pass* states: On the first day of the fast, first inscribe in red on blue-black paper. This paper is also called the *Eight-Substance True Talisman* or the *Supreme Clarity Highest Talisman*, square in form, nine inches wide, two sheets in number. When finished, facing east, recite the incantation:

*"Eight-Substance True Talisman, Nine Elders’ Jade Pass.
Heavenly gods inspect the earth, above protecting the elixir’s essence.
Nine sources sealed, eight rivers brimming with treasure.
Slaying assassins, vanquishing malevolence—jewelous brilliance shines.
Golden nectar, jade frost: the essence of the Eight Stones.
Seven transformations, five changes, nine cycles to completion."*

After reciting, take one sheet and place it in a green brocade pouch, striking it against the chest. Take the other sheet to a well, cutting it in half: cast one half into the dwelling’s water, the other half bury beneath the *Six-One Furnace*, beneath the alchemical cauldron in flowing water—this may be struck with a stone to sink it. The buried portion should be three inches deep. This is the *Mysterious Seal*—the *Treasure Seal of Miao State*. Also called *Xianbo Taiyi’s Inspection* or the *Eight-Inch White Script*. On the first day of the fast, if it falls on *jiazi* or *jia-yin* at noon, face east and inscribe with a green brush upon the *Six-One Cauldron*. Again, take a white sheet, eight inches square, and inscribe this talisman upon it. When finished, recite:

*"Spring: *ren-yin*, Summer: *gui-si*, Autumn: *ren-shen*, Winter: *gui-hai*.
On these days, entering the mountains to refine divine medicine will yield no success—spirits will not aid, and malevolent ghosts will ruin the work."*

Three prohibitions: Do not refine elixir on *Spring geng-yin*, *Summer gui-wei*, *Autumn bing-shen*, or *Winter ding-chou*—these are days when entering the mountains to gather herbs or refine will cause spirits to seize one’s soul, spoiling the elixir and bringing illness.

Four prohibitions: Do not refine elixir in the furnace or seal the divine medicine on *Spring bing-xu*, *Spring bing-chen*, *Summer xin-wei*, *Summer xin-chou*, *Autumn ren-chen*, *Autumn ren-xu*, *Winter gui-wei*, or *Winter gui-chou*—these days will cause the furnace to burst open, elixir essence to scatter, and the Five Stones to disperse, ruining the frost and brilliance.

Five prohibitions: Men refining elixir must avoid the third day of the seventh month and *jia-yin* days in the seventh month; women must avoid the seventh day of the first month and *geng-shen* days in the first month. These four days are when stone spirits clash and ghosts gather. If refining begins on these days, the elixir essence will not manifest, spirits will not respond, and malevolent ghosts will invade, bringing ruin.

This is called the *Five Prohibitions*. The *Three Taboos* are:
1. Weeping or lamenting while refining elixir.
2. Uttering the names of assassins or thieves.
3. Encountering death, decay, or uncleanliness—such as childbirth or nursing.

If these taboos are violated, the stones will fail to coalesce, the Five Brilliances will not shine, and the elixir will become poisonous, killing those who ingest it. Those grieving, near corpses, or involved in death-related matters must not participate in refining frost and snow or tending the furnace.

Elixir also has an assassin ghost—*Stone Leek Child*, surname *Hunni Xi*, whose name must be avoided on the first day of refining. If invoked again, the smoke and frost will collapse, ghostly armies will invade, the divine furnace will shatter, and the essence will scatter—four calamities:
1. The refining site trembles as if traversed by chariots.
2. Envy-bearing individuals (those with malevolent gazes) near the divine medicine invite ghostly retribution.
3. Thunder shakes the cauldron, causing the essence to fall and the brilliance to fail.
4. The presence of pungent foods or burning chicken/dog hair.

These four calamities are the Eight Stones’ greatest taboos—violating them will cause the essence to fail and the elixir to never form. If refining days are insufficient and thunder is heard, quickly cover the cauldron with a damp cloth to suppress the essence, preventing smoke from rising.

Six dreads:
1. On the first day of sealing the medicine and when first igniting the fire, dread wind, rain, and thunder.
2. On the refining day, dread hearing calls to the soul.
3. *(Original text omitted three items; fourth)* Dread hearing weeping or lamentation.
4. Dread encountering blood, filth, or uncleanliness.

These six dreads are the elixir’s strict prohibitions—violating them will disturb the rising essence and damage the brilliance.

---
**Nine Cauldrons’ Hidden Text on Elixir**

The true person’s alchemical precepts are the precepts of the *Nine Cauldrons’ Elixir*. The first elixir is named *Danhua* (Elixir Flower). This elixir has two names: *Liuzhu Jiuzhuan* (Flowing Pearl Nine Transformations) and *Danhua*.

**Method for *Liuzhu Jiuzhuan*:**
According to the original scripture, first prepare the *Xuanhuang* (Mysterious Yellow). Take one *jin* each of realgar and cinnabar water, mixing them. *(Note: Though the precept lists two ingredients of one jin each, it does not specify the quantity of Xuanhuang nor the method of mixing—dilute or thick. Thus, those who follow this may fail. Referring to the second precept under the name *Shenfu Law*, there are four methods. The second method states: After preparing Xuanhuang, mix it with the Flowing Pearl Nine Transformations’ Xuanhuang water until it turns red—though the fire-charring method differs, its consistency, like mud, remains unchanged.)*

In the *Thirty-Six Waters Method*, there is indeed a *Xuanhuang Water Method*. Yet *Danhua* and *Liuzhu Jiuzhuan* do not employ it. When it states *"above, the Flowing Pearl Nine Transformations’ Xuanhuang water,"* it refers to the Xuanhuang used in the process—cinnabar and realgar waters mixed and subjected to a hundred steams. Place them in a green bamboo tube, thinly scraping its exterior, sealing it with white wood, and covering it with fine yellow sand.

「If the chamber is too spacious, the *qi* will easily disperse, and the fine essence produced will be mixed with earth, appearing yellowish.

This is then submerged with the *Mò* and steamed, and after a short time, it becomes water.
Immediately, it condenses below, then ascends again as water—thus, a hundred times up and down.

Again, take one *jīn* each of realgar and cinnabar waters, and use them to refine the *Xuanhuang*.
Place them in a sealed crucible and subject to sublimation—do this nine times in succession.
When the *Xuanhuang* essence is fully refined, remove it.

Take this one *jīn* of *Xuanhuang*, and divide it into nine portions.
Then take one portion and further divide it into two.

Next, prepare two crucibles: one as the *Taìqīng Dān* "White Snow Soil Crucible" method, detailed in the sixth volume of *Shàngshù* (already explained).
This method is not repeated here.

Then, take twenty *jīn* of oyster shell and seventy *jīn* of red stone pitch, grind them into powder, and ferment with soil for a hundred days to form a paste. Grind them again with three thousand strokes, and coat the soil crucible.
Take two *jīn* of mercury and place it in the soil crucible, covering it with the two portions of *Xuanhuang* above and below.
Then seal the two crucibles tightly with the oyster shell and red stone pitch paste, smearing them green on the outside.
Combine them securely and let them dry in the shade for ten days.

Set an iron pot atop, with legs raised nine *cùn* high.
Use horse dung fire or fire from parched rice husks—burn for three days and nights, then cool for one day.
Upon completion, open and retrieve the sublimed essence, discarding the dregs.
If the dregs, when burned, yield a residue, it means the *qi* of the medicine is not fully exhausted.
Repeat the sublimation as before until the *qi* is fully spent.
Afterward, adjust the fire as needed, prolonging the sublimation until it is complete.

Take one portion of *Xuanhuang* and divide it into two, covering the soil crucible above and below with it, then subliming it while sealed as before.
Do this nine times in succession, then open and retrieve the sublimed essence.

Next, take seven *túlóng* (earthwax) pieces.
The master’s secret is this: the scriptures sometimes refer to them simply as *lónggāo* (wax), or as *túlónggāo* (earthwax).
There is no difference—they are all white-necked, curved ants.

Place them in a vessel, coat with salt, and let them dissolve into water.
Use this to mix with the sublimed essence, then sublimate again.»

As before, sublimate for three days and nights, then cool for one day, and open to collect it—the five-colored frost, called *Liúzhū Jiǔzhuàn* (Flowing Pearl Nine Transformations).

I privately think that even these curved ants and tiny creatures are sentient.
To take their fragile lives to prolong my own years—
this is contrary to benevolence and righteousness.
The Confucian way forbids it.

Moreover, when refining the elixir in thirty-six waters,
one should not hear the cries of slaughtered livestock,
nor the sounds of weeping and lamentation.
Even among the three taboos,
one must also avoid sorrow and grief.
Thus, even the lowliest creatures are spared.
Where blades strike, who would not fear?
Only when absolutely necessary
does the greater righteousness allow the sacrifice of kin.
If one can safely escape the four nets,
there is the virtue of opening the three paths.

Regarding the second elixir, named *Shénfú* (Divine Symbol) Elixir,
the four methods of the *Sìzhōng* (Four Central) scripture
first use the first method—
mixing the elixir with *Xuányè* (Mysterious Liquid) like mud,
which can substitute for this.

Again, the first elixir is called the *Dānhuá* (Elixir Flower) method.
If the medicine does not comply,
use *Xuánshuǐyè* (Mysterious Water Liquid) and *lónggāo* (wax) to moisten it,
mixing until thoroughly damp, then sublimate again—
thus, it is refined for thirty-six days.
These two substances
do not rely on the juice of curved ants.

Moreover, *Xīlónggāo* (Western Wax)
is the dew from mulberry leaves.
The juice of the *qūmiǎn* (curved ants) and other insects
are all autumn morning dew—
their quality varies when pressed,
and ancient methods must not be altered.
I dare not omit or change them;
instead, I rely on the *Xuánshuǐyè*’s own secret, as follows:

For those who take the first elixir,
the *Liúzhū Jiǔzhuàn* and the *Dānhuá* elixirs—
on a *Jiǎzǐ* (Gabi) day at dawn,
facing the sun, bow twice,
then kneel long and take it like millet grains—
instantly, one becomes an immortal,
ascending to the Nine Heavens.
Taking half a millet grain
makes one an earthly immortal—
unaffected by water or fire,
immune to calamities and blades,
free to transform at will,
entering and exiting without hindrance,
commanding ghosts and spirits,
with a lifespan equal to Heaven and Earth.

If one wishes to depart this world,
taking another half millet grain
will instantly send them to Heaven.
To elevate a mortal,
take it like a small bean grain—
they will ascend that very day.
Taking half a small bean grain
makes them an earthly immortal.

Even livestock, if given a large bean grain,
will ascend to Heaven at once.
Thus it is said:
A crow becomes a phoenix,
a beast becomes a qilin,
a serpent becomes a dragon,
a ghost becomes a spirit,
a woman becomes a jade maiden,
a man becomes an immortal.

Mixing snake fat into four pills,
each the size of a shot pellet,
and burying them at the four corners of one’s residence—
the house will transform into a red dragon,
lifting the entire dwelling to Heaven,
seven thousand feet above the earth,
where it becomes gold and jade,
free to roam as desired.

Burying one pill the size of a chicken egg yolk,
near or far—within a thousand *li* in any direction,
down to the Nine Abysses—
all rivers, mountains, and forests within
will ascend to Heaven.

Take one *catty* of firm, fine-grained yellow earth,
grind and sift it, then boil in three cycles of scalding water.
Add one *qian* (gram) and stir until thoroughly mixed,
simmering until the water evaporates—
it will turn to gold.

According to this secret,
at first hearing, it seems unbelievable.
Yet the teachings of sages
are not easily slandered.
Long ago, the Eight Immortals told King Huainan:
*"I can refine mud into gold in one boil
and solidify mercury into silver—
this is indeed the power of the elixir."*
Yet the King only received the *Wǔlíng* (Five Spirits) method,
not the *Jiǔdǐng* (Nine Cauldrons) secret.
Thus, Liu An bowed repeatedly
but never attained it.
The Way of knowing is difficult to perceive.

Yet even common copper and iron,
when infused with elixir power
and stirred into a paste,
naturally differ from their original forms—
this cannot be dismissed as false.

Even lead, tin, mercury, or iron—
one *catty* of any—
when mixed with one *qian* of elixir,
will all become gold.
This is the most forbidden secret of Master Zhāng,
so the original scripture does not record it.

---
**Second Elixir: *Dānhuá* Method**
The *Dānhuá* elixir uses only earthen crucibles,
just like the *Báixuě* (White Snow) method.
Place the medicine inside, seal it, and set it
on three iron tripods over fire,
as in the second elixir’s *Shénfú* (Divine Symbol) method
from the *Dānjié* (Elixir Secrets).
The first method uses the *Dānhuá* crucible
to sublimate the two divine symbols—
this is supremely effective.

This elixir, once sealed,
ascends and descends nine times without opening.
Place mercury in the crucible,
then seal the two earthen crucibles’ mouths
with *mǔlì* (oyster shell) and *chìshízhī* (red stone pitch) mud.
Let it dry in shade, then set it
on three iron tripods over fire,
nine inches above the ground,
using husk-fire for one day and night.
Invert the crucible (lower becomes upper)
without opening it, for another day and night.
Repeat nine ascensions and descensions,
then cool for one day before opening
to collect the sublimed essence.
Mix it with *lǐyúdǎn* (crucian carp bile)
until thoroughly damp, then return it
to the earthen crucible.
Seal it with *Liùyī* (Six-One) mud
as in the *Dānhuá* crucible method,
let it dry, then fire it as before—
one day and night.
After nine ascensions and descensions,
mix in *Xīlónggāo* (Western Wax),
which is mulberry dew,
until thoroughly damp.

Separately, take *qiānhuánghuá* (lead yellow flower)
and mercury, refining them as in the scriptures
to produce *Liúzhū* (Flowing Pearl) five-colored *Xuányè* (Mysterious Liquid).
When ten *catties* are obtained,
divide them into nine portions.
Take one portion and split it into two.
Prepare three earthen crucibles, each holding six,
then take the previously sublimed nine times mercury
and place it in the crucible.
Cover the top and bottom with two portions of five-colored *Xuányè*,
then seal the crucible’s rim with *Liùyī* mud,
three *cùn* thick, and let it dry in shade for ten days.
Fire it with husk-fire for nine days and nights,
cool for one day, then collect the sublimed essence
and return it to the original earthen crucible.
Again, take one portion of five-colored *Xuányè*,
split it into two, and cover the top and bottom,
sealing and firing as before.

Thus are the nine transformations complete.

For the third transformation, replace the crucibles with two new earthen ones, as per the *Tàiqīng Dān Jiǔdǐng Jíyào* method. The nine transformations require three sets of six crucibles each.

As the original scripture states: *"Three preparations for nine transformations—this is it."*

The medicinal potency and timing align with the nine transformations of *Liúzhū* (Flowing Pearl).

This divine symbol elixir can also transmute mercury into elixir. The method: take one *catty* of mercury, heat it in an iron vessel, then add one *qian* of divine symbol elixir, stirring until it transforms into divine elixir. It is called *Huándān* (Returning Elixir). As the scripture says: *"This is the method of treating mercury to form elixir."*

Ingest it as per the *Dānhuā* (Elixir Flower) method.

Another second method for the divine symbol: prepare *Xuányè* (Mysterious Liquid) separately, as in the original scripture, completing the *Xuányè*. This *Xuányè* refers to the *Xuányè* of nine *catties* of mercury and one *catty* of lead—not the three *Xuányè* methods in the *Huāfǎ* (Flower Method).

Take the previously refined *Liúzhū* nine-transformations *Xuányè* water.

According to the *Xuányè Shuǐ Běnjīng* by Zhang Tian Shi: *"The elixir flower is indeed the first flower—it is water. Upon careful examination, it is not the water of cinnabar or realgar."*

The *Xuányè* water method lacks proper instruction among the thirty-six waters. This water is obtained by steaming—no doubt about it. Mix it into a paste, heat it in an iron vessel until red, then blend with *Xuánshuǐ yè* (Mysterious Water Liquid). *Xuánshuǐ yè* is also called *Xuánshuǐ zé*—it is magnetite water.

Its preparation: one *catty* of magnetite, two *liǎng* of realgar, and two *liǎng* of *shídǎn jīng* (stone gall essence) are placed in a bamboo tube, sealed with lacquer as before, and submerged in the *Huāchí* (Flower Pool) for thirty days to form water.

Another method: carve bamboo into a *qiān* shape, fill it with saltpeter, bury it in a well three *chǐ* above water, and wait twenty days for the water to form. Add saltpeter again for another twenty days to complete the water. Add mica for another twenty days. If it does not transform, rebury it.

*"Red Dragon’s blood"* refers to cinnabar placed inside. *"Green Dragon’s blood"* refers to *zēngqīng* (blue-green vitriol) placed inside. *"Mysterious Water Liquid"* refers to magnetite placed inside.

All methods involve burying in a well. When needed, test both methods to determine the superior one.

Shape into a paste, place in an earthen crucible, seal, and fire as per the scripture.

The third divine symbol method: take the *Xuányè* from the nine-transformations *Liúzhū*, mix it with *Huāchí* into a paste, coat the earthen crucible, and let it dry. Place mercury inside, cover with one crucible, seal with *Liùyī* mud, let it dry in shade for ten days. Place on three iron tripods and fire for nine days and nights, then cool for one day. Open and ingest as per the *Dānhuā* method.

This mercury must be the nine-times sublimed, detoxified mercury. All others are unusable.

The fourth method’s *Xuányè* is also from the nine-transformations *Liúzhū*. The earthen crucibles used in the nine elixirs follow the *Tàiqīng Báixuě* method without variation.

**Third Elixir: Divine Elixir Method**
Mix realgar and orpiment as in the original scripture. First, coat the two earthen crucibles with *Xuányè* paste, three *fēn* thick, and let it dry in shade for ten days. Place realgar and orpiment inside, then coat the crucible mouths with *Xuányè* paste, seal, and apply *Liùzhōu* mud at the rim, three *fēn* thick, letting it dry. Place on three iron tripods and fire as before.

**Fourth Elixir: Returning Elixir Method**
First, calcine *yùshí* (jade stone) and *fánshí* (alum stone) with nine other substances in charcoal fire. Seal in an earthen crucible, layer one *catty* of *Xuányè* on top, then one *catty* of mercury beneath it. Next, layer one *catty* of realgar (pounded a thousand times) and one *catty* of mercury, followed by seven other substances, each one *catty*, layered as described in the scripture. Seal and fire as per the method—do not deviate from the timing.

**Fifth Elixir: Elixir Pill Method**
Coat the two earthen crucibles with *Xuányè* paste, three *fēn* thick, and let it dry. Place the medicines inside, seal, and fire on three iron tripods nine *cùn* high, as per the scripture.

**Sixth Elixir: Refining Elixir Method**
Mix *tǔlóng gāo* (earthworm juice), *tǔlóng shǐ* (earthworm essence), yellow dog bile, oyster shell, and red stone pitch into a paste to coat the crucible. Spread *Xuányè* on the crucible bottom, half-*cùn* thick, then place the medicines inside, seal, and fire as before. The rest follows the scripture.

(*Tǔlóng gāo* refers to earthworm juice.)

**Seventh Elixir: Soft Elixir Method**
As per the scripture, place mercury in the crucible, coat the two crucibles’ rims with *Xuányè* paste, seal tightly, and apply *Liùyī* mud, three *fēn* thick. Place on three iron tripods and fire as per the method.

**Eighth Elixir: Subdued Elixir Method**
As per the scripture, coat the crucible with *Liùyī* mud, then layer one *catty* of *Xuányè* or lead white at the bottom. Place mercury above the *Xuányè*. Pound and sift one *catty* each of *zēngqīng* (blue-green vitriol) and magnetite separately. First, layer *zēngqīng* over the mercury, then layer magnetite over the *zēngqīng*, and finally layer one *catty* of *Xuányè* (previously mixed with *lónggāo* to a moist state) over the magnetite. Seal and fire as per the method.

After nine ascensions and nine descensions, reapply *lónggāo* to moisten it before subliming again.

**Ninth Elixir: Cold Elixir Method**
As per the scripture, first layer one *catty* of *Xuányè* at the crucible’s base, then place the medicines in order.

**Sealing the Crucible as per the Method**
As the scripture states, the sealing must be done properly.

It is further said: *"Zǐmíng"* refers to **fire**. In the **Second Elixir of the Divine**, the method of preparing *Xuányè* (lead white) differs from the rest. All other elixirs follow the **Nine Ascensions of the Flowing Pearl and Lead White** method.

**Method for Opening the Crucible**
The subject notes: The crucible and furnace must be sturdy and tightly sealed, known as the **Divine Chamber**. Between the two vessels, the space is firmly filled with *Zhōnghuáng* (realgar), and when fire is applied, it becomes even more solid. The mud layer must be thick.

One must not strike, chisel, or tap the crucible, but rather prepare **two or three sharp saws** to gradually cut through it, or use a whetstone to sharpen it like a blade until the crucible’s material is exposed. Then, with iron implements, one may cautiously open it layer by layer.

Next, the upper vessel is inverted, and the **sublimated essence** is brushed away and collected.

The method then advises using **cock’s feathers**, specifically noting that the cock is the **bird of the *yǒu* hour** (酉禽), implying that **white feathers** are preferable. Before use, one should raise a pair of **pure white cocks and hens**, nurturing them until they lay eggs. Their **feathers from the wings’ tips**—known as *liáofēngmáo* (wind feathers)—are taken, **three from each bird**, without washing or wiping them, to sweep the **sublimated frost** (飞霜华).

The elixir is then placed in a **golden container**, sealed tightly, and wrapped in a **brocade pouch**. The scripture states: *"Dàizhòu"* (carrying at the elbow) is the correct way to keep it close, for it is too precious to leave unattended, and one must also guard against accidental ingestion before its potency is realized, lest its **transformation** (神化) fail.

**Testing the Medicine**
The subject notes: The **Daoist alchemical scriptures** state that the medicine must first be tested by refining **gold**. If the gold succeeds, then the elixir is complete. If the gold does not succeed, then the elixir is not yet complete.

Further sublimation must be conducted until the **gold is formed** as the standard. Though there are precise measures for the **Nine Ascensions**, one must carefully verify them with other methods when testing.

According to the **Nine Ascensions method**, take **ten catties of lead**, place it in an iron vessel, and boil it with **fierce fire** until it bubbles three times. The **sublimated essence** from the Nine Ascensions is **one grain**, which is then stirred into the lead. In a short while, **nine catties of yellow gold** will form.

Again, take **seven catties of tin**, place it in an iron vessel, and apply **fierce fire** until it bubbles three times. Stir **one grain of the Nine Ascensions essence** into it, and in a short while, **white silver** will form.

The obtained **sublimated essence** must first be weighed. If it is sufficient for **thousands of people**, then one may proceed to test for gold. One must not hastily sell the medicine based on a single method’s results.

The **concentrated residue** (浓丹滓) can also be used to produce silver, if desired. The testing is conducted according to this method.

At the time of refining, one must strictly adhere to the original scripture. The measures for consumption and protection must also follow the **orthodox method**.

**Subject’s Observations on Consumption and Protection**
The subject notes: Those who consume the elixir upon completion are often **unrefined practitioners** (格人). Among them, the **Three Grades**—upper, middle, and lower—are distinguished.

If the **upper-grade adept** consumes it, they will ascend to **True Personhood** (登真) in seven days. If the **middle-grade adept** consumes it, they will attain **immortality** (得仙) in seventy days. If the **lower-grade or foolish practitioner** consumes it, they will become immortal in a year.

If one’s resolve is sincere and they dare to ingest the elixir in one dose, they will all **temporarily die for half a day**, then revive as if awakening from sleep. This is the **most perilous** method, requiring strict adherence to the proportions—**half a grain of glutinous millet** is the measure.

The subject further notes: When taking **medicines for healing**, they should be consumed **before meals**. When taking **medicines for cultivating the Dao**, they should be consumed **after meals**.

This is because **medicines that attack illness** should be taken when the stomach is empty and **malignant qi** (毒气) has not yet circulated. If taken after meals, the medicine’s power is wasted in **digesting food**.

If one wishes to **nourish the Dao** by taking medicine before meals, then the **virtue/power of the medicine** (药力) is not yet fully activated, and the food will **drive it downward**, rendering it ineffective. It cannot eliminate the **upper ailments** (上病) and thus yields no benefit.

Though the **Divine Elixir** (神丹) has great efficacy, one must strictly follow the **orthodox scriptures** and their measures, not disregarding the **common prohibitions** (常涂小禁) or minor taboos.

The subject notes: Each person’s lifespan and constitution have their own **affinities**. If one’s **life-affinity** (年命所属) is **earth**, they must not consume **green-colored medicines**. Others should follow this principle accordingly.

All **restrictions and taboos** (拘忌) must be observed to align with the **natural order** (克顺). If the **golden elixir** or **precious medicines** (丹金大药) possess **transformation** (神化) of extraordinary marvel, then the question of **appropriateness or prohibition** is no longer relevant.

**End of the Twenty-First Scroll of the *Huángdì Jiǔdǐng Shéndān Jīng* (Yellow Emperor’s Nine Cauldrons Divine Elixir Scripture)**
